# 2021

## September - 2021

### 26-09-2021
#### Farewell Toby
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
<!-- 👥 Relationships -->
> This is the very first entry of this journal thing but let's not dwell on this seemingly monumental topic to make way for a much more significant event.  
> It was Toby's last day in Hong Kong. He is going to the University of Oxford to study Mathematics or something. We've already had a farewell meal on 24/09 but that's beside the point. CNok, Efren, Samuel, and myself went to the airport to give him a final farewell. The airport was quite non-crowded due to COVID or something. I have never seen a place in Hong Kong this non-crowded before so that was quite amusing, not to mention it was the first time in 3 years I'd been to the airport. He was queuing for the check-in at the British Airways counters when Teddy and Adrian Lee/Li somehow spontaneously materialised. We had a brief meal at the airport - nothing too remarkable except it is horribly expensive, but I guess it's to be expected. His dad did give all of us red packets after the meal as a thank-you for us coming along to the airport. I think he had like 6 or something relatives with him: parents + granny + some other randos. We had some photos and hugs. His dad and granny left just after one photo which struck me as odd but that's beside the point. Come to think of it, I've never hugged him before I don't think, nor have I been in a group hug before, so that was interesting and awkward, especially considering we had to hold it long enough for his relatives to take pictures of this mess of arms and torsos. Alas, it was time for him to enter the security gate thing, despite it being a whopping 1.5 hours too early, and there shall no longer be a turning back. He struggled a bit with the first self-help gate thing, which I kindly helped myself to documenting in the form of a video, later IG story. We waved goodbye intensely but he barely looked back. We kept watching until we lost sight of him. CNok stated he wanted to cry a bit but ultimately didn't. But he did say that if I were the one to leave, then he would definitely cry rolling on the floor.  
> I wasn't too emotional. It might kick in later after it had sunk in on me. Though it did make me have a sudden realisation. Life is *not* constant, nothing is. I have been taking it for granted that life is always going to be "unchanging" and everything should have a "later". But it isn't and doesn't. It just made me question my mortality for a second, even after a day, as the time of writing this, and I'd expect this feeling to grow as time goes on, every time I'd talk to him, every time we'd have some sort of now Toby-less gathering, and as I get older, in general. For instance, Toby and I have been planning for this dumb devil comedy sketch idea since before DSE even. We had planned for something to happen during the summer holidays. We have much planned for the summer actually: variety chess videos, podcasts (which honestly might still be possible), some local hotel staycations, vacation trips to the UK even. With much ambition, might I add. Guess what? Nothing got done. Like literally not a single thing got done in that summer. It was literally the longest summer I have ever had in my entire life and I did nothing. None of us did. Why? 'Cus of that mindset that life is constant, and that it would always have a "later". It *is* a huge let-down and regret for me, and more importantly, for Toby. It should be a whole year soonest until we meet again. But I guess at least I got to walk around CUHK with Toby on 17-Sep, so that's something. Also, us the gang had been holding more gatherings and events in S6, probably because it was the last year of our secondary school years. I have CNok to thank for that, for not letting the mindset get to us, especially me, at least for a short while.  
> I wish it doesn't take such a huge thing for me to realise that but the sad truth is it did. I would say this would be a life lesson for me, and that I would change my ways after this, but the truth is, there had been so many life lessons before this, and I can't say how many of them have really changed me - nay - budged me even the tiniest bit. Maybe they have, maybe they haven't, I don't know. Everything is subconscious after all. They may have been memorable, sure, no less than this one, but they may ultimately prove themselves meaningless if I couldn't really get something out of them. Ambition is a pretty significant source of regrets, but the lack of it accounts for the large majority. I guess I am grateful that those plans existed while they existed. At least we got to discuss about it despite us both knowing that they probably won't happen in time. I shall miss him.  
> I have known him since S1. Weirdly enough, I actually think he might be my first new friend in SJC, along with Bennie. We did dumb stuff back then like stalking Santos, but ultimately we just have the same channel, at least I think we do. We fell out during S2-3 due to reasons still beyond my comprehension till this day, but we got back together by chance(?) from S4 onwards. Speaking of S1 and Bennie, the three of us actually did try to make our own game, along with Marwin I believe. Well it was mainly *my* game, but they contributed in the form of 3D models. Toby also contributed some ideas(?) I believe, though the memories are starting to get vague and foggy. It never got finished, partly because my computer sucked back then, partly because of that "life is constant" mindset. That "later" turned into "never". It goes to show our ambition even back then. Guess we haven't changed too much. He was a very plastic person back then. And honestly, I would go as far as to say that he *was* the advocate for my own plasticity and that he was the major reason my personality and mode of thinking when it comes to dealing with new people and stuff are the way they are. Yes, our ambition never changed, but neither did my/our procrastinating mentality. But I guess it was all me. Toby did try to push the ideas into fruition but I was somewhat reluctant in some of them for reasons. I shall take fault for that.  
> Anyway, us the gang planned to visit the UK and have some sort of vacation there, with Toby of course, sometime in the future, presumably after the fucking COVID-19 ends. Let's see what would be the fate of this plan: shall it fall like so many before it have, or would it be the one that shall finally rise above all? Either way, it shall be at least a year until we can find out. I hope Toby won't get too lonely in the UK. He never struck me as being too emotionally attached too much to anything anyway, so I guess he would most likely be fine, probably. Though he was a really messy person when I first met him, and still is. Let's hope the two luggage of stuff shall only allow him to make the smallest mess at worst. Whatever awaits, shall it be bright and vibrant. Farewell Toby, until we meet again.

### 27-09-2021
#### Starting this journal
<!-- 💻 Personal projects -->
> Technically the last entry wasn't written yesterday as it should have been. It was actually written the very moment before the writing of this. Toby has finally convinced me to start a project like this. Actually he just made me convince myself really. To be fair, he has been advertising this idea to me for a very very long time. It is finally time that I felt the need to start this. To document my own thoughts, feelings, experiences, and such. I have made the decision that this journal shouldn't only contain huge events like many other journals might. Life is not always full of dramatic stuff, and this journal shall make that apparent. But as always, let's see how long I can keep this up. I can't say I have too much faith in myself based on past experiences. I also have little regard for the length of the entries as one might suspect reading the last entry. They shall be however long or short they feel like being. This should be a good read a few months or years from now.

#### Toby in London
> Toby has landed in London without issue (that I know of) and finished tinkering with the airport shenanigans. He said there was minimal jet lag 'cus he didn't even sleep that well on the plane but I don't think jet lags manifest the moment one lands. We'll see. He called a taxi and waited at the airport, only to find out that the driver possesses such incompetence that they had mixed up the pickup point and the destination. I guess Toby wouldn't be the only one who's a huge klutz then. It was pretty funny to be honest. Toby actually has the GPS tracking location of the taxi the whole time and witnessed this whole driving-the-completely-wrong-way fiasco. He didn't think to call the driver to warn them of their own stupidity. He said he was more confident that the GPS was wrong than the driver committing such foolery, but I think he was secretly amused that such a driver even exists. He likes to observe others' behaviour so I don't think such a hypothesis would be too out of character for him. He did end up having to wait for 3 hours in total before travelling 1.5 more hours until he reaches his temporary hostel place. I guess this whole insanity was half his fault. This journal shall be expecting more Toby updates in the short future.

### 28-09-2021
#### Getting back my HKDSE papers
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> I bought the HKDSE papers some time ago, all the subjects, all the papers, and I got them back today from the post office. It's interesting 'cus it has already been so long ago that if not for the SMS they sent me, I would've completely forgotten about this. I remember being super bummed when the DSE results were out, and rightfully so. I was in some sort of stages of grief. My entire DSE and JUPAS journey was something of a roller coaster really. It started on the day when the results were out. Obviously I have made score predictions and some plans depending on the actual final score, but it's safe to say that all of those went completely out of the window - no joke. Even in my worst planned scenarios, I should still be able to get into at least A2, and hopefully transfer back to A1; but the actual results turned out worse than the worst, far from it even. I was in shock, very much so. To be fair, it was to be expected that the scores wouldn't be the best, but being worse than the worst scenario was never expected. I guess all of my friends got unsatisfactory results too, as did the whole school. I guess Toby got the best out of this whole ordeal, but I guess this wasn't much of a doubt in the first place. He was never bad at anything really. His academics mainly just consisted of his qualities with no setbacks like so many of us do. I was planning to get at least a 5`**` in Maths and/or Physics, and some 5`*` elsewhere. I guess maybe I was being too optimistic, but to be honest I didn't think I failed this badly when I made those score predictions, right after finishing the papers. Some of the subjects were a little wonky, all things considered, especially for Biology where I was sick the whole time and spent something like 15 minutes in the washroom. CNok was aiming to get 5`**` in both Chinese and Economics. He had been doing a lot of Economics past papers, like *a lot* a lot. But ultimately he still was able to get into a rather decent programme. I mean universities do offer a huge variety of business and economics programmes, with a huge range of score requirements, which translates to students being able to apply for suitable programmes no matter what score they ended up achieving. Not me though, which brings me back to the main point of discussion.  
> Upon receiving the results, I immediately applied for a remarking the very same day. It was for English, Liberal Studies, Chemistry, and Biology I believe. Fortunately for me, I was able to successfully upgrade from 5 to 5`*` for my Biology, which was somewhat surprising considering it was my least confident subject. But either way, this gave me a ticket for a JUPAS reconsideration, which by some tricks of the system, would actually make it easier for me to get into the programmes I wanted. From the statistics database my school had provided, my score actually reached the median of last year's admission round of my A2 programme. I was really confident and under the impression that this would be it. It wasn't. The reconsideration yielded no result and it was ultimately futile. It wasn't common to succeed in DSE appeals, you know. Biology, even less. I was told that I was the first person in SJC's history who had ever had success in appealing Biology. It was pretty disappointing. I was teased but it was snatched away from my grasp in the very last moment. I was really more surprised that I didn't get accepted into the programme despite the data suggesting otherwise. It could only imply that the cut-off was exceptionally high this year. I guess those born in 2003 were just fated to be eternally unlucky. SARS was a thing when we were born, some sort of swine flu in 2009 took my kindergarten graduation ceremony, the principal got changed during my S6 year, and the whole COVID-19 ordeal of course. None of this makes any scientific sense but in a way I guess I have already adopted the belief that bad luck was one of my personal traits. Basically every big event in my life went haywire. I have made nothing short of 4 preference priority lists within the past month or so, and I don't think any one of them went my way, literally, for one reason or another, mostly for reasons beyond my control.  
> So anyhow, I am now studying Biomedical Engineering, which wasn't a bad programme per se, but it isn't what I had been planning for for the past 3 years or so. I remember borderline hating this and hating myself for quite a while. But now that I have been studying for almost a month, I would say those have subsided a bit. Maybe this would be a good chance for me to get a high GPA, and eventually assist me in successfully transferring back into Medicine. Maybe this is the only way I could ever get into Medicine, and this is some sort of fated path? Honestly, I think I am both too optimistic and pessimistic at the same time. I mean that was literally the exact thought process I went through when the DSE appeal results were out. It's kinda like the old Chinese folklore tale about the old guy who lost the horse. Let's hope that this would be the case even though deep down in my heart I secretly believe that something would decide that it would like to go wrong. Murphy's Law I guess, basically concludes my life thus far. Yes, I may be less upset and more accepting of my current situation, but I kinda doubt it would stay this way for long. Maybe I should stop obsessing over choosing my own path, and just takes whatever life delivers, buddha style or something like that, but it really sounds like dubious advice to accept whatever. I guess you could only either live like whatever without a care in the world or keep dreaming about your aspirations and be disappointed constantly. I'm not sure I want to fall under either of those umbrellas but I don't suppose there is a third way, not an easy one at least.  
> I still haven't taken a look at the DSE papers as of the writing of this. It's rather funny that my mentality would change so fast. The original reason I wanted the papers back was because I was in disbelief and wanted to get to the bottom of this. Again, in some sort of stages of grief. But now that I actually got them, I think maybe I have stopped caring about it. It would be poetic that I would just throw them away or store them somewhere forever, never to be opened. But I think I will eventually take a look at them, just not in the near future. Let's see in what mindset I would be in the next time I shall discover them among the piles of mess on my desk. This journal shall expect an entry about that by then, whenever it shall happen.

### 29-09-2021
#### Spoon-feedy education
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
<!-- 💭 Philosophy -->
> Don't expect much from this entry because I am writing this during a lecture, which is admittedly, not a very good thing to do. But in my defence, this lecture is quite dry. Not that it's boring though, the topic is interesting, but such spoon-feeding lectures prove to be an ineffective way to learn, for me at least. To some extent it may be good, but it really depends on the subject and topic. For instance, this particular lecture is about Anatomy and Physiology. With a load of information as big as this, it is practically impossible for anyone to comprehend when given in this style.  
> The point of education is to shape the way we tackle new information, in my opinion. Mathematics actually demonstrates this idea perfectly; for every new theory that you discover, you'll *have* to understand all of its intricacies and limitations for it to provide you with the greatest asset. There should simply be no shortcuts. Spoon-feeding straight up kills it. Elegant theorems are often reduced into identities students have to recite if they possess even the slightest bit of sophistication. I'm confident to say that this is the major contributor to students getting confused and disinterested in Mathematics. It is tragic, yes, to know that the worst student could have been a great mathematician, if not for this system. Everything is optimised for speed, and anything that doesn't result in direct teaching progress shall be eliminated as soon as possible. Although it may be able to discourage teachers from straying from the topic, it also encourages them to speedrun through the materials. Comprehension, skipped; consolidation, skipped; the "click" moments, all skipped. After all, there is not a more direct and straightforward way to have them perform well in tests and exams than reciting. Do you not understand the material? Well too bad, for it is your job to keep up. Students simply don't have enough time to marinate themselves in the knowledge. They don't perform well in those subjects and grow to hate them. I can't blame them. It is only human to repulse from things that make your uncomfortable. Pardon me when I say that I don't have a solution for this, but this problem must be seen by the world. Are we sure that geniuses in this system would translate into geniuses of humanity?  
> While what I've said is true for lower-level education, it is most certainly not true for tertiary ones (i.e. university education). Teachers, or rather, professors/lecturers, have nothing more to be regulated by than the demands of society, the specialty required by the profession, and their own morals. After all, it's not like anyone would notice it unless it manifests itself in the society in the form of decreased competence. But professors are scholars, and most scholars are respectful to their own field and profession. It is merely their own moral obligation and social responsibility to educate as much and as thoroughly as their capabilities allow. Medicine is probably one of the, if not the only profession that leaves so little room for error. It is no joke to be a professional in this field. The spoon-feedy nature of this curriculum is simply the natural inevitability that such a system make arise. I guess students in this field are expected to be more competent and hence should be more than capable to "teach themselves". I've heard that students are expected to self-study for three times as much than actual lecture hours, and that's for other professions. I can only imagine how much that coefficient would be for medical students.  
> I guess I'm half a medical student even right now, and I *am* expected to give and show that kind of effort and dedication toward my studies. Even though I currently only have to take one course this demanding, I'm already slipping big time. I can't imagine it would get any better than this, and it most likely won't. This course is seriously making me doubt my abilities to study Medicine in the event that I should find myself be successfully transferred to it. I guess I can try and wait and see.

#### Undiagnosed ailments
<!-- 🌞 Well-being -->
> I was feeling a little light-headed in today's PE lesson, except we haven't even started doing anything yet. We were just sitting in a small classroom listening to theories taught by the coach. Maybe it was because I had to turn my head slightly to the left to see him properly, maybe it was because I haven't drunk enough water yet in the morning. But mostly likely it should be because I have some undiagnosed disease. I can't for the life of me remember if this had been a thing for my entire life but it started manifest itself more and more during my senior secondary school years. I suspect I may have a wide variety of undiagnosed syndromes/disorders, but let's work our way up from the most inconsequential ones.  
> For starters, I suspect that I may have ***ADHD (Attention deficit hyperactivity disorder)***. I could never sit in one place still without moving around, adjusting my pose every once in a while, fidgeting with my fingers or other objects, having restless legs... the list goes on. Even in this very moment, as of the writing of this, I can't help constantly shaking and moving. Basically, if I hold long enough in the same pose, be it standing or sitting, I would start to involuntarily enumerate all the slightest discomfort I'm feeling at the moment and *have* to do something to address them, which most commonly, turns into moving around for no reason. While this is nothing more than a nuisance at best for the large majority of the time, it can really draw attention to itself when there's nothing else to distract those around me from it.  
> Next up: a slightly more annoying disorder that I suspect I may have sometimes. This is a strange one, because I vividly remember it popping up every once in a while in my childhood. It tended to stay for a while whenever it showed up, I'm talking a while as in a couple years; but on other days, I barely even remember it ever existing. It's like talking about it triggers it or something. ***OCD (Obsessive compulsory disorder)*** is the thing I'm talking about. It can manifest itself in numerous ways. From my experience, it can range from constantly blinking for no reason, to feeling the constant urge to make noises with my throat and nose, to twitching various muscle groups, to feeling the urge to touch the corners of objects, and to feeling the urge to bump my knees against each other. It is somewhat similar to ***TS (Tourette Syndrome)*** but to a milder and more voluntary(?) extent. I'm not even sure that OCD is the right term for it and it mostly likely isn't. TS should be more accurate but it's among the same field of disorders. Yes, it is weird, and yes, it bothers me quite a bit too because of its side effects like dry throat, sore muscles, and such. I believe it manifests when I'm under stress for extended periods of time. It kinda subsided for a long while but it can still pop up every now and then for a few days or so, until I forget about it and stop trying to stop it.
>
> ***Allergy***. My nose is allergic to god-knows-what, always. It and my lips are always dry. It would just swell and puff up and itch all the time. It gets worse with dry weather. I have to keep rubbing it. There is no other way of dealing with it. Trust me when I say I've tried. Lotions, medications, Chinese Medicine, nasal sprays. You name it, I've tried it. So far the most effective "treating" it is to apply a thin layer of Vaseline and really rub it in. But even it only acts as a temporary measure, effective for not long. Yes, I have to carry a small container of Vaseline with my all the time; so if you were wondering why my pockets are so full of random stuff, here's one for you. Admittedly, the situation has improved a lot as I've aged but it is just never quite gone. Nuisance, nuisance.  
> I'm no stranger to ***GI (Gastrointestinal) problems***. I practically suffer from one of those every week or so. Basically anything can trigger stomachaches and make a very bad day. To be honest, they are so frequent I have more or less gotten used to them. They come and go as they please with no rhythm or reason. They would find any reason to start making a ruckus, sometimes even none at all. I'm also virtually 100% certain that I'm ***lactose intolerant***, so that's one genre of food I can stay the fuck away from. Honestly, I wish I could talk more about this but like I said I have gotten so used to them it might as well be part of my official weekly routine.  
> Now that we've gone through all the minute and relatively insignificant bits, let's tread into the deep end. I believe I have some sort of ***anaemia***, not a severe case by any means, but it's bothersome and troubling. My mom and her family have a history of such a disease, so it's not surprising that I may have it. Anaemia, in essence, allows my blood to carry less oxygen around than normal. As such, I am really sensitive to oxygen level changes. Where others may not even notice, I can get slightly disoriented and light-headed when the oxygen level drops by any amount. Should the oxygen level drop for whatever reason, say, stale air due to a bad ventilation system, my brain starts to slow and I start to become less sensitive to my surroundings (i.e. my senses start to fade in a vague sense). Even in the shower, when there is too much steam, symptoms start to manifest. Like I said, I don't remember this ever being a problem in my childhood. I hypothesise that it manifesting only now is because I have grown and I have to use a larger portion of my cardiac capabilities to sustain myself, whereas when I was still small I could easily operate on half cardiac capacity. (Maybe this is the real reason why I'm restless - to pump blood around quicker? Not sure how scientific this deduction is though.) Over the years, I have learned to notice and identify the symptoms. It is not as easy as it sounds. Noticing yourself being delusional is a really tough feat, especially when the oxygen level drops so quickly the symptoms kick in right away instead of gradually. But let's get back to the point. Decreased cardiac effectiveness holds me back from a lot of stuff. I can't do medium-to-intense exercises without approaching the verge of a blackout and I can't recover at a normal pace. The most annoying thing is that I get tired all the god-damn time. I never seem to be able to get through a single day without feeling tired half-way. Perhaps this is the real reason I procrastinate and never managed to finish everything I wanted to finish within specific timeframes. I want to do so much yet I *can* do so little. I'm basically always on half battery despite only waking up 2-3 hours prior. I'm not sure there could be a solution/alleviation to this aliment, but I'm starting to take on more exercises as required by the university Physical Education, so let's see how that would go.  
> Did you think anaemia was the biggest thing? Far from it. I suspect I may also have some type of ***diabetes***. Thinking back, I believe the earliest sign was from my primary school years. I would always get thirsty when I'm trying to sleep. I would get up every minute or so to have sips of water, then I'll have to use the washroom because of all the water, and the cycle continues. It would take a really long time for me to fall asleep because of this. I basically can only rest when this whole ordeal tires me out to the point where I forget that I'm thirsty. Fast forward to today, I still drink water more frequently than those around me. It's like I'm doing transpiration all the time or something like that. Even when I'm just sitting still doing nothing I could still feel thirsty. And on bad days I could chug a whole bottle of water and it would do nothing to quench my thirst. I am always feeling dry. Washroom is a very popular venue in my daily routine. All this fuss about hydration and here I am suffering from basically the opposite problem. Now that I think about it, this could also go hand-in-hand with my anaemia to make me very prone to light-headedness, 'cus it also make my blood sugar level fluctuate quite a bit; could also be another reason why I'm always feeling tired.  
> I'm well aware I am weak and frail like some 80-year-old. I'm already looking for a full-body check and hopefully I can get one soon. Let's see how accurate my self-diagnosis is, although I'm not sure I'd like to be proven correct.

Honestly, a lot of the positions sound weird and make little sense, but hey, if it ain't broke, don't fix it. We were tasked to think of an activity that could bond students and professors. It was the usual sort of stuff really, nothing too remarkable. And after that we did a round of voting to decide who would be assigned to what position. ## October - 2021

### 02-10-2021
#### The undocumented and sealed-away memories
<!-- 💭 Philosophy -->
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
> Yes, I am aware that I have skipped making an entry yesterday. There was no particular reason as to why, only that I didn't do it. Granted, it was a holiday, so my sleep schedule was non-existent. To be fair, I stayed up all night after only having a small nap yesterday, so I'm kinda still living in the yesterday but that's besides the point. I was feeling anxious yesterday. Something was on my mind. I know for certain what the thing that had been clouding me is, but I do not wish to admit it, or even acknowledge it.  
> That brings me to my point, that not everything should be documented. I know I have mentioned when I started this journey that every day should have something worthy of a journal entry, that something as insignificant as a random thought I had during the day could suffice. Actually, Toby and I have briefly talked about this when he was convincing me to start this. But some things are just best left in the past. Some things are not meant to be remembered. If I wish something to not be in my life, not to be a factor in the definition of my character and my future decision-making, then it shall not be remembered. And I believe this should go for everyone. If a thought poses discomfort in you, but has little significance to anyone else, you should simply discard it - but don't try too hard, mind you, lest it become one of those unforgettable forgotten memories that would loom over you for the rest of your life. You should know what I'm talking about: repressed memories, denial, whatever you want to call it, they are the thoughts/memories you try your hardest to eliminate from existence yet inevitably re-emerges to haunt you from time to time. I have specifically not put the "thing"-in-question here, as you might have noticed. Generally, I've found that the best way to deal with them is to exploit your psychology. Try thinking about the same scenario, but in some sort of alternative timeline, where you had actually done or not done the thing that's troubling you, or something you would've done differently. Think of multiple of them. And here's the thing: try to be as vivid as possible. As unintuitive and counter-productive this may sound, it can actually help with overshadowing the actual event itself, until the point where you either cease to remember the event, or are no longer able to tell the real event from the crowd of alternative universes you have formulated. You see, your brain loves to latch onto bad memories. It's a pretty reasonable survival adaptation if you think about it. As such, negative events are significantly more likely to be remembered and subsequently recalled than positive ones. By mixing such an event with its positive alternatives, it could trick the brain into treating it as though it *is* a positive event, and have it be forgotten sooner. Making the false "universes" vivid is important because, our brains hate to have memories be vague and would always prefer to keep the more vivid version, for the same reason as before. I did not intend to make this some sort of science/psychology argument, but science and its sort interest me intrinsically. I have found varying degrees of success with this method. Some of them became vague and foggy, and maybe I've already forgotten some of them, which I obviously am not able to elaborate on.  
> Is this some sort of lying? Definitely. But I would argue not all kinds of lying is negative. *"We will always be the best judge of our actions, and they will always be punished in their own respect. A small crime will make you guilty for a short while, and a big one will make you feel awful for a very very long time, perhaps even for the entirety of the rest of your life."* That was a poorly-done paraphrase of a thing I've heard somewhere before, and I agree with it. Guilt is the best punishment against crimes, the same way looming mental worms are for missteps and misdecisions. This should be evident enough that we shouldn't try to evade them, until we consider that our brains also love to exaggerate situations and blow things out of proportions. Sometimes they can even be not in our control and we'll still have to suffer the consequences of it in the form of mental anguish. I am most definitely going out on a limb here, but I believe this could even be some sort of treatment for more, actually traumatic events, or at least be able to alleviate them. This method would be some sort of appeal system for our brains' auto-judgement I suppose. I feel like the analogy is starting to break down, but I hope I got the point out in time before this all melt into a pot of meaningless ideas and incomprehensible brain vomit. Every seal eventually leaks; and the only way to prevent that, is to have nothing to be sealed in the first place.

### 03-10-2021
#### Reality and dreams
<!-- 💭 Philosophy -->
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
> Yester-night I had dreams again. Yes, I'm aware that this is not a very significant topic to discuss, but let's hang on for a moment. My dreams typically revolve around my memories. The characters would be my friends and classmates (from secondary school, as of the writing of this), and the location would be in some sort of school (reminiscent of SJC). My dreams would from time to time involve plausible events with characters and locations convincing enough that I would actually confuse them from actual real events. Like, in a dream where a person would say something, and the next time I see them I could be reminded of that particular scene of the dream. I realise this may sound borderline psychotic, but it generally only lasts for like a day or two, until I forget about it entirely. Let's leave this phenomenon aside for a moment, for I don't know how to transition from this.  
> Sometimes I feel like I have some sort of future-telling ability. It's like I would vaguely remember one exact moment and that would happen later in life, the same way that I've seen it. It is never a "video clip" like some sort of vision, but it's more like some screenshot of my eyes in the future, if that makes any sense. Sure, it is most likely some sort of *Déjà vu*, but I think I have had occurrences where I can vividly remember seeing the thing before the event, instead of right as it happens. And yes, i have had a lot of such moments throughout my life, quite frequently, all things considered. But I guess it matters not anyway, unless I find mental asylums being my dream house.  
> I have been having re-occurring dreams for as long as I can remember, the earliest one I can remember from my childhood involve some sort of desert and pyramids, and another one involves being chased in my primary school. I should stop myself before this turns into a whole novel. Maybe I can tell them in some other time, but now is not that time. I would keep having the same exact set of dreams, with the same exact events, plot, and story. It really feels like I'm re-watching a movie over and over again. Until one day, my brain would decide that it has had enough of that movie, and would start obsessing over a different movie. I lot of them involve some sort of chase scene, and toilets (Yes, toilets. I guess it would be because I would feel the urge to urinate in my sleep and this would be the way my brain would address it. But of course urinate in your dreams solve nothing and so that dream would be me finding washrooms after washrooms. Could be another sign of diabetes(?)). As per all re-occurring stuff, my memory of them start to get more and more vivid each time I live through them. To the point where I could basically map out the location they take place in. I believe all of the locations are physically connected in some way. It's interesting because even though it is the exact same dream over and over again, I would be none the wiser in the dream, and would act out basically the whole thing with only little variations.  
> However, I've found myself getter more and more conscious and self-aware in dreams, and would sometimes even notice that I'm in fact in a dream. It's like a lucid dream, but I have still found myself be able to utilise that to my advantage. Speaking of lucid dreams, I believe I have had one, that I can remember of anyway, so far. Guess what I did in that dream? Of course my first instinct would be to do tests and experiments to confirm the boundaries and limitations of lucid-dreaming. I've found out that I would be able to feel myself in the bed, but if I think about too hard, I would start to wake up. So next up I tried to spawn something from thin air. It didn't work. I can't say I'm too surprised. Next up, I experimented with modes of locomotion. I think now is a good time to mention that the dream took place in the Pacific Place, and I was walking to the MTR station from school in that particular scene. I tried that walking normally works just as you'd think, and I could even glide on the floor with various degrees of success. However, as soon as I tried teleportation, I think I thought about it too hard or something that I woke up. It was definitely an interesting experience, but I wish I could've done more with it. But back to being self-aware/conscious but not fully lucid in dreams. I would be able to make more sensible decisions, but other than that it had basically served me to a small extent. Apparently it is in consensus that nobody can run in dreams. Everything would be floaty and you would be barely able to kick off the ground. There is a scientific explanation to this about nerves and haptic feedback but I shouldn't get too deep into this. Not being able to run and washrooms make me aware that I am in dreams very effectively. It's kind of like some kind of reality check or trigger word.  
> Damn. I thought I said I wouldn't talk too much about dreams. But I guess realising that you are veering off-track is better done late than never. The point is that, all of this dream ordeal reminds me of the one old Chinese story. In the story, "Zhong Zi" dreamt of himself being a butterfly. The dream was apparently so vivid that after he had woken up, he wasn't able to tell whether he was actually a human dreaming of being a butterfly, or a butterfly dreaming of being a human. I suppose this could be a slightly dreadful existential crisis. But honestly this is quite a scary thought. If you almost confused dreams with reality, you couldn't be sure that you haven't done that already. Consciousness as we know it is - well we don't know anything about consciousness yet. All we know is that it's an emergent property. But if that's the case, who is to say that our computers, smartphones, and other electronics are not already conscious. While they may not be able to do too much, they could be some sort of very low-level consciousness even as they way are right now. An even more mind-boggling idea is that we may not exist at all. We could just be a random assortment of atoms and molecules that just so happen to bump into each other in space and assembled into a brain by pure chance. It is actually not that infeasible with the enormity and eternity of space. It is a good thought experiment, or rather, a thought experience, but try not to think about it too hard. Is anything real? Does it even matter? I haven't even gotten into simulation theories/conspiracies yet but I feel like this should be as far as we go for the time being.

### 06-10-2021
#### Anatomy practical
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
> Today we had a practical session during our anatomy class. It was definitely a pleasant switch of environment from the mundane and monotonous lectures where the pace is too quick and the depth too advanced for us to understand without prior and subsequent self-study. I've heard that the time you need to self-study is somewhere around three times as much as the lecture hours, which sounded quite insane when I first heard it, and maybe it was for some courses, it is most likely true for this anatomy course. I guess even though this course is meant to be a lite version of what medics are studying, it is definitely not the case in practice. Since medical stuff require tons of background knowledge and reciting of countless terms, there is no studying half a medicine programme: you either don't study it at all, or you'll have to study everything; anything in-between is simply insufficient and non-constructive. So basically I am studying full medicine while being a quarter-medicine student. I guess this is why they say biomedical engineering is more demanding than pure medicine.  
> But that's besides the point. They displayed various cadaver body parts and organs on ten or so tables and talked about different stuff about them one-by-one. Stomachs, blood vessels, brains, half a face, bones, whole limbs, just to give a few examples. It is absolutely disgusting and horrifying, not the cadaver stuff, but rather the way the lecturers are handling them. I would say any normal human would treat them with care if they so decide to do as little as touching them, but the lecturer just went all-in poking with their forceps, pens, and whatnot, all without any gloves, mind you. I think the only takeaway I got from that session is that tissues are way tougher than you might think, even well after death. I guess I should've already known this from the dissections I've done in my secondary school. We dissected a pig heart, an ox eye, and a lab rat. And let me tell you right now, it is absolutely horrendously difficult to cut through skin, even with the sharpest razor blade and scissors. I remembered my hand literally hurt for a couple while from all the cutting and incisions I made on the rat. Another thing of note is that after the lecturer was done poking around a piece of sacrum, I noticed his hands are full of white powder, presumably bone dust. It was both amusing and concerning to witness. The sample was literally crumbling before our own eyes, and this guy just walks in touching and poking it like nobody's business. I guess the embalming fluids or whatever they're called don't absorb well into bones.  
> Anyway, the lecturers asked relevant questions while poking around the samples. That was the first time it really showed how lacking I am in such knowledge. I mean granted, a lot of the fundamental medical stuff are literally just reciting, which I am not bad at, per se, but I just cannot learn effectively like this. I mean I can recite if need be, but reciting is just a part of my short-term memory, which would literally vanish into non-existence after a couple days tops. I've always found it useful to make dumb theories to aid myself, which I may talk about at a later date. Some classmates, mostly non-locals for some reason, *were* able to answer the questions seemingly off the top of their heads. I guess they weren't kidding when they said in the very first lecture they were going to start studying. I appreciate their determination more than anything. I guess it also helps that they are non-locals, since I presume they wouldn't be here in the first place if not for their competence and hard work.  
> Yea I think I was supposed to talk more about the cadavers and how they were donated and stuff rather than my topic of choice. But I don't suppose there's more to be said about them. Perhaps again at a later date should we have another practical session with a more profound takeaway.

#### First night in my new hostel place
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
> I have moved in pretty much everything except for food and cookware to my new hostel place. I have finished my shower and am sitting at my desk in the room as of the writing of this. After much anticipation, I have finally met my other roommate. The stuff here in this hostel is much better in pretty much every single aspect. It's more colourful everywhere; it's more clean and pristine; the room is larger and actually has storage potential, with a proper and relatively clean closet; it has a lift; the desk is actually sized reasonably to be used properly; there exist microwaves, ovens, and even an air fryer. I mean it *was* built the most recently among all the other halls in CC, and it *was* my first choice in the preference priority list for hostels. I guess all this hassle translates to me being able to wake up later, and being able to keep on working on stuff at school when it's getting dark. Possibly I'll also have more energy for the day since I have eliminated two daunting commute trips, although I'll have to figure something out for my meals. I'm feeling this entry is becoming some mindless ramble again, so perhaps I should stop right here.

### 07-10-2021
#### HKU night walk with CNok
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> Today CNok and I got together to have dinner in Tsim Sha Tsui. It was originally intended to happen on 01/10 as a celebration for his birthday, but he wasn't free allegedly and it was postponed until now. Anyway, we had one of the best ramen I've had. Then we walked around a DONKI store for a bit, before heading off to HKU. He toured me around the HKU centennial building. It is probably safe to say that I have not seen a more gorgeous entrance to a campus before. I was immediately greeted with a long escalator ride, with lights at your feet, the whole ten miles. The wooden walls gave way to a huge mall-like space which was apparently only the lobby for one of the four sub-buildings that make up that campus. It was a huge well-lit space, with huge glass doors and such. We then walked around to find an unoccupied classroom and made it occupied by eating dessert in it. It was well-enjoyed, with the extra bits provided by the computer there. I should state that it had been raining since before we started eating in Tsim Sha Tsui, but it got much heavier when we were at HKU. We walked around the campus more from god-knows-where to god-knows-where.  
> I was pretty amused by the technology incorporated into everything: the doors were mostly automatic; students were able to enter, book, and occupy rooms simply by tapping their student ID card on the reader outside of the classroom doors. The most interesting part is that, we saw a ton of people in the libraries, like literally tons. The entire library was entirely full of students studying and whatnot, and it was already 23:30. Granted, it wasn't too late by then, but still. In CUHK, this is not the case. Students aren't allowed to enter buildings, lectures halls, and classrooms willy-nilly, and it is a rare sight to see the entire library full of students. I guess one reason is that HKU is basically located at the heart of the city, while CUHK is basically in the middle of nowhere. Students would still be able to go anywhere and do whatever even well after operating hours, whereas in CUHK you're as good as toast after MTR had finished their last train and you don't have a hostel place to settle down in.  
> It brings me to the point that there is an entirely different feel between the both of our universities. I'd like to say that HKU is at the heart of a city while CUHK *is* the city, and that would totally be true during that day, but at night, good luck convincing anyone that this huge dark maze of buildings and trees has any semblance of a city. I guess the main reason is that without shuttle buses, CUHK is just a huge mountain with no real easy way of traversal, whereas HKU is compact enough that students could just travel anywhere feasibly by simply walking. And because of that, the university is encouraged to keep its buildings bright and open for everyone. It is basically just a simple virtuous cycle of demand and supply. I guess there wouldn't be much of a reason to stay here late if you don't have a hostel place, and you won't stay late anywhere else other than your hostel place if you have one. To be honest I still don't understand why the "Night Service" shuttle buses' operating hours end at around 23:30 instead of until somewhere around 01:00. They could just dilute the number of buses and it would work just fine. I guess one reason would be that the drivers wouldn't be able to catch the last train. I only got back to my hostel at 00:30 anyway.  
> Some part of me would like to have a go at the university life in all of the (major) universities, but I feel like CUHK would always be my favourite, just because of its authentic culture - you rarely see some superficial stuff here, at least not on the few surface-most layers. Within my limited scope of knowledge, I guess I could describe it as being a mini foreign university, while having Hong Kong's unique university cultures and compactness.

#### Typhoon Lionrock strikes
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> Heavy rain ensued as soon as I woke up today, not that it ever stopped since last night. Apparently the red rainstorm warning was raised in the morning. Fortunately, I only have an assembly via Zoom and nothing else, so I didn't have to endure such horrid atrocities. During the assembly (that I did not pay attention to one single bit), the warning was raised again to black. Lessons later in the day were cancelled automatically. I thought all would be fine and dandy, until I remembered that we still had a zhong meeting later today. It was supposed to be held in the evening at school, but due to the cancelled lessons, they decided to bring it forward to the afternoon and make it a Discord voice chat instead. Well that arrangement was not favourable for me. I was still in the hostel, with my roommates bringing his friends to the room soon, so there is no chance I'm having a meeting there. I was going to go home during the weekends anyway so I just decided to take off and head home immediately. The decision was quite rushed because the rearrangement itself was quite rushed. I can't say I have thought it through too much. I think it is now the time I should describe the outdoors condition. The rain was heavy, as heavy as it could be. While it wasn't the worst I've seen, it was up there somewhere. Funnily enough, the rain itself wasn't the biggest problem, but rather the wind it came with. It made the rain go in all sorts of directions. It was quite impossible to use an umbrella properly. It was a battle against the rain and wind indeed. To make matters worse, I had my laptop in my backpack, so it's not like I can just wing it and embrace the rain. And for some godforsaken reason, I decided to wear shoes instead of slippers against my roommate's advice, and by the time I reached the MTR station, I think they had accumulated enough water to fill up an entire aquarium. That chain of horrible decisions and I was starting to believe that staying in the hostel would have be the better choice. But anyhow, I still managed to get home relatively dry-ish, if you ignore the bucket-load of water in my shoes. At least my backpack was waterproof enough to not get my laptop wet. I was a little late and it was already past when the meeting was supposedly going to start. But due to technical difficulties and whatnot, I didn't actually miss a thing. The meeting itself was unremarkable and not the point of focus here. I'd really hope something insightful would arise from this but I don't suppose I learned too much except not to attempt such a feat again.

### 12-10-2021
#### Academic competence
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
> Coursework and assignments are starting to get daunting, especially as the midterm is coming. The frequency of assignments are starting to increase and so is the pace of lectures. I used to think I was able to tackle the stuff in year 1 with relative ease, since I have studied a lot of them in my free time already, as a part of my Wikipedia deep dives or just simply out of my own interest. Although they have certainly given me an edge, dare I say it, over my mates, it is definitely waning. I would say the vivid moment this thought popped up is during that anatomy practical. It is not just a meme that what's taught in lectures had little to do with the assignments themselves. I was the one to assist in assignments at the start of the term, and now I feel like it's mostly the other way round. I have lapsed, yes, there is nothing more to said about this. My first midterm is coming next Saturday on 23/10. Maths midterm, it is. I suppose Maths *is* my strongest suit among all the other ones I'm studying right now, so I'm looking forward to perform myself in this test. Although I'll have to say that I've noticed I have become a lot more careless now than I ever had been during my secondary school years. I have been making tons of random and dumb mistakes all over the place. I guess myself being more and more insecure about my own competence is one of the factors that play into this, but if this goes on it would just be a horribly destructive vicious cycle. I really hope to get my sharpness back soon, perhaps if I start doing past papers, I could realign the few brain cells that I've left and have them work at more than half capacity. I have always had this kind of high whenever I do Maths or anything related to it for an extended period of time. It was quite addictive to be honest, I could just go through paper after paper of Maths and Physics without end. That kind of high could last for a while even if I happen to hit a wall and I would just power through with relative ease. I believe this is the kind of flow game designers talk about so often. It's the delicate balance of power and challenge to keep players on the edge and engaged. Now that I talk about it, I believe some game design principles could be applied to exam setting, but I doubt they ever will since exams were never the main point of this whole ordeal, but I think the devilish people in the HKEAA could learn a few things from such principles, for better or worse. I have noticed I have veered off-topic again. I will start doing past papers starting tomorrow, I hope to get my old self back. Wow that made me sound old.

### 13-10-2021
#### Self-awareness
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
> As you may have noticed, I tend to say that I veer off-topic a lot in these entries. This is a sort of self-awareness I guess. Toby and I have talked about this before. He commented that I was quite self-aware of what I say/type. For example, if a conversation is starting to get stale, or I've found that something I've said didn't quite land right, I would straight up just point it out and kinda do a fourth-wall breaking moment. It may sound cringey, jarring, or disregarding of the flow of the conversation, but I am willing to say that it helps more than it does harm. It's not like I'm doing them too consciously anyway. They just kinda pop into my mind and I would just feel the urge to point it out as the next logical step in the conversation. Like most things, it extends out of just conversations. Even when I'm in my own thoughts, I would do this. I would a lot of the times go meta and think about why I'm having the thought I was having. To put simply, I would randomly start psycho-analysing myself. This can sometimes also extend to psycho-analysing other people just because, although I tend not to do that very often. I realise this is a tough topic to try to explain, but I figured if you don't get it, then it probably doesn't concern you much anyway. I would do this even to my own actions, not only thoughts. But as you might have guessed, it could get meta again and I would be thinking about why I'm having a meta thought all of a sudden, and then it would just keep going deeper and deeper into this meta rabbit-hole. Yes, it does make be blank for a moment and I may randomly stop whatever I happen to be doing prior to this whole mental trip. It may sound really counter-productive, and to be fair it could be sometimes, but I think this is some sort of self-criticism mechanism. I do believe this kind of self-questioning behaviour did a lot to help me understand myself, more particularly, my thought process. I have talked about noticing myself going light-headed during showers in *[Undiagnosed ailments](#undiagnosed-ailments)*, and I think it may be a part of this mechanism. I could be doing something slightly off or inaccurate, and then my senses would start to tingle before this self-questioning start to kick in. For example, I could be going on a wrong though process in a question, or logical deduction, I would be able to feel like something doesn't add up and most of the time it would help me correct myself before my mistakes start to manifest themselves. It's something like the old Chinese saying "you should rethink your own actions many times per day". I'm noticing that I'm being really vague here and I'm well-aware that I lack the articulatory capability to express this fully, but I really hope I got whatever I tried to say out there. I mean this process *is* pretty vague by its own nature. Perhaps if I should find a better way to put this into words, I would make another entry.

### 14-10-2021
#### New phone
<!-- 💾 Technology -->
> I finally got a phone. The old one was a ***Huawei Honour AL-10*** and it broke ages ago, one or two months before DSE. The screen shattered and there were pieces of glass sticking out sometimes and it would be annoying. This new one is a ***Mi 11 Lite 5G***. I also got a new pair of earbuds with it: ***Mi True Wireless Earphones 2 Pro***. As per every time I had switched phones, I had to undergo the whole data transfer process, and it has always infuriated me. It struck me as odd that there is still not a perfect data transfer method outside of the Apple ecosystem. I guess it would be because of Android's non-standardisation given by its flexibility. But even then it still makes little sense. Sure, the Android ecosystem was wild a few years back, with all the tech companies innovating, trying new form factors and new gimmicks. But now? I don't suppose it would be the case anymore. The Android ecosystem has settled down for the most part, and as well it should. Everything is digital nowadays anyway, so I don't believe this wouldn't be something tech companies would like to invest in. Even Google themselves don't seem to be able to make this process seamless. There exist millions of data transfer apps out there and I could guarantee there isn't one that can transfer everything within reason. You'd think I am asking for too much here but I really ain't. All I'm looking for is something that can transfer all your files, contacts, apps, and basic settings. I don't suppose this would be too hard. Even the manufacturers of the phones couldn't seem to do that. But this problem extends far beyond phones. Computers also suffer from this, although I would argue to a much lesser extent. This may be something of a bias though, because I generally like to keep things on my computers clean and concise, whereas that on my phone is generally quite unorganised. As of the writing of this, I still have not yet finished the data transfer process, and I already am seeing duplicated contacts and whatnot. Such jank, such annoyance. Tomorrow I have a lecture at 14:30 and now it's already 04:43 as of this very sentence. Please for the love of god somebody make an app that works before I have to switch phones again... or perhaps I could be that somebody? I doubt I have that kind of time but it should be a ~~fun~~ peculiar project.

He seemed quite intrigued by university life, which to be fair, I don't know why he didn't ask his own older brother but I guess he has always been more estranged than he was (Yes I'm aware of the pronouns). ### 19-10-2021
#### One small step at a time
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
<!-- 🌞 Well-being -->
> This had been on my list of things to do in university since before I'm here. I had wanted to start doing exercises in whatever form regularly during my university years, especially during my stay in the hostel (i.e. this year). I got some friends and ran 6 laps around the field today. I have done this before in my PE lesson, which was quite exhausting to be honest. I think I got something like 14m53s. I almost died that time, with myself almost blacking out during a large part of that. I don't think I had enough blood sugar then, but again I doubt it had much to contribute to my long-term stamina. I'm glad to say that this time I no longer felt like blacking out constantly, but rather dehydrated. I could taste blood in my mouth during the later laps and for some time after I've finished. I've also been wearing a better pair of running shoes compared to last time so at least my feet didn't feel like burning from friction(?) afterwards. Either way, it felt much less demanding than my first ever attempt at running 6 laps, but my time somehow got even worse, clocking in at 14m56s. I guess it wasn't much of a time difference, and I definitely didn't feel like my entire respiratory system was collapsing during the laps as I did the first time, although my ribs, diaphragm, and abs did still expressed sharp pains. So I would say this *was* an improvement despite my time saying otherwise. Maybe I had just been running more slowly than I had before? To be fair, I had been keeping up at an excellent time per lap of around 2mins for the first 3 laps before I had to start walking to catch my breath. For the last few laps, I alternated between jogging and fast walking.  
> I haven't mentioned it yet, but the reason we were jogging was that running 6 laps is a part of the examination of our PE class. I think I will keep this up weekly at least, but I'd really like to integrate some gym sessions into the routine and work on that too ('cus it's another part of the examination). Weirdly enough, however, I wasn't particularly hungry after that and I couldn't even finish half of a moderately large meal, although I guess I did pour a whole bottle of water down my throat due to the aforementioned seeming dehydration. I actually was about to throw up right then and there 'cus of the stomach-load of water but eventually didn't.  
> I have always had terrible stamina. I would feel horribly exhausted and dehydrated after running even 100 meters during my primary school years, so I just stuck with just 60 meters. Conversely, I had excellent explosiveness which I guess played a role into my choice of going 60 meters only. I guess this was one of the reasons why I hated 4x100m races despite my teachers and classmates rooting for me a whole lot, which was, to be honest, the major reason I dropped out of the class 4x100m races. I realise I am withholding quite a bit of lore everywhere in this journal but I'd like to keep everything neat and organised, so I'll have to say this shall be a story for another time as tantalising as it is.

#### Progress for tedious tasks
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
> I've always had a way to kinda monitor the progress of tedious tasks while not making them psychologically daunting. A lot of people say that it would be best not to think about the task if you'd like it to go faster, but I'd suggest otherwise. Not only is it not feasible to just wing it and not plan about such tasks beforehand. I found that splitting then into arbitrarily small pieces would usually do that trick. For example, let's say there is a boring lecture that lasts for a whole 3 hours. The way I would make it easier is to set milestones, such as 10%, ¼, ⅓, 50%, or break down the entire duration of the task and do a countdown, like counting down from 300 every 5 minutes. For the most part it should work just fine, and should it fail, I could still implement a combination of these strategies. A thing that I used to do but not anymore is to do binary counting with my fingers. I would do that and try to do it in reverse, then invert the state of the fingers, and then the reverse of that. It could usually eat up a lot of time but in exchange I would have sore fingers at the end of that. As in the previous entry, my goal was to run a lap in 2 minutes, and I would break it up into 4 sections, each containing 100 meters and I would count down from 30 for each section. That would generally be a good enough distraction to make time fly. This entry really doesn't have too much significance, oh well.

#### Mental reality hypothetical
<!-- 💭 Philosophy -->
> There is a hypothetical that I just can't stop myself thinking about from time to time. What if everything I've ever learned about this world is all in my head? Everything I've seen, heard, tasted, done, what if they are all just a figment of my imagination? What if the real me is psychotic, and that I have been literally living in my own head this whole time? For all I know, I could be in a padded cell in some mental asylum, and from an outsider's perspective, I'm just acting out random things and saying random things that the virtual me is "actually" doing or saying. Or alternatively, I could just be completely naked on the streets somewhere and I'm just acting like it's normal and going about my day willy-nilly. It's sort of like a dream, but also not. It would be some sort of reality dream, if you may. Everything could have just been made up by me entirely too. Nothing may be found in my dream that is in the "real world". But to be honest, what would it matter if it turned out this is the case? I wouldn't know the difference, for once, and neither do I think there is a way to tell the virtual apart from the real. Could this be what actual psychotic patients are experiencing? Well, I'm asking like I couldn't be one of them, but yeah.  
> I guess this hypothetical extended from a thought I've discussed with numerous people. What we see, hear, or taste could be completely different, and we would be none the wiser. For example, my red could be your green, and yours could be my blue. It just so happens that we were taught since we were little that this neuron excitation is called "red" whereas that is "green". The same thing could be said to other senses. Could this be way some people like a particular food more than others? It could be the best taste of the world for one but the most disgusting taste possible for another. It's not like we could just swap consciousness and test this theory, not that it would matter anyway. If everything is so inconsistent to the point where it *is* consistently inconsistent, does that not make it constant? I'm not pulling this from my ass either. Scientists have found a gene that would make someone taste bitterness where others couldn't; or that some disorders would make someone not be able to feel an emotion or feeling. I think this should be enough prove that my theory could actually be true. Maybe I have something like that even. I mean I couldn't tell you what hunger feels like. Most people would just say they feel it in their stomachs but I do not have that kind of feeling at all, or rather if I do, I didn't associate it with hunger at all. Instead, I just kind feel like I want to eat and that would be that. I guess you could say my habit of eating is based more on impulse than necessity(?). Or I could be a complete fool, and that the feel/urge to eat *is* hunger. Either way, it would be impossible to tell unless you could get into someone's head, not figuratively.

### 20-10-2021
#### Academic frenzy
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
> It is definitely not common that there could be a theme that runs through your whole day. Today's theme would be academics. Perhaps it was because of the looming Mathematics midterm examination, seemingly everybody was in an academic mood, even outside of Mathematics. In fact, we have been doing Maths past papers together for 2 days already. I didn't make an entry about it yesterday because there was simply too much going on there already, but we went to Martin's hostel place again to do Maths past papers together. It was surprisingly productive without much interludes. We got stuck in a few questions and they were carried over to today. We decided to ask the lecturer during today's class but I ultimately was able to figure out the solution to two of them before having to ask him about the third question.  
> Then it was in the anatomy class which I had previously deemed boring. The course is actually called ***Human Anatomy and Physiology***. However, it is not until today that physiology started being taught. In my defence, anatomy *is* a boring topic. I mean it is *literally* just reciting terms and phrases and terms and phrase. It is dull, dry, and uninspiring, barring the occasional eureka moment when you figure out the roots of a composite term; whereas physiology concerns more of the actual mechanisms and interactions between different systems and such, from interactions as macro as how a stimulus can trigger a certain response through this chain of reactions, to those as micro as how an electrical impulse propagates through nerves cell via ion migration shenanigans. It is definitely a much more intriguing topic in my book. I know a lot of people may disagree, and would suggest that simple reciting is just what they need, but I cannot disagree more. I simply am not that kind of learner. I guess this is why I chose Physics and Chemistry as two of my electives in the first place (Biology was kind of an odd ball but it was an interesting enough subject). I'm not saying that there aren't terms and phrases one would need to recite, but they just simply make way more sense since basically all the terms are composite. It would be comparable to assembling words into a sentence instead of learning an entirely new language. For example, *leukocyte* is the scientific term for white blood cells, with *leuko-* being "white" in Latin, and *-cyte* being "cell" in Latin; and with *-osis* being "increase" in Latin, *leukocytosis* would be "an increased level of white blood cells". It simply works without you questioning it. All one has to do is to familiarise themselves to a relative handful of root words instead of an entire dictionary of jumbled letters. Either way, this was basically the only lesson in this entire course so far that I actually paid attention to some extent. Remember when I said everybody was in an academic mood? People actually started discussing Maths and Biology during the class and got me involved. It is always inspiring whenever I lead someone to the discovery of word composition. Their eureka moments are so precious it's almost orgasmic. I don't know too much about anywhere else, but this skill is undoubtedly essential to studying Biology. I guess it applies to Chemistry to some extent but I wouldn't say it counts too much.  
> Anyway, after class finished, we went to Martin's hostel place again to do more Maths. It was the third day in a row that I have been there. It was definitely a weird reason to head to someone's hostel place considering the normal popular choice is one of the dozen libraries we have here. Again it was surprisingly productive objectively, even though I feel like my brain was stuck for the most part.I haven't said this anywhere and I don't think I even noticed it until the writing of this very sentence, but I may be giving myself a lot of stress in the upcoming midterm. It is some sort of subconscious expectation of my Mathematics capability I guess. I guess I simply have not been doing enough Maths to keep myself in the flow I would find myself in a lot during my secondary school years. For once, I'm actually lacking in past papers and exercises to do.  
> I would say I'm now in the state I used to find a lot of my classmates in when they were stuck in problems: inflexibility. The inability to use all tools at one's disposal (theorems, theories, techniques, identities) to solve a seemingly difficult problem. I would go as far as to say that I was pretty good at navigating confusing or misleading questions during my secondary school years, definitely much better than whatever I'm doing right now. It could be the lot of new theorems, or it could just be my brain slowing down or my sloth asserting itself, whatever it is it's not helping. But hey, at least I found an incorrectly set question. However, I'm glad to say that I still haven't lost my sharp sixth sense where I could practically sniff out the general direction the solution should lie in, or traps the setter has embedded into the questions. I still stand by the notion that Mathematics and its derivatives should only be done with pencils. I believe it is some psychological trick where one would be more willing and daring to experiment with wild approaches because pencils are generally considered to be non-permanent. Working with pencils should encourage you to try out more methods despite them looking sketchy. I would argue that this habit of being more open to experimentations also affect your mental process to encourage the enumeration of all possible methods. I would find out some possible logic chains that I'm quite certain would exist somewhere in the solution, and in combination with different observations and techniques, I would simply play connect the dots and would figure out a path to the solution. While this method of mentally solving problem may be able to give me an answer pretty much all the time, they tend to be really convoluted with much redundancy and inefficiency. Instead of committing to the first approach you come up with like most people, I tend to put it aside in favour of finding a better solution. It's like what they say about chess: "when you find a good move, find a better one". I'm aware this sounds quite floaty and ungrounded, but I *did* say it comes from my sixth sense which I guess is my intuition. Perhaps this iterative process of finding more elegant solutions than the first one *is* what makes Maths and its derivatives addictive to me. Maybe that is the "high" I was talking about. I guess I should find someone with Mathematics symbols coursing through their veins to ask about this (\**ahem*\* Toby \**ahem*\*).

### 21-10-2021
#### Lecture time allocations
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> I have just gone through the Maths lecture notes, five chapters of them, and I've found that they are actually much shorter than I felt them being. It is weird really, because it seems that the lecturers spend the same amount of time for each and every topic, no matter it being basic definitions or some complicated theorem. I don't believe this is a good way to use the limited lecture hours, not by a long shot. I would go as far as to say that its *only* merit is the ease of progress tracking and time allocation. As you might be able to tell, it is exceedingly boring for students to listen to the lecturer talk about definitions and what the symbols and notations mean, for a whole hour. For instance, in the very first lecture, he talked about mathematics set symbols, as most university Maths courses like to do. It concerned symbols like '{ }', '∈', '***R***', ':', '∪' and such, and that was basically it. While I do believe definitions and properties are important to get right, I still don't believe they deserve as much attention as was given. It also gave students a wrong sense of difficulty, that if the lecturer spends this much time talking about trivial stuff, the course mustn't be too hard or demanding. However, this left not much time for the other topics that actually require more time and explanation. I found that theorems were kind of rushed through. Basically the lecturer would just talk about it for a while, then do one or two examples, and that would be it. It was definitely not enough time for students to explore the intricacies of the material. I get that students are expected to spend a lot of self-study time, even more so than lecture hours, but I doubt that should be an excuse for the improper allocation of time. Perhaps it is a policy given by the Maths Department, or it might simply be the lecturer himself, although I doubt the latter seeing that he had a lot of teaching experiences. Mathematics can definitely seem alien if you get on the wrong side of it. It simply does not tolerate inaccuracies in one's understanding of it. Maybe I should mend my statement about the notes being short. I should have said that it consists of only few important theorems surrounded by filler. In contrast, I would say the Physics course is arranged much better. Everything there *is* important, and this comes from the eyes of someone who has studied most of the covered topics in secondary school. Not to downplay their work, but maybe it is to no merit of the lecturer or the department, rather the lack of filler being a nature of physics in a way. I guess this should also mean it would take much longer to study for Physics. Speaking of which, its midterm is coming in two weeks, in-between of something like three other non-small assignments. Either way, the Maths midterm is on 23/10 and I should definitely focus on finishing all the past papers tomorrow.

Then Martin and I decided it would be a good idea to start studying for the upcoming midterms at the University Library, which brings us here, where I have finally gotten back to my hostel place at 03:30. I though I would be too exhausted to study at all but I am the kind of person who wouldn't stop for anything once I started doing something. He undertook a lot of work, curricular and extra-curricular, I'd even say more than he could chew, but he somehow manages, for now. I have witnessed for the past 2-3 weeks how packed his schedule is and how he is constantly working on assignments and studying non-stop, all-the-while being in a zhong and helping with an event of his college. I would say he has worked harder within this week than I have been this whole month. I too, have more than a handful of assignments, exams, and tasks hanging in front of me at any time. I can already tell I will be struggling with them immensely next week and I'm not looking forward to it. I guess at least there will be a day off on Friday 29/10 due to some CUHK holiday so I can't say it is as bad as it would have been.
