### 03-11-2021
#### Human Anatomy and Physiology CA1
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> I just finished taking the midterm exam for *Human Anatomy and Physiology* and I don't think it could've gone much better. It was a Multiple-Choice test with 21 questions to be answered in 30 minutes. I was able to do a first pass in 8 minutes with only 3 questions I was unsure about. I guess I could say it had gone rather smoothly, as smoothly as it could ever have been. I have spent so much time in the past week studying for it, something around 40+ hours, which was definitely more longer than I have studied for any one subject. But, I don't think this title was just since a lot of those hours could be saved had I been actually paying attention during the lectures. I spent time with my friends studying and also an entire weekend studying in my hostel place. While I can't say all of those hours were spent as effectively as they could have been, they were definitely not unproductive. Honestly I think some of the hours spent studying with my friends were more productive than those alone, although it varied quite dramatically.  
> ***Human Anatomy and Physiology*** was definitely the class I dreaded, and thus procrastinated the most among everything else before I started studying for it. Honestly, I expected it to be more challenging, but it really wasn't too bad. I guess the majority of dread came from the Anatomy part since it mainly consists of reciting and nothing else. I kinda expected that before I started studying, but still took more time than I had planned for. Contrarily, the Physiology was a lot easier than I had expected and had taken me way less time and effort than expected. I think another reason I procrastinated was because I kinda felt like this would be something like a proof to myself that I could potentially be capable of studying Medicine.  
> Honestly, studying for this wasn't too different from studying for DSE Biology, which was kinda unexpected, given how different the circumstances were. Sure, I couldn't skip parts as liberally as I could for the DSE syllabus, but it was still relatively, dare I say it, relaxing to study for. Some topics were completely covered by DSE syllabus so I barely even needed to revise them at all; and a lot of the Physiology slides were redundant being alternative conceptualisations and presentations to the same ideas as the previous slides. I guess they were really the saving grace for me, since if not or them, I would surely not have enough time to go through the entire syllabus in time. I would say I had been quite thorough with my studies, frequently making flowcharts and tables to aid myself. Honestly, they helped more than I had imagined. Basically I could save studying a whole 10 slides for every flowchart/table I made, whereas for DSE, my own flowcharts and tables barely helped. I guess it could be that the teaching materials were already so concise and precise you couldn't have done too much as an improvement whereas the lecturers here supposedly wouldn't want to waste too much time nitpicking their slides if they could already get the point across just fine. One thing I'll say is that I'll definitely start to pay more attention to the lectures from now on, at least for all the Physiology lectures. Heck, maybe I could even just go through the lecture notes myself during the lectures if I find them boring.  
> There isn't much else to mention except we also had another practical session after the exam, which wasn't too noteworthy except for what had already been mentioned in the previous entry about practicals. Physics midterm is coming on 06/11, so I should probably start studying for it now.

The dress code was that we had to wear the zhong T-shirt and jeans. And I'll say it right here: I *hate* jeans. They are really as uncomfortable as an article of clothing can get. The creases it would make at the posterior of your knees whenever your knee bend even slightly are absolutely irritating. Unless they are made of really thin fabric, this problem would be there no matter what. Moreover, their pockets are never deep enough for anything, and their positioning is horrendous. Maybe I'll talk some other time about my grunt with various species of clothing, lest this become an endless rant.

### 06-11-2021
#### Physics midterm
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> Honestly, I basically winged this midterm. Partly because I didn't have much motivation to study it, partly because I had no clue how to even study it in the first place. Either way, I basically did the least amount of preparation possibly; any less and it wouldn't have counted at all. I skimmed through the lecture slides, did some past papers to no avail, and typed up a cheat sheet (Yes it was allowed). Surprisingly, I'd say it went the most smoothly among all the midterms. I had time remaining for some reason, to perform double-checks and self-doubt. Interestingly, the most challenging parts of the entire Physics midterm were questions that involved more Maths than Physics, where you had to do a lot lot of algebra to prove something. The cheat sheet honestly didn't really help much 'cus I don't think you would really need a cheat sheet or formula list if you are familiar with the curriculum. I don't think I've referenced the formula list at all in my DSE, except for the Einstein(?) atomic stuff. Anyway, after sessions of peer-cross-checks, I was feeling pretty confident about my performance. Honestly I have no clue what this entry would be about when I started writing it but I kinda feel like I should write something, so this is that.

### 09-11-2021
#### Maths midterm results
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> *[Here](#mathematics-midterm) is the corresponding post-exam evaluation.*  
> Today, the results for the Maths midterm was released. I got 110 out of 150 which translates to 73.33%. It definitely wasn't ideal, and I can't say I am too impressed by my performance. And in addition, I believe some marks were deducted unjustly which I will probably request a regrade on. I guess I can't dwell too much on this, since a non-insignificant amount of the deducted score came from time constraints. Despite this, it shall't serve as an excuse for the other rather-significant amount of that from my carelessness and incompetence. As of the writing of this, I still am not too sure about how GPA is calculated for each and every course, nor do I know whether they are calculated by absolute grading or relative grading, so I can't say how bad my current GPA is right now, especially not when my performances in the other midterms are still shrouded in mystery. I can't say I'm too thrilled about everything that's going on in my life in terms of academics. Not just the midterms, but also the assignments, or more specifically the time allocation for them. Since about two weeks ago, I had lost track of my to-do list and had been failing to stay ahead of it. (I guess you can tell by how many days I've skipped writing entries for recently) Last week flew by while I barely even noticed it. Deadlines are now looming closer and closer while I still have little clue about them. I basically started giving up some of my group assignments and had left some of them to the group and basically started free-riding. That's quite a role-reversal for me seeing that it's usually me who's the one being free-ridden. Yes, I'm exaggerating a bit here but honestly it's further away from the truth. I know I have to keep my shit together, but with the projects, presentations, assignments, meetings, and finals all piled up and due in November, I can't say I have the confidence I could achieve this and lighten my burden, both academically and mentally, before they prove too great to be handled and I just end up breaking. Yes, internal transferral is still a thing, at least I hope so. It would just all come down to my performance in my finals and whatever should happen in the next semester.  
> > ***Post-script***:  
> > Honestly this semester felt more like a whole year than barely half of it. I guess things are just moving at a different pace than I'm used to. I'll probably have more insights once the semester actually ends, so let's wait and see.

### 13-11-2021
#### Zhong promotion period
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
> It's now supposedly the promotion period for my zhong (and most other ones). The pictures that we took before, it was for this. The design team whipped up profile pictures for everyone and started making posts on Instagram. Apparently I'm the first person to have their post posts, alongside with a brief text about myself that I've written, strangely in third-person as requested, as though someone else was introducing us. They had us change all our profile pictures on Instagram to be that. We'll also have a banner and tons of other things. I realise I haven't yet stated this, but the promotion period is the period of time where zhongs have to make promotional material to basically make themselves known. Honestly I don't see the reason why this is necessary but I guess it's a kind of tradition. Not all types of traditions are good, honestly most of them are bad, but this one I'm mildly fond of. Apparently most zhongs are having their members "dem beats" but mine doesn't even have a beat to begin with. It's rather interesting that a zhong can be so chill that its beat is non-existent. I guess it's both a blessing and a curse. It's supposed to be really demanding and "chur", as seen in my one of my roommates; but on the other hand, it's an interesting experience and something that's unique to Hong Kong university culture. Either way, where people from other zhongs may be busy with the promotional period, I'm still busy with actual zhong tasks with emails flooding in. I'll still have to refine the consultation document after this. Good news is, as busy as I may be, I'm starting to regain control of my own tasks and to-dos, which was the most helpful thing I could ever have done. It's not to say that I'm not busy or my schedule not packed in any way, it's just that my mind is no longer as clouded as I had been this past two or so weeks. At any rate, I should really get going.

### 19-11-2021
#### Zhong new beginnings?
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> As you might be able to tell, I haven't been writing entries for quite a long while, partly because I had been busy with schoolwork, but more so, I had been busy tackling about zhong stuff. I'll try to make the story more straightforward and clear, but I don't believe it is even possible at this point, especially considering everything had been evolving over the course of at least a month. To put simply: the zhong had been on the verge of disintegration.  
> From the every beginning, around the pre-pre-consultation, the president (hereby **P**) and internal vice president (hereby **IVP**) had been very close even before the establishment of the zhong. Apparently, they had some sort of issue with the external vice president (hereby **EVP**), and thus their relationship was never good. At the beginning, things were still fine as they should be, but quickly declined when the P and IVP stopped responding to the EVP's messages in their own group. When the EVP added them to the cross-zhong group and initiated self-introduction as he should've, the P and IVP immediately ignored it without ever saying a thing in that big group. When we were busy working on the consultation document, the P and IVP barely gave any orders or suggestions. When one of the designers whipped up designs for folders and single-line papers, which a lot of people including myself thought were amazing, the P and IVP immediately banned his designs without giving much in terms of reasoning. Things started escalated when we were nearing the promotion period. We were supposed to decide on a time for various different parts of it (placement of banner, physical promotions, consultation dates, etc.), but what should've been decided on together by the whole team, were instead decided on by only the P and IVP. That was not too big of a deal yet, but the thing was that they didn't even bother to inform the rest of the zhong about their decisions after making it, thus making the whole zhong extremely confused and disorganised. To add on, we had only ever had one meeting immediately right after the establishment of the zhong, and never since. To put simply: everything was messy as hell.  
> Those were the objective side of things. But of course things were never going to be that simple. One day, I was informed by Wales that the P and IVP were proposing to quit and give up this whole ordeal all-together. They were accusing the EVP for his lack of communication and being too external, not catering for internal business. They reasoned that the reason they hadn't been saying much in the group was that the president and vice presidents themselves were having arguments. Keep in mind that I was still part of the "I have no clue what the fuck is going on" gang and had no knowledge of the things mentioned in the last paragraph. They were proposing that they were now left with two choices: either they'd split up the zhong and exclude the EVP, or they'd quit by themselves. Now either of those options had more that meets the eye. Splitting up the zhong to exclude just one person would never happen. If splitting were to occur, there would undoubtedly be two sides battling to the death. Them quitting by themselves would never happen either. If they were to quit, it is most certain that their supporters would also quit. They were trying to convince Wales, Tom, and me to join their side if this splitting would happen. According to them, some other people in addition to some members from the previous zhong would join us to form a new zhong, and they promised that the new zhong would function fine under the guidance of the members of the previous zhong.  
> I was slightly sceptical of them, since it was supposed to be the IVP's responsibility to ensure such conflicts wouldn't happen, and that they hadn't yet raised evidence or convincing arguments as to why this would be necessary. But since I have only heard their side of the story, and saw someone with more insight also agreed to stand by the P and IVP, I was rather convinced. Wales, Tom, and I were basically as far away from this mess as we could've been, and as neutral as we could've been this whole time. I guess this would be the reason why they were trying to recruit us since we still hadn't yet heard the other side of the story.  
> Until yesterday night, when the "other side" consisting of the EVP, Kart, and more people asked me to join their meeting. They were formulating a plan for when the zhong would split. I at first wasn't too sure about conspiring against the P and IVP since the EVP was still the villain in the half-picture that they had painted. But upon further reasoning, I discovered that the EVP had basically nothing to do with this whole ordeal. He showed me prove of him trying to initiate conversations between himself and the P and IVP to no avail. Kart was the first person to notice this abnormality and had been trying to bring together both sides for already a whole month, also to no avail. According to him, the P and IVP stood firmly on their grounds and refused to back down, saying that splitting was the only option. So far, that proof of initiation was the only solid evidence that I had ever seen since this whole ordeal started, and of course I immediately reinforced my scepticism against the P and IVP. But I told myself that the EVP and Kart could have just been making this up and using one instance of their miscommunication against the P and IVP.  
> However, when Tom asked if anyone had been complaining of his productivity, nobody had. The P said in the pre-consultation to the previous zhong that several members of this zhong had been complaining that Tom had done nothing. Of course, the imposter could be among us, and someone could've complained without pleading that they had done it. But this accusation made little sense either way. The night before the pre-consultation, Tom had been openly asking about financial budgets for various events in the big group, and had worked on the entire financial statement all by himself. This much was not to be doubted. His efforts and contributions were as solid as diamond, and it was quite hard to believe that someone had made such an accusation. Alongside with other plot holes, I had figured that the P and IVP had been making up stories and falsely accusing others. They said that the idea of either splitting or quitting was given by the P of the previous zhong, but upon further investigation with members of the previous zhong, we had found out that he merely approved that it could be possible but had not suggested it. Among various other things, I had decided that I couldn't trust them anymore.  
> We then went to the library for further planning. I still hadn't chosen sides yet at that point, since I hadn't been too close with the people on "this side" barring a few. However, they managed to show the passion and determination to win this war that I failed to see on "the other side". They kept asking and inviting members of the previous zhong to consult and plan with. They managed to lock the P and IVP out of the Instagram and Google account of the zhong, lest they delete them to erase evidence. They had already made plans for the entire work distribution, consultation, and promotional period within the short 4 hours, something that didn't happen in the old zhong in the two months we've established. I was finally convinced that this *would* be the zhong I'd like to be a part of instead of the mess we had before.  
> To make a long story short, we'd had to wait until today for the P and IVP to make their decisions. And finally they did. They resigned in the group with the previous zhong, along with two of their supporters. Wales also quitted since he absolutely despised messes of social interactions. Now we are working on a (somewhat) fresh canvas, with Kart being the new P, the old EVP staying EVP, and Marting being IVP. We definitely had much more passion and ambition than before. While I can't say we would be successful, I can say that at least this would be more productive than whatever we had before.  
> > ***Post-script***:  
> > This is already as short as I could possibly make this story. I have *definitely* missed something or made mistakes somewhere, but I hope the general plot/flow of the story made sense. I tried to be as unbiased as I could be in the narrative but of course we all know that it is rather impossible. I had decided to lay out the story in chronological order instead of the order I experienced it in, since I decided the alternative would be more confusing despite being more dramatic and movie-like with all its betrayal and last-minute plot twists. There will definitely be more entries regarding this. This isn't anything that you'd see every day, and frankly I don't believe this had even ever happened in CUHK before, so either way we're making history.

### 21-11-2021
#### Zhong war begins
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
> I told you things were never going to be that simple. We immediately started working on stuff for the new zhong assuming that would be the end of this whole ordeal, but today the other side just announced they are going to battle us to the death. Fuck. You can initiate a battle well after resignation? My brain is on the verge of melting and shit. I had been working on assignments for the whole night and now this. You can tell my brain is beyond messy but I guess I can't be anymore, not if I'd like us to come out on top. Emergency meetings would be extremely frequent and demanding, on top of the piled up assignments and projects, wish me luck. First in CUHK history, I guess.

#### Zhong war ends
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> Yes, I realise how stupid this is seeing that this supposed "war" barely lasted a day.  
> It is now 04:23 the next day but time is the least of my concerns right now. We started a meeting since 18:30 in Martin's room in ***Shaw College***. It was rather smooth sailing until the P and VPs of the previous zhong decided to side with the other side and started to explicitly blame our side for various things, no matter how insignificant they are. Everything was exaggerated and blown out of proportions to an unfathomable extent. Pardon my strong and biased phrases but as biased as I am right now, I can say I am already more neutral than the P and VPs of the previous zhong. But I suppose all of these talks are futile right now, since we have all decided to stop and quit seeing that this competition was basically rigged and it was no longer worth continue doing. I am writing this on my friend's laptop since I'd like to document my thoughts this very moment. As mentioned before, the other side started using dirty psychological tricks to recruit people and even convinced the P of the previous zhong to help their recruitment. It was simply not worth going on since we heavily doubt it would end any other way with the largest figures of the previous zhong rooting for and canvassing for the other side. They had been found to have kept contacting the "other side" after they supposedly "resigning", and even manipulated rules and deadlines of the duel to favour the "other side". We simply lacked the mental power to keep fighting this rigged battle. We simply failed to see the point fighting the unwinnable unless we also play dirty. To be fair, we had a really strong passion for it, the moment before their dirty tricks let themselves known. The meeting was so heated right until then. Everything started falling apart: our plans, ambition, everything we had ever discussed about. I am not the best person with words so I can't possibly express what I am feeling right now. Some was furious, some sad, some cried. It was really a shame to not have this go through till the very end. I myself, as insignificant my post might be, put so much effort into the events assigned to me. I had spent weeks managing and replying emails from graduates for their photo days; I made a whole lists for not only my photo day but also helped the others with their respective photo days; I spent days working on a Google form for freshmen of the next year, trying to make it as enticing as possible to peak their interest in joining the ODay; I even picked up an entirely new event just because they were lacking in manpower. But all of these are futile right now. We have all posted our resignations. Our new ex-P even spent a whole phone call reasoning and scolding the P of the previous zhong for their incompetence. I can't possibly express in words how intense the atmosphere was. It would be something like both heated and sombre.  
> As for the aftermath? What's next? I don't know. I don't think any of us know. The previous zhong added us all back to the group after we left it, seemingly trying to change our minds implicitly. Such drama is not the kind I'd usually like to get involved in. But I stayed until the very end, the bitter end, and I can't say I have any regrets working with "this side", as short as it had been. As I had mentioned, I have tons of work all piled up, so I suppose this could leave my dedication to be solely on my academics. I'd say this is like a fetus dying in the womb, but such metaphors do little showing the true nature of such trauma. I guess it allowed me to see the dark side, or rather, the intentionally or unintentionally incompetent side of human. I should stop before this starts getting philosophical and become gibberish. As per usual, I've left out a lot of details, both good and bad ones. It's not like I could've documented everything anyway.  
> As I had previously mentioned, things and emotions usually wouldn't kick in until after a while when they had settled. As for now, it is currently 05:00, and I'll be sleeping in Martin's room tonight. I shall sign off now.

### 23-11-2021
#### Flopped BMEG presentation
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> I have no idea what happened. Today was supposed to be when the group presentation of our BMEG project happens. I woke up early but somehow managed to fall back asleep despite not being tired. I completely missed the the session and only got up when I got a phone call from my friend 30 minutes into the lesson when my group was being called onto the stage. I have no idea why none of my 5 groupmates had decided to call me when they inevitably realised my absence within the first 10 minutes of the lesson. I was completely baffled. The silver lining is that it was a video presentation so it at least didn't completely flop. However, I failed to attend the lesson which means that my attendance wouldn't be perfect. And in this course, a non-perfect attendance would translate into at least a 10% penalty of the final score, which I find rather idiotic, to say the least. It wasn't like I could've asked a friend to help me sign my attendance either, since it was taken with our Student ID card. On top of that, the presentation consisted of a Q&A session after our video was played. That accounted for 4%, and according to my groupmates, they had no clue what they were asked, so it was highly likely that the questions concerned the part I worked on. Welp, so that's at least 14% gone from a course. I guess the silver lining would be that it was only a 1-credit course so it shouldn't affect my final GPA too much, fingers crossed. Welp, now I'm going to look like a free-rider despite having taken on the work of two other groupmates because their work was unsatisfactory, and I'm going to be talked behind my back for this deplorable incident.

### 24-11-2021
#### Physics midterm results released
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> *[Here](#physics-midterm) is the corresponding post-exam evaluation.*  
> The results of my physics midterm examination had been released today. I got 93.5% in it. As mentioned, it felt rather easy at the time, and it sure seemed so now. Despite this, it shalln't be used as an example to be followed since I skipped practically all lectures and tutorials of Physics barring the first few, and I meant "*all*" when I said "all". I'm in a kind of special relationship with Physics, I would say. It was the subject that I banked the most on achieving a 5`**` in in the HKDSE, and hence it was the most disappointing to not have a 5`**` in, alongside with Maths. So I'd say I kinda have a grunt towards Physics. It's not like I dislike Physics or anything, it's just that it can be annoying at times. I guess I could say tha same about Maths, seeing that university-level Physics is basically applicable Maths with more flare anyway. Either way, I guess it was somewhat justified since the syllabus mostly covered stuff that I already had the fundamentals nailed in my secondary school years - actually not really, since it now apparently involves more derivatives and integrations than the Maths paper. "Like" is a strong word but I genuinely think I like Physics. The way it makes you think and reconsider interactions based seemingly on intuition, and makes you wonder what makes this whole world tick. It allows you a playground in which you can express your logic and proficiency in the subject matter to a satisfying degree, but not too boundless and ungrounded as pure Mathematics can sometimes be. No matter how complex the proposed scenario might be, it would always work at the very end. A solution will *always* exist, since basically the entirety of existence itself banks on it. I'd say it would be very rare that you couldn't visualise a Physics scenario with enough comprehension of it. But that was enough of me being a salesperson for a field of science. The point is, I have no idea what the point I was trying to express was. Physics is quite beautiful I guess (when excessive amounts of calculus aren't involved).

### 25-11-2021
#### Year 1 Semester 2 course registration
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> It is that time again. I spent so long preparing for it and yet everything was to be decided simply by how soon we click a single button once the clock struck 20:30 sharp. I have so many problems with this system, as do every single human being to have ever used it. Out of the top of my head, I can already think of a handful of better solutions. In conjunction with the auxiliary tools, or rather, the lack of, the system seemed to be designed to be hostile towards students to make their experience and the courses they subsequently have to take as miserable as possible. I have come across with a lot of custom-made tools and applications specifically for CUHK students: shuttle bus app, timetable manager, school information hub, just to name a few. Apparently our IT department is either too incompetent or just couldn't care enough to do their job properly to serve the university's students. Again, this project would probably never be done if I fail to create a working prototype before my initial influx of energy and determination had subsided, but I have started working on a timetable planner system to aid students in course registration. I tend to waste a lot of time on random programming projects during my free time anyway, so I thought this would be quite a useful way to waste time during the semester break, or some other holiday. If no further entries about this project were to exist, it would very likely mean that the project was long forgotten and had faded into obscurity, like so many other ones had.

### 26-11-2021
#### Taxis can fly
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> I woke up at 14:02 today, at home, and had a lecture in CUHK, at 14:30. Fuck. It would take 50 minutes at the very least, just to transit. But I had the bright idea, or rather, the only idea, to try my luck and took a taxi. Honestly, that was a rather big gamble since taxi drivers usually tend not to entertain passengers trying to go beyond their usual work area, namely from Kowloon to the New Territories. Anyway, I got onto the taxi at 14:10, and somehow managed to arrive CUHK at 14:26. I was quite dumbfounded by the speed it managed. For the times we tried driving there, it took around 25 minutes. But I guess I shouldn't be surprised by how efficient Hong Kong people can get. And to add on, the taxi driver took me exactly where I needed to go to (***Chung Chi College*** entrance) since he apparently didn't know any other conventional entrances (MTR station/ Main entrance) to CUHK. Apparently taxis can really fly in Hong Kong, hence the term "fly taxi". Oh yeah and it costed something like $136, so never again.

#### Human Anatomy and Physiology CA1 results released
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> *[Here](#anatomy-and-physiology-ca1) is the corresponding post-assessment evaluation.*  
> There isn't much to say honestly, but I thought I should make an entry for every exam/assessment just for the sake of documentation, but also for cross-referencing my post-test feel versus the actual scores themselves. Anyway, I got 18 out of 21, which translates into 85.7%. I don't know how to comment on this except that it seemed to be a rather admirable score compared to the rest of the class. The fail rate was as high as 30%, if I had heard correctly. True or not, I should be preparing for the next CA, which was proposed to be on 07/12, weirdly close to the finals seeing that the Physics final would be on 10/12 and the other subjects would soon follow. Not much else to comment except my piled up work again.

#### Some zhong meal/gathering
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
> Honestly, I don't know at this point. I believe I no longer have any clue what this whole ordeal is evolving into. The IVP of the "other side" contacted a few of us yesterday trying to recruit a whole new cabinet, which proved to be quite futile, seeing that they still haven't yet managed to establish one even today, as of the writing of this, on 29/11. Either way, the people on "this side" along with two of the previous zhong who we are close to had decided to dine out, at exactly where everything had started, the place in *Fo Tan*, as seen in the entry on 30/09. I didn't write too much about that restaurant thing then, since I thought it was rather ritualistic and shouldn't warrant too much of a mention. Someone proposed that we should "go back to where everything had started" and hence that was the place that we chose, or at least that would have been the case, if that someone had booked the correct place. He actually booked the place next to that restaurant, which surprisingly tasted a lot better than the place we were originally planning to dine at, not to mention it had air-conditioning which the other place didn't. It's not like I understood the concept of "returning to the starting point of everything" in the first place. Other than that the food was rather tasty and that we managed to scam the restaurant by having them repeatedly refilling our large pot of congee for at least five times. The staff/boss was getting really annoyed which was quite funny. As usual, the meal itself wasn't otherwise too eventful.  
> After the meal, however, I had the bright idea to walk our way back to CUHK, and for some godforsaken reason, they entertained the idea. We got some ice cream along the way at least. We had to walk right through the *Fo Tan* MTR station, just to get to the pedestrian walking, which I found funny. We ended up walking 4km along Tai Po Road, which took 50 minutes. Honestly, it was a rather enjoying walk, with all of us chatting and delivering plastic. They blasted some music but that led to some dumb shenanigans. We took some pictures at the entrance to ***Chung Chi College*** and that was pretty much the end of it. Who knew an unplanned walking trip could be that interesting?

### 29-11-2021
#### Stuffed alpaca toys in CUHK
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
> I was walking with Martin in CUHK at night and came across two stuffed alpaca toys just laying next to garbage pins. Seeing that they weren't dirty and didn't have any tears, I decided to bring them with me. We walked around CUHK with them, much to the amusement of other pedestrians. Since we were originally intending to go to a study room to work on our assignments or study, we just brought them into the room. It wasn't too eventful since the study room was isolated and there were only the two of us. However, when it was past its operating hours, we were asked to leave and had to continue at the ***Chung Chu College Library*** which was nearby. I found it quite funny when I walked in willy-nilly with two huge stuffed toys in my arms. As of the writing of this, I just finished my assignment, and we are still sitting in the library with the two huge stuffed toys beside us on the table. I guess I'll have to disinfect them either way before I should further handle them.

## December - 2021
### 07-12-2021
#### Finals approach
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> It has been very long since the last entry, my longest hiatus yet. I thought this entry would serve as an update to everything that's going on. First off, the finals are coming, starting from 10/12, until 15/12. Let's not dwell on the fact that I have basically no hope of studying in time just yet. 10/12 would be when my Physics final examination would be, and it just so happen to coincide with the deadlines of *two* college general education term papers. I have no clue why they even exist in the first place, considering general education courses are supposed to relatively chill and smooth-sailing, not to mention the plurality of which. That alone is exotically dumb. However, on top of that, the deadlines are also purposefully set in a way that it would guarantee time conflicts with students' revision schedule. Why on earth does this college exist at all anyway. While it may be true that it is relatively trivial to get good grades in the college general education courses if you at least tried a little, it also comes with a price, namely the sacrifice of other courses. Is this a fair trade-off? I mean the *two* college general education courses do account for 6 credits in total, so maybe I should take this deal and focus on the term papers- ***fuck no***. No one should be made to make this horrible decision between a rock and a hard place. Why in the fuck is chung chi college this sadistic? Yes I didn't capitalise or bold or italicise it 'cus it does not deserve any respect at all. All of these might as well be some satanic ritual for all I care, it's not like it's any different from carving my heart out to be sold to the devil. As things stand, I have just finished the second ***Human Anatomy and Physiology*** continuous assessment, and now I have precisely 2 days left to finish two term papers and to revise for the Physics final. You might think I have terrible time management and that's the cause of this whole ordeal but I can assure you that it is not true. I don't think I have stopped working since the beginning of October, and I haven't even stepped out of CUHK for more than a month, barring the few hours as in *[Taxis can fly](#taxis-can-fly)*. I already have more than enough of actual work to be done, and now this shit popped up. I could've put them in my well-beyond-saturated to-do list, *IF THEIR TOPICS WERE ANNOUNCED MORE THAN A WEEK BEFORE THEY'RE DUE!* I can't stress this enough but it is excessively abusive. No one in this world should be given this stupendous amount of workload just for an insignificant college general education course - oh did I say *a* college general education course? 'cus by "a" I meant two courses plus weekly assemblies. I'm saying it right now, that I'm not giving these shitty papers more than 10 hours combined, and that is already too much time allotted. I don't care that the title of this entry implies this would be oriented around the final examinations. Don't expect these kind of rants to ever stop until I graduate, because as long as this abysmal college share the same dimension as me, I would be suffering in more ways than one.

#### Human Anatomy and Physiology CA2
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> I just finished taking the second CA of this course, which is interestingly 8 days before its corresponding final examination. I definitely performed worse this time than the last, there is little doubt to it. I didn't have enough time or mental capacity to revise to extents that could be considered effective. I mean I did manage to go through the entire syllabus and made flow-charts and such, barring one PowerPoint where I literally just discovered the existence of 3 hours before the test. I was really not in the flow when I was doing this test. I just wasn't feeling it. Just from glancing, I could already tell I have made countless mistakes, although I did manage to find a mistake in the questions which the professor later confirmed, so I guess I wasn't completely brain-dead when I took it. If I have understood the terribly confusing mark allocation scheme, this CA should only account for 7.5% of the final grade. I don't know what I can comment about it really. I guess I could just hope for the best.

### 10-12-2021
#### Physics final
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> Right off the bat, I'll admit that I did not study as much as I should. Honestly, I didn't even prepare at all, except for making the cheat sheet. But, despite this atrocity, I do believe I performed rather well in the exam. This entire week has been a mess. My sleeping and working schedule was haywire and I have no clue what was going on half the time. I don't believe I have much else to say about this other than what I have already said for the mid-term exam. Though one thing I would like to add is that, I found it quite funny why a senior who is currently in Year 3 asked me for help for this examination. He dropped this course once, failed once, and thus had to take it in his third year. Anyway, I have a very annoying book report to finish before 23:59 tonight, and it is already 18:43 as of the writing of this right after the exam had finished. Actually, I had two essays due tonight, and fortunately I had to foresight to give up my sleeping schedules to squeeze time to finish it the previous day/night/twilight(?). But at any rate, I should get going.

### 13-12-2021
#### Calculus final
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> This was the most dreadful examination I have ever done in my entire life. It was pure misery. I studied quite a lot to be fair but I just can't seem to be able to quite to them. In a lot of the questions, I have a solid lead and solid idea of how I could tease the answer out off the question, but I just couldn't quite execute the calculation itself. And it's not like I didn't understand the theorems and tricks either. I feel like I was stuck in Mathematics in a way I have never been before. The paper wasn't quite structured in a way that one could wrestle some partial credit either. I just don't know. I don't think I have ever been this unconfident ever after an exam.

I guess writing is really a process of exploration and self-reflection, as I could clearly say as of the writing of this. Speaking of language, I find myself deteriorating in terms of vocabulary and general writing quality ever since I have been in university, both Chinese and English. Honestly, I found it extremely odd that this would be the case. Of all things, I would've thought the abundance of non-locals would help to make this environment more academically-oriented, and that English would play a more prominent role in the picture. But it seems that my SJC is somehow more internationalised than CUHK. I really need to get working on my language, lest they forever leave me and become a thing of the past, as proven in today's examination where I managed to forget how to write a lot of very common words. What a weird place I am in right now.

And with that, it would conclude this semester for me. I have had this nagging headache for the past two days and it seems that it just won't go away. I should be getting some actual rest.

#### End of Year 1 Semester 1
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> Honestly, a lot of things happened in this semester. I would say that this semester has had me progressed more than a whole year and more in secondary school. It had been a wide ride, from every aspect imaginable. The most recent and prominent one being the "zhong" stuff which apparently still hasn't concluded yet. I would say I have enjoyed this lifestyle really, and that's partly the reason why I haven't stepped out of CUHK for a whole one and a half month, no-joke. Academically speaking though, I don't think I am holding up too well. Despite there being course that I performed well in like ***Physics*** and ***Human Anatomy and Physiology***, there exist more courses well I didn't think I did too great in. They are all some stupid course like university core subjects and college general education. I honestly do not understand one singular bit why we have the number of courses that we do. I would really rather they give us more free credits to choose for ourselves. I honestly just find this whole system very counter-productive to the finest extent. The one thing I have as a takeaway is that I am not really that good in Calculus, all things considered. The fundamental stuff I can get no problem, even all the theorems I can understand easily, but I just cannot do the pattern recognition, recitation, number-crunching necessary to excel in. One way or another, I really need to get my shit together, since I'll be taking two other calculus courses in the next semester.

Either way, the dates for all the procedures have been planned. For the profile pictures, the majority has decided that suits and ties would be the dress code which I don't particularly fancy since I don't really like formal settings nor do I like to be pretentious which I find suits and ties to be. Either way, I'll have to buy a suit for one reason or another so I thought this would be a great time to do so. However, from what I've heard, each one costs at the very least $1200 which is just absurdity to the fourth degree. I cannot for the life of me look at the price tags without flinching. So this is definitely the one part I am not looking forward to. Speaking of profile pictures, we have created a new Instagram account and did the appropriate notice about "personnel changes" and whatnot, with much hiccups in terms of typos and confusion.

It was rather funny seeing how everything was made up on the spot. The utensils for the cake were stolen from the canteen nearby, the candles were replaced by the torchlight from a phone, we didn't even have plates at all so we just ended up spooning cake from the cake directly. I have literally never seen anyone eaten cake in this manner before.

#### HKDSE Report
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> I finally had the time or energy to review my report. And it ain't pretty.  
> First to lay out the status quo, I applied for remarking for Chinese, English, Liberal Studies, and Biology. It had successfully granted me a 5`*` in Biology, but that's the best part of it. This report has much more detailed score breakdown, and I have found out that 3 out of those 4 subjects I applied for remarking were not the right choice. I found out that I was 3 marks away in my Chemistry from 5`*`, 5 marks away in my English from 5`*`, 5 marks away in my Maths from 5`**`, 7 marks away in my Physics from 5`**`. It was basically unheard of that someone could make such ill decisions as to applied for remarking in the subjects that I did. Do you understand how much of a difference 3 marks can give? I could be studying Medicine right now for all I know. I don't believe any more ranting would be helpful anyway though. One thing I found funny is that after remarking, I apparently scored 19 marks less than what I initially had, which would have set me back to 4. Either way, this really showed how sporadic and unreliable the whole system actually is. The scores fluctuated a lot between markers and were just generally very inconsistent. I wonder how many students were just doomed by random chance and fated to become way less than they otherwise could've?

### 21-12-2021
#### Suit purchase
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> I have never been a fan of formal stuff, and it's not too hard to guess that I have never own nor worn a suit in my entire life. For some reason, they decided that our zhong profile pictures should be taken in suits and hence today Martin and I went out to *Mong Kok* to purchase suits in the *Hollywood Shopping Centre*. I don't know the first thing when it comes to suits so I was basically a clueless observer in this purchase. We tried on many different ones and eventually bought two that fits. I also got three ties of different colours just because. It turned out way more expensive than I have ever expected, $1250 for me, and ~$1500 for him since he also got a pair of shoes. It was a slim fit which I don't think I fancy too much but what do I know?  
> Anyway, when we got back to CUHK, Martin had just realised he never checked the shoes and upon that, he found out that the salesperson had given him the wrong pair. I mean wrong as in wrong model, wrong size, wrong style, wrong colour. It was basically as far off as you could get. After thorough rounds of ranting and complaining, he figured him going back to the shop to exchange them would be the only option, much to his disgruntle and dismay. So just like that, he wasted another 2 hours of transit just for that stupid mistake that wasn't even his. He didn't even ask the salesperson for a discount of refund or anything which I found rather un-opportunistic of him. I got to chill in his room and finish a movie within those 2 hours. What a profound waste of time!  

### 24-12-2021
#### Christmas party
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> There was a christmas party planned tonight with gift exchanges, hence I got out in the morning with Martin to buy some gifts. They proposed to exchange one regular gift, and another awful one. Not that I've ever heard it before, but I guess this is a thing.  
> I actually have bought the gifts already in a [gathering](#some-sort-of-gathering). I got a box of a dozen of macaroons, and a photo frame. The macaroons costed $20 each and I ended up spending $240 total, which was totally not within the budget of $100. I could've bought only half a dozen, but since there were 11 flavours, and that we would have 9 people in the party, I figured it would be best if I buy a full dozen. I thought of buying dog food, baby food, dollar sign shaped pasta, or even half pairs of socks, shoes, and mittens for the awful gift. But I figured the food items wouldn't really come across as too appropriate and the articles of clothing would be way too expensive. So I ended up buying a photo frame with the thought of putting a horrible meme in it. However, I think I instantly regretted this idea the instant I bought it.  
> Anyway, Martin hasn't bought anything yet so we went to a *Don Don Donki* store in *Tseun Wan West*, which I mistook for *Tseun Wan* and got off at the wrong station and ended up having to walk my way there for 15 minutes since taking the MTR again would take too long. Either way, he got a baguette and bottle of oil lotion from the 18+ section for the awful gift after my recommendation and I got a pair of bright red topless bikini from the same very section. Again, it was way over budge. I didn't think I realised how expensive they were, since I originally planned to get a full-on maid costume which was apparently priced at $300. He also got two boxes of fruit jelly for his actual gift which I honestly found odd.  
> Either way, we gathered in a party room booked in *Kwun Tong*. The room was quite insane, to be fair. There was a projector with karaoke, a large TV connected to a Nintendo Switch and a PS4, a full-sized poker type gambling table, a Mahjong table, a swing set, another swing set with cushions, a sofa, two large shark stuffed animals, and a ton of board games. It's exterior was really deceiving considering it was located in an industrial building. We played a bit of everything and had a lot of fun. One thing I'd like to note is that the Mahjong table was electronic which was rather inspiring. I looked away from one second and fully assembled rows odd pieces just appeared out of thin air. The main event was the gift exchange. We first exchanged the awful gifts. Someone got a literal tire for their gift and it beats me how that is even a thing. Turns out I was not the only one who thought to get articles of clothing since two other people also thought to buy a skirt and a dress as their gifts, but mine was ultimately the most flashy I'd say. I got a random notebook as my "awful gift" which I didn't find too awful but I'd love to not have to carry the tire home. For the good gifts though, I got an air humidifier, with was actually really nice, both functionally and aesthetically speaking. I gifted the macaroons and then tried some. They were so good, although I'm not sure they should cost $20 each. In the end, we played from 18:00 to 00:00. I and some people left for home while some of them went for a second round along the coast or something and apparently they kept on going after 07:20.  
> Honestly, I have no idea how to end this entry. I suppose I should give some reflections or whatnot but honestly, I can't really find anything too interesting to talk about other than it is my first time in an actual party-esque environment where I actually enjoyed myself. To be honest, I think I prefer sophisticated and impactful events over meaningless time-burning events such as this one. It's not that I didn't enjoy it while I was there, but just that I can't find much purpose to it other than the pure sake of the event itself.

<!-- 👣 Experiences -->

Two previous previous previous zhong members also joined us. It went on like normal for the most part. At the very end though, one of the previous previous granddaddy zhong member, Jack, started talking. Halfway through, one of our previous zhong members started having an argument with him. It ended with a small lecture in which he got the point across really well. Jack was a post-graduate and even he felt the need to come back here to intervene, which I found to be quite caring of him.
> After all that tension was over, they left. One of us found a message presumably left by her, and from what they had deciphered, she was tying to ease the tension and initiate some sort of open conversation. I was never really in too deep about the situation as I usually like to sit as far away from such interpersonal annoyance as physically possible, so I'm afraid I'm in no position or judge or comment.  

### 31-12-2021

> Somehow I am now basically carrying the entire zhong.

The photographer for the day was one of our shadow zhong members, and I'll tell you he is not a good photographer at all, not that he ever said he was. His framing, focus, and directing were all horrible. I have no idea why they got him to take our photos. I'm whining about this because I had to fix a lot of stuff in post-production, and his incompetence left me a lot of limitations in terms of how I could, or rather, how I couldn't, tinker with the photos.

Trust me, it goes on. I don't even think I can list all of them if I tried. Well, it's not all me who's working in this entire zhong. It's only me and Martin. This absurdity would go on and I am basically going mad with all the stuff I need to do. We stayed behind in the Computer Lab after the pre-consultation ended and worked on stuff until past 03:00. And by us working, I mean myself working while everyone else were doing god-knows-what. I had to pick up two entirely new software from scratch and had to make stuff with them all by myself. And if you've messed with anything Adobe-related, you'll know that their software are not the most beginner-friendly. This went on or an entire day. I woke up 10:00 today and had been working on stuff until 23:10. I have no clue what happened, nor how I became so loaded with work. I mean it had been my intention to keep my committent as little as possible, so I must've failed somewhere. I guess it's just that the perfectionist in me wouldn't allow stuff of subpar quality to come out. And since everyone else was careless or incompetent, I had to take on the role.  
> I don't know anymore. I guess I don't yet feel stressed(?), but I can't imagine this would still be the case when the semester break ends. Maybe I'll figure something out by then.

# 2022

## January - 2022

### 01-01-2022
#### 2022 new year
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
> Honestly, I have no clue what I should write in this entry. I don't really think an arbitrary date should define our perception of life. I can't see it being healthy to convince yourself that such a threshold exists, since it would just contribute to procrastination. I've never really set too much deadlines for myself, nor have I made plans with certain timeframes in mind since I never found them to be particularly productive. My mindset has always been to put your passion or interest into what you're doing. After all, you can't work productively if your passion isn't there. In terms of what I'd like to achieve though, I just wish to do well academically. The results of the first semester would be out on 06/01, so I guess I'll see if it's even remotely possible. I have been wanting to develop games ever since S1 I believe, possibly even earlier. So I guess that's one thing I would try to work towards, although I don't think it has much of a place over my academics. My YouTube is definitely another thing I wish to do more with, since it shouldn't really take off too much of my time, unlike game development. I guess we'll just have to wait and see.

### 05-01-2022
#### IKEA stroll
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> I got Martin to walk around in an IKEA with me. IKEA stores are surprisingly rare in Hong Kong, and the nearest one is already all the way over in *Tseun Wan*. Anyway, my goal there was to buy a blue shark plushie. They have been quite popular recently for whatever reason. It was honestly one of my first if not *the* first time I've been in an IKEA store. It has their infamous winding, maze-like, confusing layout. I guess the stuff IKEA sells is really not very noteworthy, except that their branding is quite consistent. Apparently they also sold many other plushies of basically every animal there is. So what I was looking for was apparently an old model blue shark, but despite there being numerous shark plushie "booths" throughout the entire store, we only managed to find the new models. Here's the deal with the new models: they're objectively inferior. Their bellies are mysteriously swollen for no reason, and it is rather aesthetically unpleasant. It basically made them have the silhouette of a pufferfish. After about an hour or so, we finally found the one old model shark after digging for so long. I also picked up a shark bag along with it just because. The shark itself costed $170, and the bag $20. After that, we decided to have lunch right there in the IKEA store, since as per their business model, any IKEA store must also consist of a cafeteria section. The food looked great, with quite affordable prices, too. We ended up ordering way too much since we wanted to try a little bit of everything. However, its food left a lot to be desired. Sure, the meatballs and mashed potatoes were good, but that's basically the end of it. The fries were soggy, lobster and shrimp soup tomato-y, blueberry cheesecake chemical-y, salad bitter, even the soda were too chemical-y to be any good. My conclusion is that a furniture store shouldn't try to go out of its league to be something it's not, especially when you suck ass at it.

#### Bank account
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> I finally opened a bank account. It was long due. I have been meaning to do it for the last year, for various different reasons. It was honestly less hassle than I thought would be. I guess my only experience with banks so far were the times when I would want for people to finish their business when I was a kid, and I'm telling you it took forever. Honestly I don't know what to talk about here. I guess I can note that I still don't really have a signature for. I mean I guess I do have a pretty simple one but I don't believe it would suffice(?). But everything is digitalised anyway so it's not like I would need to sign anything anyway, not that I would bother to show up physically even if I have to.

### 10-01-2022
#### Revisiting SJC with Marwin and Marcus
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
<!-- 👥 Relationships -->
> We had been trying to meet up for a while now. The school magazines were ready today and we just so happen to decide we can collect the magazines together and have a little rendezvous. It was a good thing that I obliged even though I was extremely busy this entire week since our zhong promotion period and consultation day is upcoming, since apparently they moved their flight forward so that it would be two days from now, on 12/01 instead of 26/01 as they had originally planned.  
> Anyway, we met up in the MTR station and started to walk to SJC. It had been a really long time since I last hiked up *Hong Kong Park*, even longer since I last met Marwin and Marcus. It was rather relaxing to tread a path I am so familiar to, with them, no less. I still remember we used to walk down to the MTR station every single day after school, although we stopped doing so for reasons I still don't quite know. Perhaps time drew us part, although I don't think this was the case. Either way, we got the magazines, and decided to meet up with Ms Ip. She was quite an interesting person. For me, she was the playful art teacher, who would always play into our little jokes and dumb stuff. Her lessons were really the one thing I can for sure say I hated no part of. For them, she was an inspiration, the one who had encouraged them to no end to pursue art. I believe she was the consultant for the many art competitions they had joined over the years.  
> I think I veered off-track.  
> So we left after a short while, without taking photos for some inexplicable reasons. There really wasn't too much going on, just that we chatted about everything. I wish we could've done more, but I was busy was my zhong stuff and had to get back to CUHK immediately after this, and they had to prepare and pack their stuff for take-off. Ultimately, as uneventful as it might have been, I think I was just grateful it happened.  

#### Dem beat: Conception
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
> They insisted that we must dem beat, not only for ourselves, but to show the previous zhong that we can do shit. Welp, apparently that turned out to be a hot pile of nonsense since we hadn't even conceived a beat at all before we were supposed to actually start today. Instead, we had to cancel it last-minute and push it back a day. Anyway, we started meeting at 19:00, and started to conceive and refine the beat. We had a lot of trouble refining the lyrics when half of them were just sitting there eating doing nothing at all. It was like another hour before we can actually start to practise. We went to the empty space at the podium next to the *Wen Lang Tang* in *Shaw College*. It was mostly more finalising the beat than actual practise. We got a few horrendous practise rounds in before Tom finally decided to show up. Due to time constraints, we made the executive decision that it would be impossible to practise all the verses, and decided to only do one of them. It was honestly rather terrible. After a while, some randos decided that right next to us would be a great place to set up shop and started eating hotpot. We were rather dumbfounded to be frank. Either way, we migrated to the third floor of the *Lee Shau Kee Building*, right outside the elevator. The place was quite echo-y and it gave an illusion of our non-existent power. The process was really quite un-noteworthy except that I can clearly tell some of them were not quite invested into this whole thing. We carried only until around 01:00 and decided whatever it would be the next day, it would be.

### 11-01-2022
#### Dem beat: Day 1
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
> It was at *Science Center L2*. Our audience was all year 1 students. We had to rush down there the moment the lecture ended and managed to start our whole thing before too many people had left. Honestly the power was lacking, and the soft carpet floor definitely wasn't helping. We were rather nervous but honestly it turned out alright, as alright as it could've been for 3 hours of practice. The synchronisation was terrible, and barely any of us yelled nearly loud enough. I would say it was unacceptable but to be fair I can't see it going too much better without some serious efforts.

### 12-01-2022
#### Farewell Marwin and Marcus
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
<!-- 👥 Relationships -->
> It was rather sad to see more people fly away. They booked a surprisingly early flight, much to our disgruntle. It was a 09:00 flight, and we had to basically arrive at 06:00. Right off the bat, I'll tell you this was way too early for a flight. I had to wake up at 05:30, and considering that I still have to dem beat and do all that jazz in the afternoon and at night, this was a rather undesirable start for the day.  
> Anyway, Ron, Timothy, and Andy also came to farewell them. They are going to fly to *Los Angeles, USA*, and settle there. But since COVID restriction or something like that, they'll have to first fly to *Tokyo, Japan* to then transit to their destination. As for the reason why they're going to the USA, they mentioned that their parents had been planning for this from the very moment they were born. Honestly, I don't believe I have ever heard someone plan something like this this long ago but I guess it's ultimately none of my business. They have relatives there, so I guess that's another factor. So we did all the usual stuff, taking photos and chatting. I got one of the luggage carts one would use to move luggages around in the airport and got them to sit on it. I pushed them around for a while and got some photos. I had been wanting to do that since the last time I've been to the airport but Toby refused for some godforsaken reason.  
> It wasn't long before they have to go through the gate. Apparently their mom is also going with them, which I didn't know was the case prior to the very moment she started to walk through the gate. They had like 8 suitcases full of stuff in total, hand-carry and not, among the 3 of them. I cannot fathom why or how one would need so much stuff considering Toby only had like 2 suitcases of stuff in total. They all got through the gate just fine except for Marcus, who got stuck for some reason like Toby did. Are they really that hard to operate? It was without too much fanfare though, probably because everyone was still half-asleep, but I don't really know.  
> I suppose here is where I should talk more about us. I've known them since S1, even though we weren't in the same class until S2. I still remember the first time we met was just outside the *Cheung Sha Wan* MTR exit after school one day. My dad was being overly socially expansive and greeted them for no reason other than that he recognised their SJC uniforms. Honestly I still do not understand how parents work since they just seem to chat up with the most random people for no reason at all. Despite this, we never were really that close until we were actually in the same class. Ron was also one of the catalysts since he was our common friend. The main reason I would say is 'cus of my plasticity. Come to think of it, I believe most the friends I made during my junior(/senior) secondary years were due to my plasticity. I'll have Toby to thank for that. One thing I'll note is that, I don't believe our conversations ever became more than mundane day-to-day stuff. I don't believe we have ever talked about topics too deep or specific. The most was academics or something. Maybe it's because most of our time spent was in the junior secondary years? I realise I'm making it sound like it was rather boring. I'm sure we had talked about non-mundane stuff, but whatever they were, it wasn't vivid enough to be the shining example of what our conversations tend to be like. As opposed to topics with Toby, I found them more sophisticated and in-depth, like sometimes thought-provoking or something. I'm making him sound like Plato or Socrates or some philosopher but it's true to some extent. It's weird to score and judge conversations like this. I'm not saying our friendship is shallow or anything, but it just... isn't the same(?) I should stop before I make it sound like some sort of novel about unacquired love.  
> I believe the rest of their family is going to fly there soon. It's not just studying overseas, I believe they are aiming for full-blown immigration. I guess I shouldn't be too surprised seeing that they have been talking about this openly for as long as we've known each other, but still it's quite unsettling. They are now going to study in a community college before making further plans. I'm not too sure about Marcus, but Marwin seems committed to work in Pixar eventually and said he was planning to studying computer animation or something similar. I shall wish they'd find their passion whatever they may eventually decide to pursue. I'm more worried than anything really, since the art market is quite hard to earn a living in, but I guess their talent shall carve them a path within this mist of uncertainty.

And since we came in from the only door, nobody managed to leave before we could start. I think we performed horribly, even worse than yesterday somehow. Some of the previous cabinet were also present and they found it quite satisfactory contrary to my thoughts. Apparently some of the previous previous cabinet were *also* present and they found it *not* amusing to have a beat dem'd was such low quality. Ultimately, whatever worked works. If our direct predecessors deemed it satisfactory then so be it. This entry is full of mindless rambling, as you might be able to see. My mind was really clouded since I had just farewell Marwin and Marcus this very morning and I have practically no energy left.

> | Introduction to Biomedical Engineering                                              |   1    | B+    |

> As you might be able to see, I performed quite well in all of the high credit courses. I actually attained scores within the A-range for all of the "expensive" courses. Turns out I made pretty decent predictions about these courses. However, apparently I decided to fail every single 1-credit course just because. The entire results of this is rather ridiculous since the harder the course was, the higher my grade had turned out to be. I literally have no comment about this at all, not that I know how to. The one thing I would say is that, in *Introduction to Biomedical Engineering*, I failed to attend for *one* of the lessons, and apparently that gave me a -10% penalty to the final score, which I believe accounts to 2 sub-grades. And coincidentally, this was the *only course* among these that counted to my honour GPA. I practically killed everything. If not accounting for all the 1-credit courses that I B-ranged, my GPA would have been 3.746. Looking forward, if I wish to go for internal transfer, I'd have to attain a cGPA of at least 3.75 across the two semesters, which means I'll have to get at least 3.844 GPA in the next semester with my 18 credit of courses. I don't believe it would be quite achievable to say the least. Why on earth would CUHK offer so many unrelated 1-credit courses??!?!?
