#### Zhong consultation day
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> It's finally the day we've been preparing so much for. I honestly wan't too worried about it, but I'm not sure about the others. However, we did catch wind yesternight that a lot of people are planning to make a scene at our consultation, so I can't say I'm looking forward too much about that. It would supposedly involve ~5 groups of people, each with a different stance, goal, and target to scold. I don't believe we would be the main target tough, but rather our previous zhong. We even prepared somewhat for actual fighting to ensue.  
> So either way, the event would start at 19:30 and last for 12 hours. We met up at the *BME Computer Lab* two hours prior to the event to print stuff, and by god, did we print *a lot* of stuff. The printer got jammed half way, and I kid you not, two of them worked on disassembling the entire machine to find out what the problem was. While they were exploring the wonders of engineering, the rest of us tried to making the older, shittier printer to work, to little avail. Eventually, they somehow managed to reassemble the jammed printer and made it work again miraculously. We carried on to print whatever we had to print. We tried to save money by printing multiple pages onto one, and in black and white. However, the printer took forever to print anything. Luckily, Kiwi, a staff who's somehow always around, offered to help us print everything in full scale, full colour, and even helped us staple everything together. I can definitely say that her contribution then and across various different occasions combined, had surpassed that of some of our own zhong members.  
> I left the computer lab early to carry all the printed stuff to the venue and to help the rest to set up the place. Kart decided to play the piano *for obvious reasons*. To be fair, he was pretty good at it; however, the dramatic pieces he was playing definitely didn't help with the tense atmosphere. Some other completely unrelated bystanders even offered to give us more chairs since apparently they had also caught wind about the groups of people who were going to show up. We bought something to eat, but didn't really get enough time to finish it.  
> So either way, the previous zhong arrived adn settled down. One thing I should mention is that, their P and IVP flew to somewhere else for an exchange program, so they couldn't be there, but instead opted to join in via a Zoom conference. At least now the most deadly serious person of the previous zhong is out of the question for the most part, I guess it would be easier. As we proceeded, the Zoom conference started to deteriorate, and they figured that Zoom just wouldn't work and ended the conference. I found it pretty amusing that it ended before either of those "elsewhere people" could ask anything, although they did supposedly sent some questions to be asked on their behalf through WhatsApp or something.  
> Pardon me but my sense of time was basically non-existent. After a certain unspecified amount of time, people started showing up. At first, it was just the previous previous zhong, but them more and more unrelated people showed up. The aforementioned Jack of course showed up along with the previous previous zhong, and started to ask us questions, although his tone was inexplicably calmer and leaned towards being more parental(?) than authoritative(?). Like, he wasn't being as judgemental as he was last time, but instead gave us advice and recommendations after pointing out our mistakes and shortcomings. Apparently, those other unrelated people I talked about were called in by our dearly P, Kirtus. Apparently, he thought it would be a good idea to call his friends and use them as a way to indirectly insult Jack, for reasons I still can't quite grasp. While the previous previous zhong was having a hot pot party at the back, those unrelated people started shooting questions our way. Well, all of the questions were directed to Kirtus himself, funnily enough. When asked after the event, apparently, they thought that by asking us(him) questions, it would somehow insult Jack in some way. I'll be the first to tell you that I didn't find this to be the case, and neither did Jack or anyone else. They asked questions for so long that at some point, everyone who were actually related to BME went outside of the venue for some break or something. Like, literally only us and those unrelated people were left in the venue. Other than this little interlude, everything was actually quite calm. I'm not sure where that wind came from, but no fighting was going to take place. I guess Kirtus did almost triggered a fight, but the people he brought was so incompetent that Jack didn't actually feel any aggression from them, and miraculously that was the only reason no fighting happened. Yeah, nothing made any sense.  
> Anyway, Jack and the other people left eventually, and we and the previous zhong were the only ones left. Supposedly, it should always ever only be these two parties present, as was the case in the consultations of literally every other zhong ever. This was a quite amusing turning point for the event. We were all starting to loosen up and we ended up basically chillaxing for the rest of the event. We took a generous amounts of breaks and got a lot of time to play around with the piano, some random football, another smaller random football, three hula hoops. Two of the previous zhong even went to sleep in some side room. Eventually, this whole event became a shit-fest, and the entire atmosphere somehow became more casual than the pre-pre-consultation from ages ago. It was around 01:00 that we decided to order food, which apparently wouldn't arrive until ~04:00. Basically, the second half of this were just them barely asking us any questions, just to kill time to wait for the food to arrive. From their conversations and jokes, they mentioned that our supposed previous zhong that didn't come to be were extremely incompetent. Allegedly, they denied a professor's request to use English because "the designated language is Chinese", they trashed the society room and threw everything out the corridor the very first day they got access. There were more stories that I don't think I remembered even half of them. Apparently that was the reason they never came to be, rather than the influence of our previous zhong. So that's one major knot of our relationship untied.  
> One thing to mentioned is that, we had literally 3 whole boxes full of random food and drinks gifted to us in the very beginning, and we managed to eat literally everything within such a short period of time. Eventually, the food arrived after three hours of mindless jokes and non-consultation. Someone in the previous zhong recommended that restaurant, but it was absolutely horrible. I wouldn't comment too much on the food, lest this become another food review. But the broth was weird, both briny and tasteless at the same time; the noodles were somewhat sour; the chicken was unseasoned.  
> We ended at 05:30 and left. To be fair, despite how chill it might seem, I felt like it was rather unsettling and unsatisfying to have such an anti-climatic ending to what we have worked for so long for, and I'm not alone in this. I guess ultimately the most laughable part was how we though there was going to be a fight but there wasn't, then we almost triggered a fight ourselves but didn't. Whatever will be will be, I guess. All that's left was the voting. We would need at least 1/3 of members to cast a vote, and at least 1/2 of those votes have to approve of our designation. But honestly, I have never heard any zhong failing to pass their voting session. The most we can fail at, would be to not have enough votes cast at all to make up that 1/3.

### 15-01-2022
#### Sleep paralysis
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> I'm not sure what was the cause, maybe I was too tired, or maybe I was just in a constant state of drifting in and out of consciousness as I usually do. I've heard and read numerous anecdotes about sleep paralysis and how they are very terrifying or something like that, but I can assure you that mine was nothing like it.  
> I was still sleeping from the consultation yesterday, and I tend to drift in and out of consciousness since I always feel like I should be doing something other than sleeping despite my body telling me otherwise. I should first lay out some background. I was sleeping in my hostel room, and it was a bunk bed with stairs leading up to it. The stairs would lead to where my feet is. I was sleeping on my side, facing the wall. I remember that the room was still dark. I thought I felt something near my leg. I opened my eyes, and saw something that my brain had conceptualised to be a humanoid figured made of tree roots (more on that later). It was rather interesting, since despite having my brain already conceptualised it being a root person, it was at the same time trying to figure out what it was. It was like trying to figure out what something is when you already know what it is. I thought that it could be one of my roommates, but then I thought they wouldn't be here at this point in time. Yes, that was my exact train of thought and logic. So then, I tried to turn my head towards it. I managed to actually see and confirm that it was indeed a root person. It was standing on the stairs, trying to reach me with its arms while leaning on my right leg. My mind was still quite clouded since I had barely woken up, but I remembered that I couldn't turn my head towards it despite trying to. It was quite a weird sensation, since I felt like I have physically turned my head, and my vision would confirm that for a slight bit, but then I would be in the same exact place I was in. I felt like I was turning my head that whole time I was trying to. It was something like those optical illusions where the object appears to be moving but not actually. I tried a couple more times before confirming that I indeed couldn't turn my head. It was this information that made me click. I figured that I was indeed in some sort of sleep paralysis limbo. I literally thought little of it and just turned my head back to where it was (physically/figuratively?) and closed my eyes to resume to my sleep.  
> I don't believe I have ever experienced sleep paralysis, and I would love to have experimented with it more, but honestly I was too tired at the time. One thing is that, I was in a weird state of lucidity and daze. It was like, I was in the state one would be in when they had just woken up, but at the same time weirdly logically and being able to think in a way that made sense. It's honestly quite impossible to explain. I distinctly remembered thinking that I should write about this experience in this journal. One speculation I would make is that perhaps it was because I had been trying to [lucid dream](#reality-and-dreams) before, and have done so with varying degrees of success. I would say that me trying to lucid dream would be the reason why I was kind of hyper-aware of myself as if I was an outsider to the point that I was able to figure out exactly what was happening. I also don't remember ever feeling like my breathing was restricted, as other sleep paralysis anecdotes would often suggest. I guess it would be because I was sleeping on my side, such that the weight of my ribcage didn't restrict my breathing. Also, I'm not really sure if one's eyes actually opened during sleep paralysis, since my experience could support either. On one hand, I distinctly remember that my vision turned towards the wall when I eventually decided to go back to sleep, which would imply that I had indeed looked at the root person prior; and I wasn't able to turned my head or visions to look directly at the creature, nor was I able to look anywhere else or have an out-of-body experience using "my mind's eye" as some anecdotes had suggested; both of which would suggest that my eyes had actually opened and moved around. But on the other hand, I don't remember myself blinking at all during that encounter, which would suggest my eyes hadn't actually opened. More research needed.  
> As to why a root person would be my nightmare of choice, I had watched a YouTube video about a horror game that featured that same root person as the antagonist right before my sleep. Nothing too interesting.

### 22-01-2022
#### Binge-writing
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
<!-- 💻 Personal projects -->
> I haven't had much time writing for the past weeks since they were the busiest weeks of a zhong. As such, they also felt much longer than any other. The past 7 entries, excluding this one, were all written only just now. I guess writing is kinda fun in the way that I can look into myself and really look into what my thoughts meant, and to reflect upon the tiniest details of my experiences that I will have otherwise overlooked. I guess binge writing like this also has an advantage, namely I can connect the dots and chain the entire story much better. However, it also kinda defeats the purpose of this journal as it was supposed to be a documentation of my *daily* thoughts, however disorganised or disjointed they may be. Another I would add is that, I have always had a weird obsession about typing, especially typing quickly. I find it somewhat satisfying and meditating. I guess this would be one of the reasons why everything I type on my computer tend to be really really long, whereas I cannot endure typing more than two sentences on my phone. Another thing would be it can somehow spark my vocabulary. For too much have I learned words and forgotten about them immediately after. I've found that so far throughout my journaling adventure, random words would just pop into my mind in random intervals, words that I somehow know existed but have never used. They would provoke me to look up definition after definition. This might be weird to talk about what writing shitposts brings you, but I guess everyone has a different something to get out of this. I'm not sure what Toby thinks his adventure had brought him, but I can see why he had recommended this.

#### Character introduction
<!-- 💻 Personal projects -->
> I don't know why, but I tend to dismiss the mentions of the names of the characters in my entries. Honestly, I have no idea why. Some characters I have divulges the names of, others I haven't. I guess it is because I don't believe a good story would need too much extra information. Come to think of it, I think my standards for this is whether they appear often in a story or a saga. I can't imagine many other people writing like this, since as far as I can tell, most books/movies/stories tend to introduce all the characters from the very get-go. I find them quite overwhelming, especially since I have a hard time remembering names. Ultimately, I guess I have chosen to slowly reveal each and every character for this reason or some other. Or not. Maybe I'm just uncomfortable about typing names for some reason. What even is this entry anyway?

## February - 2022
### 05-02-2022
#### Zhong hike trip
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> We had proposed to organise a hike trip for the freshmen next year, and today we went there to hike up ourselves to scout the trail. It was the *Dragon's Back* trail in *Shek O*. The trek was to start at 13:00, but some of us thought to get something to eat before that. We met up in the *Shau Kei Wan* MTR station at ~12:00. Martin insisted to buy a bottle of mineral water from the nearby supermarket since apparently he was obsessed over the taste of mineral water. We entertained his little water discovery journey while getting some snacks for ourselves before eating at a restaurant. After the meal, we waited for a very very long time outside the MTR station for the rest of them to arrive.  
> After a brief trip by bus, we finally arrived the starting point of the trail. The first thing we had noticed was how crowded it was. The majority of the first half consisted of shuffling around other people trying to make way for ourselves. There were also dogs for some reason. I can't imagine they enjoyed trekking up such a path too much seeing as how crooked the terrain was. The trail itself was honestly very disappointing. It mostly consisted of climbing stairs after stairs, which I consider to be far worse than simple slopes. The path was dug into the greenery and was very narrow. With only most dead shrubs and bushes lining the path, scenery was non-existent. It was very uneventful until we got to the very top of the mountain, which mind you, was off the intended trail. It was surprisingly windy at the top. Some of us climbed atop some rock formations and that was basically it. We kept hiking alone the trail and stopped occasionally for sightseeing or breaks. When we thought we have reached the very end of the trail, we realised we have somehow gone in the wrong path, despite there being no forks at all the entire way. Anyhow, we kept going and the dead bushes gave way to lush greens and trees. Honestly, this wrong path is somehow way more enjoyable than the correct path. I have no clue why who chose that original path chose that original path.  
> We finished the hike at ~16:00, and took a bus to *Shek O* for lunch/tea. I have to quickly rant about that shitty cafe which charged 20% service charge for god-knows-why, much to our disgruntle. We walked around the nearby residential around, for some reason, then finally decided to head to the beach. There were a bunch of rock-climbing fanatics pondering how to conquer a random pillar of rock, which tickled Martin's fancy and he almost jumped down there to partake, though he eventually decided against it, much to our disappointment. We crossed the *Lovers bridge* and someone proposed to skip stones. We spent quite a while there, until we realise a whole bunch of other randos have following our suit, with one guy throwing huge rocks into the water for some reason. We left and climbed up on top of a huge rock for a photo. Some of them kept trying to take pictures of waves and wouldn't leave. We ended up spending as much time at the beach as the hike itself and only left at ~19:00.

### 12-02-2022
#### Last day in hostel
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
> The university had announced that all lessons in semester 2 will be held online and that everyone will have to check-out of their hostels permanently before tomorrow. So I guess this is the very last entry I will be writing in my hostel room.  
> Where do I start? It is such a shame. Excluding the mishaps that I had in my first hostel, I have only been living here for less than 4 months. I checked in on 04/10, and will check out tonight, so it should officially be 132 days to be exact. But with holidays and semester breaks and stuff, my rough estimate would be that I have lived here for only around 80 days maximum. I haven't even started packing yet and it's already 19:44 as of this very sentence. I guess its quite dreadful really. Although it's not like living in the hostel is anything irreplaceably good especially since it's all online classes now, but just that losing it would be so much more devastating than not having it in the first place. I honestly don't believe I have experienced loss as impactful before. This should be on par with graduating from SJC if I had to rate it, despite having spent obviously way less time here than in SJC. It's not quite loss as in mourning the death of a loved one, but rather just a general emptiness that I have. I guess it's mostly because how sudden all of this is. They only announced it this Monday afternoon (07/02), and this is already the last day. There's no build-up, there's no anticipation, and most importantly, there's no ending.  
> I came back here as soon as I heard the news. And the first thing I've noticed was the schedule calendar for all the hostel festival events was posted on the elevator wall, starting next week. I think that's the moment that hit me. How much have we lost because of this? Who is to say other than it's "too much". One of the events are the photo-shooting for the entire hostel. We didn't even have to chance to do that before we all got booted. I've mentioned that dramatic events like these take a while to sink in for me, but I think this one had sunken itself quicker and deeper than anything else had. There's too much to talk about and too little time. I'll probably follow up on this after I'm done moving everything. I should start packing now.

## March - 2022
### 03-03-2022
#### Multivariable Calculus midterm
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> To be fair, I did not attend a single lecture of this course. I just started revising yesterday and it somehow seem to have worked for me, in this exam at least. Honestly, I didn't find it particularly challenging. Partly credited to this exam being open-book, but I guess the one exercise that I've semi-done yesternight also helped somewhat.  
> As for the reason why I hadn't been attending lectures: the lecturer sucks ass. I shall now take liberal time to rant about him. His notes are horrendous and incomplete. I would go as far as, if not further than, to say that they are the worst notes I have ever seen in my entire life. Entire examples and theorems can be missing from the notes, since apparently he would like us all to attend his lectures where he goes through the curriculum more slowly than a beginner with absolutely no knowledge in the topic at all. I'm glad we have a feedback questionnaire at the end of each semester cus you bet I'm going to report his ass with his incomplete notes. I have basically dropped this lecturer entirely. For my revision, I have been using notes from another lecturer, whose notes are extremely professional and quality. Apparently, this is only his side job too. He mainly teaches secondary school maths in tutor centers, so I guess this would be where the format, layout, and flow of this notes are from.

### 08-03-2022
#### Logic midterm
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> The exam was honestly much harder than I had thought it would be, although it's definitely still doable. I honestly though the allocated time was too adequate for a whole bunch of MC questions, however, it turns out I have barely enough time to go through all of them. I had to foresight to compile a cheat sheet in this already open-book exam, which definitely cut down the time I had to take going through the lecture slides. To be honest, I was quasi-attending the lectures, as in, I would attend but put the lecture in the background. I was still able to get the most important points of each lectures though (somewhat).

#### Human Anatomy and Physiology 2 CA1
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> First and foremost, I admit that this is completely my fault. In the previous semester, it took me a whole weekend to study for this, but I only had ~6 hours for this semester. I had to churn out two long essays the previous week. They both required tremendous amounts of thought, planning, research, rewrites and whatnot. I completely underestimated the time they would take. I planned to finish one of those in the week prior to the previous week, but it proved infeasible and it bled into the previous week, which made me start the other one late, which ate my entire weekend. In combination with all the other exams I have to study for, I literally have no time to study for this exam.  
> I ended up sleeping for 2 hours then woke up at 02:00 to start studying. I was miraculously able to chow down an entire semester of lecture and successfully went through everything at least once while making notes, before my lectures started at 08:30. Despite this, I obviously couldn't get too familiarised with the curriculum, which I absolutely had to for this course. Surprisingly, I did all right in the closed-book exam, but I ended up falling for some simple traps and details that I would've known about had I gone through the syllabus multiple times. I guess I was glad that exams for this course didn't require you to understand the subject completely since it is arguably leans not too much on the logic side of things.

### 11-03-2022
#### Linear Algebra midterm
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> I had the displeasure to be taught by the same ass lecturer again, and suffice to say, I once again didn't attend any of the lectures again. However, that other good lecturer doesn't teach this course so I was basically on my own with only the help of Martin's notes. I spent some time whipping up a cheat sheet since this is another closed-book exam (for some reason). This course basically only concerns mostly secondary school level M2 stuff, although much more meticulous and tricky. To be fair, I had no problem with the "difficult" parts, but got stuck in simple algebra. I would say I have never done a worse paper in since secondary school. Let's hope I didn't do too badly that I would have a chance to catch up in my final examination.

## April - 2022
### 09-04-2022
#### CUHK Camping trip
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> I guess this was a rather logical continuation for the trends of our events. We have been discussing about having a legitimate "wilderness" camping trip in the UK for our graduation trip thing, which did not happen sadly, due to border lockdowns. And then there was a failed hiking attempt, which is also very sad and uncalled for. Anyway, the idea came when I shared myself having seen tons of stars in CUHK. I suggested that they would come and watch the stars together, since Samuel was suddenly very fond of watching stars for some reason. I proposed us to set up a tent in CUHK for the night.  
> We didn't have a tent, so in the afternoon before the main event, we went to *Decathlon* to buy one after eating a hotpot buffet. Tents were surprisingly expensive, honestly much higher than I had anticipated. To be fair, they wanted to get a cheaper one, but I have never been the kind of person who'd be fine with compromising quality over price. Additionally, I wanted to be able to reuse it for our upcoming Orientation Camp so I thought we could get some of our money back. After a whole lot of convincing, we ended up settling on one for $999, which mind you, was only the third cheapest option. We got some lights, pillows, and headed to CUHK.  
> We put the stuff in my society room except it was locked and I still don't have the key for some ungodly reason so we actually just put them in the corridor. I had an idea for a tent spot but we went scouting anyway while I was doing a bad job at giving them some sort of tour. My initial idea was to camp right in the middle of the fucking road, literally. From months of experience, I found that right in the middle of *The University Mall* (which is a walkway and not a mall in the conventional way of using the word 'mall'). However, there were a lot of people despite physical lessons before cancelled entirely. We were mainly scouting for grassy areas since sitting on concrete doesn't exactly scream comfort.  
> It got dark. We brought some snacks from the supermarket and sat on the stairs of the mall-road to watch the stars. I think we saw ~15 stars, maybe more. They were quite surprised. Honestly, I think they believed I was only exaggerating the star visibility. Either way, the skies were nice despite the moon cycle not being optimal. I managed to take a decent picture of the stars with a long shutter speed. We thought it was time to set up the tent after some photos, however, there are still quite a bit of people around since it was only ~23:00, and the place wouldn't be free of people until past ~03:00 from my experience. We scouted further on the rooftop of the *Lady Shaw Building* since it was close enough to the "optimal" spot and there is a nice patch of grass, but there was this annoyingly bright purple LED strip for some reason which absolutely killed visibility. Anyway, we ended up deciding to set up the tent on the rooftop of the *William MW Mong Engineering Building*, which is quite convenient really since my society room is on the highest floor. However, we scouted the rooftop when there was still light, and it turns out that despite being much darker, the sky visibility was much worse than in the road. Also the ventilation units there were very noisy. To give you a perspective, you literally cannot see your hands at all; it was so dark that we actually had to take out our torches to even walk even though it was only ~21:00.  
> We set up the tent anyway even though it wasn't the perfect location. As far as I'm concerned, everything before this point was merely the appetizer. This is the main course of the entire day, since it took so long and so much effort to set up the tent. First of all, it was dark as I've mentioned, we bought one LED light from *Decathlon*, Samuel had a head-mounted light, and we had the torches on our phones. Those were absolutely inadequate for what we were trying to do. We basically had to do this entire setup blind, and none of us had any experience before. Secondly, the design of the tent is highly unconventional. There were two pieces of large nylon fabric with a whole bunch of mounting and connection points. I myself had never seen such design, and I thought they were supposed to be the left and right side of the tent. We weren't sure about the topology of the tent so I proposed it would be easier if we unfold the entire thing and reduce it to a 2-dimensional problem. So it took us a while to disconnected all the things to fully separate the two pieces which took us quite a while since the connections are quite strong. We fumbled with it for ~40 minutes to no avail. I discovered there was an instruction manual, or rather, instructions on a small piece of tag on the tent bag. They consisted of two vague artistic representation illustrations of the tent that didn't tell you anything about the assembly process. They also started watching YouTube tutorials about it but needless to say, that wasn't of much help either. At the end, Efren and I figured the ordeal out. The tent was actually double-layered. A piece of fabric was the outer shell of the tent while the other one is the entire interior. That was completely not unintuitive at all. Another thing is, you had to spend so much time under the fabric to set up the connections where it was so hot. We ended up taking a total of ~1 hour to set the thing up.  
> So we finally finished the setup at ~22:00. We hooked the LED light on the ceiling of the tent, and surprisingly it was of a decent brightness. Although, considering the rooftop floor was pure rough concrete, you could imagine it wasn't very comfortable to sit even with the padding of one thin nylon fabric. To be fair, I foresaw this and bought a pillow to sit on, but I ultimately failed to convince them to buy a floor mat thing back at *Decathlon*. Anyway, I managed to gain access to the society room and we got a lap table thing, some games and pillows up there. Stars were quite non-existent up there, at least not as much compared to at the mall-road, and all the photos we took up there couldn't top the original ones at all. We ended up playing games until ~01:30 before we decided to walk more around the campus. I thought we could get some lovely hot chocolate from the library but apparently the 24-hour section closed due to pandemic regulations, which is something I don't think I've ever heard of before. Disappointment aside, there were still some people walking along the mall-road. To be fair, I was really fond of the idea of setting up tent in the middle of the fucking road, although I knew we would have to have waited for an extra 5-6 hours. Anyway, I led guided them through some infamously dark semi-hike tracts around the campus (CUHK is just really dark in general for some reason) since I thought it would make an interesting experience. However, to much of my dismay, they have taken the chance to install a lot of extra lighting fixtures all around the place. I can't say I enjoyed these installations too much since I've always thought walking in the darkness was quite tranquillising. There were still some dark staircases here and there but it was nothing compared to what it used to be. Anyway, we headed to *Lake Ad Excellentiam* and it was fortunately still pitch black. In the pitch darkness, I somehow managed not to find the pavilion despite all walkways leading there. Much to out surprise, we managed to see fireflies. They were quite sparsely distributed among the general area, and they weren't as bright as I thought they would be, although it was still quite surreal to witness. I don't believe I have seen a firefly before either (probably untrue?). We tried but sadly none of us managed to get a picture of them. After that, we sat on the benches on the semi-rooftop of the *Yasumoto International Academic Park* and chatted for an hour or so.  
> We ended up headed back to tent at ~04:30. We cleaned (Samuel snapped the table in half during the ruckus somehow?), before CNok and I got to sleep while Efren and Samuel decided to do whatever. We managed to get ~1 hour of sleep before we woke up at ~05:40 to see the sunrise. Initially, we were going to see the sunset but the bearings couldn't align; but I digress. We sprung up and took some good photos of it. Sunrises are surprisingly bright, much more than I had imagined. I thought they would be around the same brightness as sunset, which, to be fair, I don't know why they aren't. That sunrise ended up being somewhat generic, lacklustre even. It didn't paint the sky crazy colours, barely even orange actually. No clue why. At least the pictures turned out alright I guess. The temperature fluctuations were quite drastic, and there were a lot of condensation everywhere. Everything was soaked, as if it had been raining the whole time. We had to lay everything out to dry them in the sun. We left everything like that and went to grab breakfast. The *Maxim* place was jam-packed for some reason so we ate at the rooftop bench place from the night before. We packed everything up and left the tent at the society room and called it a day.  
> This entire thing was both more and less than what I had initially expected. I thought it was going to be a star-watching thing, but that only lasted ~45 minutes. I thought we were going to set up tent either in the middle of the fucking road or on a grass patch, but of course we chose the least comfortable location possible to do so. I thought we would have the time to walk around the entire mountain, but time only allowed us to walk around the front half. I guess I also never expected to be able to do everything we set up to do. I'm still very much fond of the UK camping trip though. And now that Toby is in the UK, I figured that could be some sort of backup plan in case things go off-plan (which they most likely will to be honest). But for now, I guess this is one thing half crossed out in the list of *"Things to do before we fall victim to the eventual and inevitable death and perish"*.

### 14-04-2022
#### Inevitable reoccurring hiatuses
<!-- 💭 Philosophy -->
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
<!-- 🌞 Well-being -->
<!-- 💻 Personal projects -->
> I realise it has been well over a month since the last entry (discounting the last entry which was retroactively written), and its not like there isn't anything to talk about, just that I found myself in that sort of mindset again. It seems to be very much reoccurring, every two three months or so. It is basically this sort of dread or sudden flood of morbidity. It's like the first time someone has discovered their own mortality. As usual, my words cannot convey nearly as much power as these thoughts/realisations entail.  
> The trigger is basically anything and everything, though this time in particular, it was from a minibus ride. I was riding for my first time in a long long while. I used to ride the minibus daily, with my brother. I suddenly remembered when we used to play dumb games during the ride, as kids do, and my attention drifted towards how fast we'd pick up on each other's games: the rules, the gimmicks. No matter how utterly ridiculous or nonsensical they may be, it would be take only minutes before we would understand what the other was trying to do. It is weird to describe, not that my language abilities are helping, but to illustrate, it was like if we were randomly dropped into the most whimsical game shows, we would be able to grasp the gist and the rules of the game very quickly on-the-fly. Maybe this experience is very common, maybe not, who knows. But that let me to suddenly noticing how much my brain has deteriorated since then. It's like I can still rather vivid remember how hypersensitive my brain and senses were versus what they have now become. I can remember my pattern recognition abilities, correlation abilities, comprehensive abilities, and so on. It filled me with dread to realise that my peak potential has passed already. It is literally scientifically proven that you can only go downhill from there. It honestly is some sort of cosmic joke. The time when you have the most potential is exactly when you have no idea how to use it.  
> As is usual for morbid and philosophical subjects, I have semi-discussed this with Toby, for more times than I can remember. He mentioned the trade-off between mental capacity and memory accumulation, and how our potential is never reachable without knowledge. I guess it is still somewhat understandable, since you will most likely have to trade off mental flexibility for stability, and it would be my speculation that mental stability is what made adults differ from children. I feel like this drifted off-topic somewhat. The thing I was trying to say is that we will never reach our potential potential. The ceiling to our potential capabilities can be very very much higher. (Side-note: The movie *Limitless* explored something within the same realm). It's not like I care about veering off-track anymore so let's go with it for the time being.  
> Getting back on track, another reoccurring thought would be the realisation that we really don't have too much free time in our lives to do whatever we would like to. Ever since S6, I believe, we've had a list of *"Things to do before we fall victim to the eventual and inevitable death and perish"*, and so far we have ever only done one single thing. It sounds grim, and it is, truly. Time is really very much like our mental capabilities. You can never get it back after you've lost it, and in every second in your life ever, you have done nothing but losing them. Yes, your brain technically doesn't grow to its theoretical maximum potential until after infancy, but genetics also play a big role in that too, so the argument still stands.  
> This entry is very much jumbled and disorganised, much like how I would be every time these sorts of ideas would dominate. I would lose the passion or energy to do literally anything at all. For a whole month, I have barely touched anything, not my academics, not my passion projects, not everything. All I have done is burning time, the very thing that I'm lacking. I'm not sure if I've talked about similar stuff before but I feel like I can finally attribute this to my perfectionism. I have talked about this with CNok in at least two separate occasions. I figured that I really only am ever satisfied with everything going according to plan, perfection. Anything that I am unsure about, I would genuinely rather not do at all. This contributes greatly to my procrastination, as you might have been able to figure. It is only until recently that I have realised this not only manifests in my tasks, my also in my life. I believe the countless times I feel like I lack the energy to do anything, is actually because I am suffering such unproductively vicious mental loops. It would drive me to sleep through days at a time, inducing massive hiatuses in my workflow. I'm not sure if this has always been a thing in secondary school, but I recalled having consciously realised this in my university years. I sleep for way longer. I'd say ~50% longer in general per day compared to my secondary school years. This may be due to me having to manage my own life and daily routines a lot more. I would assume this would cause the perfectionism thingy to kick in way more often and in more aspects.  
> A tangentially related thing is that I believe I have aged quite significantly this year. Apart from the sleep thing, I get tired a lot more easily. Although I would say me peak productivity have somewhat increased overall, I can't say that they would be sufficient to make up the increased downtime that I would have to take in-between productivity sessions. My brain moves substantially slower, as mentioned above, and I've gotten a lot *lot* more forgetful. My vigour and passion dipped. I feel like this is somewhat about ageing, since I've read that your body ages a lot more in certain years of your life instead of a steady decline. This may be one of those years. I may also be worrying more about various things. I genuinely have little clue.  
> Yes. No conclusion, no outlook, and no cue for the end of the entry.

I was stuck on the simplest algebraic calculations, even on ones that doesn't involve any high-level mathematics at all. I genuinely have no idea why that was the case, but I guess my mathematics senses have left me, at least the fundamental mathematics senses.

I guess it had somewhat achieved this goal, but I can't say I'm too certain about it. I guess we'll have to wait for its final examination.  
> Another thing, due to the [hiatus and burnout thing](#inevitable-reoccurring-hiatuses), I didn't manage to write these as separate entries as I had last semester. TO be frank, I didn't even check my grades at all despite them being out for more than a month already. I guess this point of me documenting these in the first place was to allow myself time to think and reflect, or was it? No idea. I should stop rambling before my words stop making the slightest hint of sense.

Either way, I should have a grand total of ~2 days to study for this after submitting the papers. However, you guessed it, I didn't have the slightest chance to get myself out of the burnout that started like 2 months ago since there has been nothing but tests, assignments, presentations, and papers. Not to mention that I had little sleep in the past 2 weeks focusing on the papers (do you know how long researching takes? *jesus fucking christ*) and prior tests.

I don't believe even I got distracted by anything at all either. This should typically get me into studying and hard focus mode rather effectively. However, nothing clicked in my brain. I would estimate I had only around 16 hours left when I started going through the slides at a reasonable rate (i.e. *not 5 slides per day*). Keep in mind, that since both of my previous times revising this material was quite rushed, I didn't have time to consolidate anything. Practically nothing was committed into my long-term memory, so I basically had to re-learn the entire syllabus. I was profoundly tired, but I stayed up all night and "finished" going through the material *barely*. I had to take time to jump around in my room and in the living room so as to regain my focus and concentration. I even turned to caffeinated energy drinks around 3 hours prior to the exam. They didn't even do much other than raise my heart rate.

To be fair, I don't believe I'm even knowledgable enough about the material to gauge my performance, so I don't suppose I should. Not satisfactory though, that's for sure.
