### 05-05-2022
#### Logic final
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> This entire course is really quite enjoyable despite me not having attend a single lesson. She just talks too slowly, what more can I say? I found that university lecturers suck at time management, in that they very much like to teach the very complex topics in the same amount of time they used for the very easy topics. I've already [written once](#lecture-time-allocations) about this phenomenon, and this just further proves my point. But I digress.  
> I spend a day self-learning the material from lecture slides, making my own notes. Honestly, I found a large majority of the exam pretty easy, with the only exception being the aforementioned very complex topic: *natural deduction*. I'd say the concept itself is not too hard to understand, but from the lecture slides and the few lecture recordings that she had put up, I found that she had missed some very key concepts that are vital to actually grasping and answering these types of questions. Natural deduction is basically like proofs in mathematics, in that you are given >1 premises statements in the form of logical operators and such, and from those, you'll have to transform them into the given conclusion statement, also in the form of logical jargon, using a set of identities. While the identities themselves are not hard to understand, and frankly, I don't think the correct way of tackling such questions is to understand those identities anyway, and what you had to do to derive the conclusion is easy to wrap your head around, the complexity of this entire ordeal grows exponentially as the statements get more and more complex. I'm genuinely unsure if there is an actual method to actually compute them but I can assure you that they are definitely not trivial to do despite the easy examples in textbooks and lecture slides coercing you to believe otherwise. While I was able to complete some steps and push the problem in the correct general direction, I ultimately couldn't finish any of the three questions of this sort to completion. They didn't account for too many points so it's not like I was too sad about this but I'd say this is quite a shame to not be able to complete them despite the goal seemingly within the reaches of my fingertips. I can't say the entire exam in general is too hard, since we were allowed to use as many tools to help us as we please, although the effectiveness of those "tools" are rather non-existent. All in all, I'd say I did passably. Perhaps I may even dive deeper into such topics in my own time.

### 06-05-2022
#### Year 1 concluded
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> Time flies. I couldn't even believe it has already been a year, cus' it sure doesn't feel like it. It is definitely a shame getting kicked out from hostels and not being able to study in-campus, although I'd say thankfully I still got to experience it before the policies even if it was for shorter than I thought I would be able to. I can still remember how rushed this lockdown announcement was made and how little time all of us had to react. But with this aside, I figured it would be appropriate to go through this entire year in a somewhat chronological order. This is not meant to be a comprehensive summary or all the CUHK-related stuff, but rather only the stuff that came to mind when I'm writing this. This might be a good practice depending on how you look at it.  
> I believe the biggest and most memorable event for me so far is definitely the orientation stuff despite my dumb self having missed a whole bunch since apparently I was under a rock in the first few weeks. I guess the first major event has to be this. The orientation day in particular held quite a dear place in my heart. It was my very first introduction of CUHK, its campus, its people, and whatnot. I'd say this is what pushed me to join "zhong" later down the road. This sounds very cringey but I felt it was important to recreate this sense of wonderment and guidance to those after me (This made me sound very old). Although there was a very major roadblock/barrier/setback in the form of a sort of internal conflict zhong war *(**Zhong war saga**: [1](#zhong-war-begins), [2](#zhong-war-ends), [3](#zhong-new-beginnings))*. It had been rather emotional at times, although it still worked out okay-ish at the end. Honestly, I would say this might be an overall positive for the entire zhong, and in correlation, for those we serve, since it made a more compact team. I'm a strong believer of small teams being better than large teams. This purge somehow is good for productivity, partly attributed to us being more aware of related problems. Despite this, I definitely cannot say we are working perfectly together as a team, although I don't think it would be healthy to start pointing fingers; however, I would say that the workload in this is distributed very unevenly from the very beginning, before or after the "reformation". As for the zhong activities, however, they are most certainly lacking due to the pandemic policies and stuff. Everything is cancelled with little saving grace to note of. I still hold true to my initial reason for joining this society though, since I really do not believe an experience as important as orientation should ever be compromised. Such can really leave a permanent regretful hole unfilled, as I have found time and time again.  
> In chronological order, there was actually one more thing right before the zhong stuff: the hostel thing *(**The hostel thing saga**: [1](#checking-in-to-my-new-hostel), [2](#preparing-my-new-hostel), [3](#checking-in-to-my-new-hostel))*. I said I might talk about it later, but honestly, I'm not feeling I should dwell on it anyway. It's not like its shameful or traumatic or whatnot, just that it's in a way rather cringey. I think it might be of my best interest to just forget about it entirely, or something like that. Again, perhaps I might talk about later or something. Who knows.  
> On the topic of hostels, I genuinely am not too terribly connected to my own hostel. I'd say I'm more connected to the people in Martin's hostel more than in my own. This is partly by choice, I suppose, since I'd very much like to keep to my own bubble without external distractions. I've heard enough to learn not to mingle too well with my hostel-mates. This sounds very weird but I really think there is merit in practice. Either way, I have spent a significantly of my time in Martin's hostel. And yes, it is highly illegal and against the university policy, but this policy is rarely enforced in *Shaw College* anyway. I guess the main appeal of hostels for me is still the elimination for transit. Waking up only 20 minutes before a class is blissful. Additionally, the shuttle bus system in CUHK is so good(adequate) that it is convenient to do everything in-campus anyway. There are also nice canteens/restaurants so it's quite liveable. In fact, I spent roughly ~50 days not stepping a single foot outside CUHK during my [semester 1 finals period](#finals-approach).  
> Academically speaking though, I would say it has been somewhat satisfactory in semester 1, but I'm not too sure about this semester. I'm definitely still going to try and apply or internal transfer, but I don't suppose I can qualify. I guess I figured before that chances are I couldn't get a year 1 transfer anyway. Actually, my first year hasn't actually officially concluded, since I still have a summer semester to go where we'll be mandated to take a *Summer Practical Training* course. Apparently we'll get to actually go do stuff in a hospital, so let's see how that goes.  
> > ***Post-script***:  
> > As mentioned, this is not a complete yearly summary, but rather only a summary of the CUHK-related stuff. For yearly summaries, I thought it would be appropriate to do them every 27/09, seeing that it was the day Toby finally got me to start [the very first entry](#starting-this-journal).

### 22-05-2022
#### Lab exposure programme 1
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> As you might be able to tell from its name, the lab exposure is basically us being exposed to a lab environment. I should first give some background information about what this programme even is. There were 11 supervisors that we can choose to follow, all with their respective research areas. We had to make a priority list for our preferences (which, if you didn't know, I absolutely despise from various past experiences). I believe it was assigned to us based on academic achievements and grades since they also required us to submit a CV alongside the application form. Anyway, I was assigned to my first choice, and my supervisor was the department's chairman. To be fair, that was also partly the reason I put him as my first choice since I thought he would have considerably more resources at his disposal. He has three research areas: soft robotics for rehabilitation, Kinect AR rehabilitation system, and brain research EEG MRI. Honestly, the scheme was so poorly introduced to us that I didn't even know we have to/ could choose from the research areas. We just thought all 3 were in the same package. So I chose the brain research EEG MRI.  
> Some post-graduates in his team acted as my correspondence and added me to a group chat. I should first tell you that for this supervisor, he has provided 8 positions for us. You could imagine how surprised I was when I found out that the group chat has only myself and my correspondences. It wouldn't make much sense to create separate group chats for each student, since they also said that all arrangements will be made in the group chat. Maybe the brain research thing was just very niche(?) although I highly doubt it. I told Martin about the absurdity of this. He also chose the exact same thing as him, but he said no one has replied to his emails so far. Long story short, he was shortly added to the same group chat so at least it would be half as silent/awkward(?).  
> The correspondences told us there would be an EEG experiment today and invited us to observe. I had little expectation going into this since, as I've mentioned, we were barely given any introduction prior. I arrived at ~11:00. The lab was rather quaint, if I might comment. It was located in my department's floor of the building, and I have walked past it quite a few times without batting an eye. Well I have taken the time to notice that the were using Linux but that was as much interest as I have given it before. It was rather small and crowded. It was mainly separated into two rooms. The entrance gives way to the "control room" with some computers and stuff. It was connected to a small toilet-looking area with no toilet weirdly enough. Then there were two thick doors, comparable to those seen outside of MRI rooms. Probably filled with lead or something, although weirdly enough there was a window on the door for some reason. They were in serial, mind you, not side-by-side, so it was quite apparent that they were trying to block radiation of sorts; but again the window just completely baffles me since it defeats their entire purpose. Behind the doors was a room lightly padded with sound-proof lining. There were quite a lot of prototype machines, gadgets, and whatnot.  
> The associates gave us some brief introduction of what they'll be doing, namely measuring the brain waves of a stroke recovery patient while she is doing tasks. Not long after, said old lady arrived alongside her caretaker/daughter(?). She was seated in that experiment room where a probe-filled headgear was put onto her. The associates then proceeded to inject a gel in-between the headgear and her head with syringes. The probes will be measuring her minute brain voltages so the gel is quite important as they minimises the resistances given by the air gap. The way they apply the gel is quite a sight to behold though. There were holes in the headgear for this exact purpose, but apparently the gel couldn't spread well enough on its own so they had to wriggle the syringe in all sorts of directions to spread. It genuinely looked a lot like they were performing minimally invasive brain surgery on her. The whole I was just thinking about the bare metal not-non-sharp point of the syringes scraping against her scalp. As this ritual is taking place, we could see the computer indicating the resistances was reaching acceptable levels with a map of the probes lighting up sequentially.  
> That whole process took ~45 minutes. An associate came out and briefly talked about what they will be doing next. He said apparently the hugely thick doors are to block stray radiation and signals from the outside world since the equipment was very prone to external disturbances. He then closed the two aforementioned hugely thick doors and went back into the room. The experiment then began. They were measuring her brain signals while she was doing motor tasks. We were just asked to sit and wait outside. The experiment went on for a very long time. Martin eventually got tired of it and went to fetch his laptop to work on an assignment. After ~10 minutes, an associate came out and chatted with us about various things. He showed us some MRI images and models and we discussed about the contemporary challenges and future research directions. Somewhere along the line Martin just straight up fell asleep. We kept on chatting for ~15 minutes before he went back into the room. Martin then proceeded to finish the rest of the assignment while we kept waiting. The entire experiment lasted for around an hour. The old lady was escorted out of the room. Her hair was soaked in the gel. And now finally the pieces were put together: the toilet area was so that she could wash her hair. That still has to be the most ridiculous infrastructure I would imagine seeing in a laboratory environment. They quickly dried her hair with a hairdryer and escorted her out of the lab. And that would be the end of this. We left at ~13:30.  
> Going into this, I genuinely expected the supervisor himself to show up somehow in some shape or form. He didn't. And I expected the lab to be more lab-like instead of whatever cramped room that was. I can't say it was disappointing, but this wasn't what I had in mind, nor can I tell you what I got from this experience. Eh.

### 24-05-2022
#### Lab exposure programme 2
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> This is way dumber than I can ever imagine it could be. First off, this associate gave us the wrong building address. The thing is, the "wrong building" doesn't even exist, and it was wrong in a way that the wrongness could lean into either way between two different buildings. One of them is an engineering building, while the other is a completely unrelated social studies building. Logic should dictates that the engineering building was more likely to be the one he was attempting to convey. So I went to the building, and guess what- the room doesn't even exist. Let's set aside the wrong address for a moment to consider, why on earth would a biomedical engineering experiment be conducted in a social studies place instead of in an engineering building place?? Anyway, I headed towards the social science building as dumb as it sounds. Throughout this whole ordeal, I was frantically texting in the group with another student who I didn't even notice had joined the group. She had the same discovery I just made ~5 minutes ago about the non-existence of the supposed room. Meanwhile, the associate was completely offline for some godforsaken reason. I eventually reached the stupid building and it turned out to be the right place for some unfathomable reason. Martin was gonna be late for half an hour, and I have to say that saved him a lot of unnecessary hassle that we both had to go through.  
> Anyway, I entered the lab at long last. We were supposed to start at 14:00, but I only managed to arrive at 14:11 amidst the chaos. The lab was very very disappointing. It was merely a small room decorated in typical office fashion. The test subject was a retired old man, who was busy completing tasks on a computer monitor. The associate said that this was supposed to be a cognitive experiment. It aims to study the cognitive functions and its improvements after prolonged training with and without the assistance of exercise alongside. Apparently it has already been ongoing for a year and this is the guy's thirtieth or something session. Apparently he is a part of the control group; the experiment consists of the subject literally just sitting there completing tasks after tasks, from object memorisation to simple logic deduction (comparable to those in children's IQ tests) to facial recognition. Allegedly the experimental group got to use an exercise bike while doing the same tasks. I promise you this is ten times more boring than I am able to express it in words. Side note, the software used in similar researches are so buggy. I have personally partaken a few studies as the subject and have had my fair share of frustration with them. And it was no different here. The guy have encountered, roughly, at least five or so crashes and such.  
> So I watched this boring-ass "research" for ~30 minutes before Martin arrived. Intriguingly, he arrived way before the other girl who was supposedly only ~5 minutes behind me. I have no idea what dimension she had wandered into but that's besides the point. On the topic of this ridiculousness, I saw the associate's phone ring during the experiment, so I have no idea how he managed to miss our frantic chat messages earlier. Such bewilderment. She only joined us another ~15 minutes later. Did I mention the "lab" was really just a very small office? 'Cus the way we're sitting, latecomers get a more disadvantageous position progressively, so she basically cannot see a thing about the "experiment". The associate explain a little some more before going back to reading some research papers himself.  
> Anyhow, Martin just could not take it anymore and decided to leave out of boredom at ~15:30. The "experiment" was over shortly, but I stayed behind for a bit until ~16:00 to chat with the test subject. Honestly, I would say that was the most eventful part of the day, which is honestly quite depressing, all things considered. Apparently he was just a random old man they found instead of some kind of stroke recovery patient as Martin had conjectured. All in all, an utter waste of my and everyone's time. 0/5, would not recommend to my worst enemies.

### 31-05-2022
#### Year 1 Semester 2 results released
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> This is overall quite weird and unexpected. *(This is not the final grades since there was idiocy involved, see updated version [here](#english-grade-appeal-conclusion-probably))*  
>  
> | Course Title                                                            | Credit | Grade |
> | :---------------------------------------------------------------------- | :----: | :---- |
> | In Dialogue with Nature                                                 |   3    | A     |
> | [Multivariable Calculus for Engineers](#multivariable-calculus-final)   |   3    | A     |
> | [Linear Algebra for Engineers](#linear-algebra-final)                   |   3    | A-    |
> | [Logic](#logic-final)                                                   |   2    | A-    |
> | English Communication for University Studies                            |   4    | B+    |
> | [Human Anatomy and Physiology 2](#human-anatomy-and-physiology-2-final) |   2    | B+    |
> | Physical Education                                                      |   1    | TBD   |
> **Term GPA: 3.665 @17**  
> *Cumulative GPA: 3.655 @33*
>  
> As I said, weird indeed. I have no idea where to start so I think we should go through them each according to their grades.  
> For starters, I have actually sunken a tremendous amounts of work into the *In Dialogue with Nature* course from the very get-go. Martin took this course by the same lecturer the previous semester and he said that this lecturer favours hard work by the way he calculate his grades. I suppose I should introduce a little about what this course is about in the first place. In essence, it's meant to enrich students with the history, conception, principles, and whatnot of modern science and mathematics with the occasional philosophy mixed in. We had to attend weekly lectures that I skipped all of since they are entirely optional as I've been told by Martin, and weekly tutorial sessions which are really just some class discussion shit. It is highly encouraged that we learn the material, i.e. read 40-60 pages of the textbook, before the discussions since you would otherwise be very unlikely to know what on earth the discussion is about since they got pretty deep and complex at times. We also have biweekly quizzes that you should be able to get all correct if you had read the textbook and memorised the stuff (and yes even the minute stuff is very important). Anyway, this is only his method of assessment. From what I've heard, every lecturer has a different set of assessments and standards so it is of utmost importance that you chose a decent lecturer when you take this compulsory course. Now I haven't read, nay, attempted to read a book for, I'd say, around 6 years or so, and the book consists entirely of "classical" excerpts by anyone from Plato and Euclid to Newton and some other very important scientists that I didn't even know existed prior to this. Long story short, I was kinda expecting half broken medieval Latin-English with weird Shakespearean phrasing, which surprisingly were all translated into readable english. Fortunately, I was, and luckily still am, quite a keen reader, so I was able to get away with only starting to read the required materials an hour prior to the discussions, every single time. To be fair, I wasn't intending to do this, but rather I was quite against the grotesque idea of rushing through books; however, as the gods of all things unfortunate would dictate, I had the most demanding 2-hour course, *University English*, first thing in the morning right before this with only an hour break in-between. *Anyway*, for the actually demanding assignments, we had to write an 800-word reflective journal during our midterm period, and an 1500-word term paper during our finals period. Both of them required an enormous amounts of brainstorming, re-reading the entire textbook, further researching, and fine-tuning. And if you consider both papers were assigned in the middle of exam periods, you can imagine that it wasn't particularly too fun of an experience. I even sacrificed an entire other course just for this (more about this later). So ultimately, I got full score in the quizzes, a staggeringly high 89.2% for my reflective journal, and a decently high 86% for my term paper. I even choose to write a free topic for my term paper since I didn't find any of the given ones to be very interesting. Holy shit, this is a long paragraph. The point is, if I hadn't gotten an A in this course, some murdering of the lecturer would probably have occurred.  
> Both maths courses *(**MC**: [M](#multivariable-calculus-midterm), [F](#multivariable-calculus-final); **LA**: [M](#linear-algebra-midterm), [F](#linear-algebra-final))* are quite similar so I'll just talk about them together. I will try my best not to start ranting about the shitty lecturer again seeing that I've already done it 2 times already. To be fair, their grades were very much unexpected. Unexpected not in a way that they're very high or very low, just that I didn't really have an expectation at all since I honestly didn't care or them too much now or ever. Partly I'd say this would be 'cus I was too focused on the other courses this semester. To be fair, I'd say I had only devoted around 5 hours to both courses combined, so this is definitely very cost-effective.  
> *Logic* *([M](#logic-midterm), [F](#logic-final))* is really a hit-and-miss scenario. It's honestly another cost-effective course, and I knew this damn well the moment I had the conceived of the idea of taking this course. Sure, this course was harder than I had expected, especially because of its difficulty having ramped up exponentially after the midterm. But for a 2-credit course, it was an alright grade despite it not being what I had in mind when I decided to take it. One thing I'd say though, is that, this had been a worse investment in terms of time-cost than both the maths courses combined.  
> *University English*. Where do I begin? This is rather outrageous. I have spent great time and effort, for what-, a B+? I have done so well throughout the semester, in all assignments. This course, mind you, also has two papers during both the midterm and finals period. So it, along with *In Dialogue with Nature*, has contributed to the sacrifice of *Human Anatomy and Physiology*. I'm just going to say straight up: I am going to appeal the shit out of this ridiculousness and I swear I will not allow this jester of a lecturer trample all over my grade. I shall dive deeper into this in another entry so I think I'll spare the details here for now. *(**University English appeal saga**: [1](#english-grade-appeal-bureaucratic-hell), [2](#english-grade-appeal-conclusion-probably))*  
> Last but not least, the sacrificial lamb, *Human Anatomy and Physiology* *([CA1](#human-anatomy-and-physiology-2-ca1), [CA2](#human-anatomy-and-physiology-2-ca2), [F](#human-anatomy-and-physiology-2-final))*. Despite its sacrificial status, I was genuinely hoping for better, in the A-range at least. Wishful thinking, it was. But no matter, I expected this outcome. I have simply encountered so many logistical clashes and brain retirements. If only I hadn't been such a mess. Not that I could've done too terribly differently anyway. I'm still unsure whether sacrificing a course had been a good idea. I initially thought I could sacrifice a 2-credit course for a combined total of 7 credits, but that plan involves the mentioned 7 credits are actually in the A-range. Not sure.  
> I have talked about this numerous times before, [since I have been in university](#getting-back-my-hkdse-papers) really, but my goal was to internal transfer into Medicine. And for that, one would need to have attained at least a 3.7 GPA, which I clearly hadn't. Although I would say, it is tantalisingly close, especially considering if not for the pestering *University English* B+ but instead an A-, I would've attained a cGPA of 3.703. Fuck this. I mean I had prepared mentally for a 4-year long GPA struggle but this is still too close to not get frustrated by. APPEAL AHOY!!!

### 02-06-2022
#### CU Medical Centre tour
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> This is completely out of my expectations. I'm unsure if this is part of the original curriculum or an add-on since most of the summer practical training programme has been converted into online teaching. We were supposed to go and attach in Prince Wales Hospital for a while but instead we got a whole lot of online teaching and a tour to the *CU Medical Centre*.  
> Although it is merely a cross of the road away from CUHK main campus, I never really went in there and looked around. The lobby was very grand, definitely more of a shopping mall or hotel lobby than one of a hospital. Yes, it is a private hospital and all but apparently that also means you can just spend money on stuff like this.  
> In the first session, we were led to a lecture theatre where they briefed us about they history and aims, just a standard sales pitch type of introduction. But then suddenly the lecturing doctor casually mentioned that he has a surgery to do in 5 minutes and left. Apparently there is an array of cameras in the operating theatre and we get to watch his surgery live remotely. It was a minimally invasive ACL reconstruction surgery. It involves pulling out a couple hamstring tendons and reshaping them into a ligament then grafting in onto the torn ACL. The doctor was talking the whole time about the surgery and he started to move the patient's knee in weird ways demonstrating the torn ACL. I genuinely did not even see his scalpel touching the patient but only the incision appearing on the knee. He made 2 more incisions and started jamming ("jam" is a very accurate verb in this case) the endoscope and other instruments into the cavity. After an endoscopic inspection, he wriggled the instruments towards the hamstrings and just simply extracted two. The whole process sounds very forceful because it is. He even just straight up used his hands to poke around at the tendons *ex-vivo*. He then handed them to his assistant who then quickly combined them into a graft ligament using a mess of staples and wire. It is genuinely more akin to arts and crafts than to delicate science. The doctor spared some time to do a Q&A before going back drilling two holes into the femur and tibia where the graft ligament was threaded through. The surrounding water was straight up boiling when he was drilling and you can clearly see him putting in a lot of elbow grease during that. He also spent a lot of time poking around the bones and the hole talking about it; he literally started poking around the cavity seemingly without much concern. Screws and a metallic button cap thing (which he talked a lot about for some reason) were installed to secure the graft. He did the mobility test that he did earlier to demonstrate that the weird knee movements were instantly inhibited right after the installation. Water and random fluid keeps getting squeezed out from the incisions as he was doing the movement test and that was quite unsettling to witness especially with all the sharp instruments still in the knee cavity. The whole procedure was surprisingly blood-free. I don't reckon there was any bleeding at all except from the bone drilling. I guess it'll have to be blood-free lest the endoscopic camera be completely obstructed. The whole operation took around 2 hours when it was supposed to only take 1 when performed normally, without all the talking and stuff. I can't imagine this does too much good to the patient. It was quite a bewildering experience, especially with the four camera angles. Martin apparently thought of it otherwise. He was initially afraid of blood stating that it was quite disturbing to watch, but then proceeded to straight up fall asleep. He snored so hard that literally the entire lecture theatre can hear it.  
> We were then split up into two groups and were given a tour of the pathology, radiology, pharmacy, surgery, and sports medicine and rehabilitation departments. Nothing was too terribly noteworthy about the tours. I was honestly quite distracted by the [grade appeal shenanigans](#english-grade-appeal-bureaucratic-hell) towards the end of the tours. We took a group photo at the very end, which I found quite odd but it's whatever.

#### English grade appeal bureaucratic hell
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> I suppose I should do a detailed breakdown before anything else lest my eagerness makes little sense.  
> First of all, this course accounts for 4 credits, which is nothing to scoff at. To give you some perspective, I have only take na total of 33 credits this whole year, so it definitely matters a lot for my GPA.  
> Anyway, as I have mentioned, I have put a lot of time into this course. And frankly, I got quite decent grades:  
>  
> | Assessment item            |    Score | Weighting |
> | :------------------------- | -------: | :-------- |
> | Summary Synthesis Exercise | 83.5/100 | 20%       |
> | Essay Proposal             | 80.5/100 | 20%       |
> | Oral Presentation          |   83/100 | 20%       |
> | Expository Essay           |      TBA | 40%       |
>  
> The first item, *summary synthesis exercise*, accounts for a whopping 20% of the entire course. However, the entire assignment involves only writing a grand total of 20 words. You literally only have to rephrase a sentence from a paragraph and that would be it. An absolutely ridiculous effort-to-weighting ratio if you ask me.  
> The second one, *essay proposal*. It's basically just a compilation of the general flow and ideas of the essay we would have to write later on. This course is basically one big assignment, in the way that everything taught in this course leads us to the final essay. To be fair, it was a bit of a rush for me to complete this particular assessment item since I had decided to change the essay topic rather close to the submission deadline of the essay proposal, and hence I was not able to do too much research. An on top of this, I managed to submit it late despite having rushed the content, which costed me 3 points off the score. Most of the time taken was actually to cut down on my word count since for some inexplicable reason everyone loves to put harsh word limits on papers. Considering that, I actually got 83.5% in it, which is actually pretty decent.  
> The third one, *oral presentation*. We had to present the entire content of our essay in just 5 minutes. Did I mention I hate harsh word limits yet? because this is the next worse thing. I had to talk so fast to cram everything into the 5 minutes I was practically giving the presentation in double speed. Luckily I managed to not trip up too much as I tend to do when I speak, especially at that kinds of speed. The final grade is respectable I guess.  
> At this point, I was expecting an A- from the course, since it only requires 80%, which I am comfortably within the range of. Considering this is a 4-credit course, I was putting in quite a bit of effort trying to even squeeze an A out of it, which I would be able to manage if I could get 89%, although this is nigh impossible. Anyway, when the final course grade is out, apparently I have been awarded a B+, which would imply that my final essay had been awarded ≤64%, which obviously doesn't sound right. My essay topic is quite decent too, all things considered. ***"Institutional racism in the United States: Its origins, persistence, and impacts on social mobility"***. I genuinely believe I did a great job writing this, I had even asked others to comment on its flow and ideas and whatnot. The stuff that was in the final essay was pretty similar to the essay proposal, which he had given great comments about, only more detailed and elaborated of course. I had even made sure to follow his every suggestion and amend the essay accordingly, so I really doubt the problem was the content of the essay. To add on, this B+ has a great impact for my final GPA, considering, must I remind you again, that this is a 4-credit course. I was absolutely having none of this. So I went and sent an email to ask for a grade appeal right away. I was in the middle of the [CU Medical Centre tour](#cu-medical-centre-tour) at that moment. To my dismay, the guy was out of Hong Kong enjoying his vacation, and his replies were snail-paced. He said that apparently I had surpassed the word limit of the essay, and that had somehow costed me ~20% of the score, which I found to be rather appalling. Did I mention I hate word limits? I specifically remember going through all the documents looking for the word limit tolerance but somehow not being able to find it at the time, so I just assumed it would use the university standard tolerance of ±10%, which would equate to 160 extra words. But apparently this assignment in particular is special for some reason and it had a specific tolerance of only ±50 words. **50!** This information was for some reason not mentioned in the assessment rubrics or assignment instruction, but instead hidden within the course introduction documents, the very same ones that includes his name, position, telephone, etc.; unimportant stuff. I even asked him about the word limit before the deadline since I was so positively confused at the time I thought that would be better than nothing, which mind you he didn't reply until it was past the deadline.  
> Anyway, I mentioned all this in my second email to question his grades. I'll admit my grounds are evidently weak although I would consider them logically sound. And you'll have to agree that despite all this fiasco such word limit overrun would not deserve a ~20% grade deduction. But upon my second email, he had already enabled his auto-reply, which would imply that he was no longer checking his inbox until he would be back in Hong Kong. I was rather anxious since should this appeal be successful, my cGPA would become 3.703. Crucially, it would pass the 3.7 threshold which you allow me to apply for the Medicine internal transfer. However, the deadline is 05/06 (only 3 days away!!), and a grade appeal, even a successful one, takes a very long time to process. Why are course instructors even allowed to take holidays before the grades are released and appeals are settled??  
> *[Conclusion](#english-grade-appeal-conclusion-probably)*

### 14-06-2022
#### English grade appeal conclusion (probably)
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> A lot had happened since [this ordeal began](#english-grade-appeal-bureaucratic-hell), countless emails
> He eventually did respond and said I should go ahead and request an official grade appeal from the English department. I felt like he was trying to ignore me to lessen his workload during his holidays. I couldn't stand his sloth, so I went straight ahead and involved the English department to request this grade appeal. I made sure to CC him in the email so he wouldn't be able to ignore me. I don't believe he really meant it when he said that I should ask the English department directly, since immediately after my email, he said that I had *"bypassed him"*. I made it clear to him that I was merely following his instructions and of course I also CC'd the department just to make sure we are on the same page. After a total of ***21*** fucking emails, he eventually agreed to entertain my appeal and bumped me up a sub-grade from B+ to A-.  
> So here are my grades as they stand:  
>  
> | Course Title                                                            | Credit | Grade |
> | :---------------------------------------------------------------------- | :----: | :---- |
> | In Dialogue with Nature                                                 |   3    | A     |
> | [Multivariable Calculus for Engineers](#multivariable-calculus-final)   |   3    | A     |
> | English Communication for University Studies                            |   4    | A-    |
> | [Linear Algebra for Engineers](#linear-algebra-final)                   |   3    | A-    |
> | [Logic](#logic-final)                                                   |   2    | A-    |
> | [Human Anatomy and Physiology 2](#human-anatomy-and-physiology-2-final) |   2    | B+    |
> | Physical Education                                                      |   1    | TBD   |
> **Term GPA: 3.756 @17**  
> *Cumulative GPA: 3.703 @33*
>  
> One might think this is a completely ridiculous endeavour, but might I draw your attention to the 0.048 difference in GPA, which is definitely nothing to scoff at. I hope I never encounter this absurd demonstration of bureaucracy and sloth ever again in my entire life, although somehow I doubt this could ever come true.

## July - 2022
### 09-07-2022
#### Interpersonal relationships
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
<!-- 👥 Relationships -->
> In a late night 4-hour phone call with Samuel, we discussed various things and among them we explored the roots of the relationships of and around us. I have always have this sort of meta viewpoint to things that have happened and are currently happening (I have frequently talked with Toby about [this](#self-awareness)), but I always thought it was merely part of my typical overthinking as I always do. I used to analyse myself and the people around me quite a lot, not so much anymore but I now still do it sometimes. It used to be a constant task that I have to tend do, as though someone is always in my head nagging for objective statistics and insights and whatnot. I have to say, it kind of helped with learning to read people. I have always been commented by other to not be able to read people well, but I guess I just have not tried hard enough before(?) although I think it might just be my incompetence for subjectivity.  
> Anyway, I have always thought that I have always acted as a bridge for people around me. The way that I interact and joke with people tend to also bring completely unrelated groups together and basically let them introduce themselves to themselves non-verbally. For instance, I would sometimes start a joke with one group of people but finish it with another. I realise it sounds odder than it feels like if you are actually there, but I admit it is quite a weird act. If I have to describe it, I would say it is like as if I am the protagonist of a show or cartoon and I'm doing throwback jokes or references that only the audience will be able to follow and understand. It sounds quite self-centred when it's put this way, but I argue that everyone can only ever wish to be self-centred anyway since it's not like you can just be someone else and experience their entire storyline, so to speak. To be honest, I have always been aware of this phenomenon, even when I was at the moment in the middle of said acts. I never really paid too much thought to it though, although I admit it did lead to some weirdness from time to time, but they tended to fit my thematic personality of being highly plastic. *(**Side tangent**: The thematic plasticity, I figured, was [mainly from Toby](#farewell-toby). I believed it started since he was arguably my first friend in secondary school. It just so happens that plasticity is a very easy and somewhat novel way of [knowing new people and making friends](#farewell-marwin-and-marcus), although I have to say that it is definitely not everyone's cup of tea nor can it be even performed in front of certain people.)*  
> Anyway, Samuel noted this phenomenon too and I think that's the first time I realise it is not merely my overthinking (or perhaps we are boh very prone to overthinking?). He said that he specifically try to approach me as a means to broaden his social circle, which looking back, sounds very odd, especially considering I don't really see myself as a really social person. I can definitely name a few scenarios where this is pretty evident though; the most recent one being me having introduced Eddy to Martin, and somehow they become more acquainted than I am with Eddy despite us having ~10 years of head-start.

### 14-07-2022
#### Pain and suffering
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
<!-- 🌞 Well-being -->
> I am sick again somehow. Not sick sick, but suffering from some kind of GI problems again. They are really quite reoccurring. I'd say I suffer from something like this at least once a month or something. I have been ailment-prone since I was a kid, so maybe I was just built weird or something, but I have definitely been fully utilising my dad's company's health plan for the past 18 years. I really can't begin the name all the reasons I've been to the doctor for. Luckily I don't remember anything being too serious in particular, barring 2 hospitalisations, most of my ailments only invited me to general clinics and only sometimes specialist clinics. Partly because of the aforementioned health plan, I have been to clinics all around Hong Kong. Just off of the top of my head, I have been to *Cheung Sha Wan*, *Lai Chi Kok*, *Mei Foo*, *Mong Kok*, *Kowloon Bay*, *Lam Tin*, *Wan Chai*, *Queen Elizabeth Hospital* all just for clinic visits. I can honestly say travelling to and from various clinics accounted for most of my travelling as a kid. While others are travelling around the world to visit landmarks, I was travelling around Hong Kong to visit doctors. It is genuinely a very weird track record to have. It might not come as a surprise that I have contracted more than the normal share of ailments, most commonly GI problems, respiratory problems, and fever. I was unwell so often that I started being able to recognise drug names and doses.  
> My GI tract in particular is the worst offender throughout my entire life. Along with its frequency, the intensity of pain is not to be downplayed. I've briefly mentioned it [before](#getting-back-my-hkdse-papers). I had spontaneous sharp abdominal pains that woke me up at ~04:00, and after god-knows-how-long in the toilet, I literally almost fainted while walking back to my room. I even had to take 15 minutes off during the Biology HKDSE exam to use the toilet.  
> The pain. I'm not sure where I got this idea, but it was definitely when I was very young. I thought of committing suicide. Think about it, life is painful, undoubtedly. In comparison, the sweet release of death seems like a no-brainer, especially if you're subjected to frequent and intense pain for absolutely no reason. Yes, I have been rather grim since I was very young. I don't believe this was where the idea of suicide originated, but this was definitely one of the triggers. I speculate I know where suicidal thoughts first danced with me (It was not because of some kind of ailment). My childhood is rather bumpy. I might talk about it some time. The first time that I can remember wanting to end it right then and there (I think I was ~6), I was sitting on the bed in my parents' room. There is this huge glass window in the room. Obviously, the idea was to break the glass and just jump. I remember testing out the strength of the glass with my fists, but ultimately determined that I would need something like a hammer to break the glass. But the thing is, I didn't know where to find a hammer in the house. And every single time, this was the sole reason I ceased my plan. Another obvious option was to just head to the rooftop and jump, but I remember my parents saying that the rooftop is always locked, so I didn't even bothered to attempt at all. I had also considered just stabbing myself to death, but I also considered that I might not have the strength to puncture my intercostal muscles to my heart, and that there was conveniently no knife sharp and small enough to fit through my ribcage.  
> Amidst this seemingly dark topic, I genuinely find it funny sometimes. In moments of literal desperation, anger, and sadness, I still considered thoroughly the feasibility and effectiveness of my plans. I guess logic really can stop you from suicide, but this is a very exotic way to apply this quote. Every single time my idea would start and end on the bed without me taking a single action. I honestly have no idea why I was this dark and grim ever since I was so young, but this has became sort of an inside joke, if you will, that every time the word "suicide" would pop into my mind, this would be the first thing I would be reminded of. This probably says a lot about my mental health. I'm not saying I have gotten better, just not any worse I think. It's weird how my darkest times are my childhood. I'd like to extrapolate this trend and say that I have changed my point of view and whatnot, but mostly I think I've just stepped back from life a bit, stopped caring every once in a while. For better or worse, I'm not sure, but I speculate that it is just hiding behind my back, waiting to burst any moment. Well, this entry ended up more light-hearted than I had expected (no, this is not sarcasm), so I guess this is a good place to sign off.


## August - 2022
### 01-08-2022
#### Failed bowling
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> I have no idea why we proposed bowling, but here we are anyway. We found a place in *Whampoa*, and it really is one of the only places in Hong Kong with affordable bowling. So we met up at 12:20, and of course CNok was late by half an hour as usual. It really had been quite a while since we've seen each other. Such is the reality when none of us is in the same university. Anyway, we split up; Samuel and I went to the bowling place to try to secure a booking while CNok and Efren went looking for something to eat. I gotta say, the exterior of the bowling place is very drab, and the plaza is literally empty. I really did not have high hopes for the place. Once we step in, however, it was like another world. The place is much much larger than I had imagined. I'd say there are ~20 lanes, with passable decor. When we got there, there wasn't really much traffic, so we thought it wouldn't be necessary to get a ticket. I don't believe the place offer such ticket booking services anyway, judging from how cost is calculated there. So we went back to meet up with them. I have no idea what CNok and Efren were doing but apparently they still haven't found a place to eat yet, so Samuel and I proceeded to stroll in nearby malls on our way to them. Every restaurant we looked at had terribly long queues, and after ~40 minutes of looking around, we gave up and just went to some small restaurant instead of waiting for a curry place or some shit.  
> We ended up eating for ~90 minutes, and by the time we got back to the bowling place, it was completely packed with people, like literally full of people everywhere. Stark contrast to what it was like earlier in the day. We sat around waiting for ~30 minutes, but the ticketing number did not tick down once. So we eventually gave up. It is honestly rather funny how we can never seem to get things to go with our plan whenever we plan something; [last time](#an-attempt-to-hike) it was because of the weather, and this time it was because we ate for too long. I guess we are better at doing unplanned shit? Is that even a thing?  
> CNok suddenly had the idea to go to the *Science Museum* for some reason, so we took a taxi there. And of course it just so happens that there was some sort of special dinosaur exhibit going on (What did I say about being better at doing unplanned shit?). It has genuinely be so long since I've been there, but barely anything seems to have changed. I don't know what else I can talk about, but somehow we managed to spend 2.5 horus there. This has got to be the stupidest day we've ever spent.

### 27-09-2022
#### Peculiar encounter
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> This had got to be the weirdest encounter I have ever experienced. I was riding the MTR home from school when a junior schoolmate asked me a maths problem. I whipped out my iPad and proceeded to tackle the problem right there and didn't give it a second thought. But when I was exiting the train for an interchange, some old-ish couple tapped my shoulder for my attention. Apparently they were so amazed by my "iPad skills" and my ability to "use technology fluently" that they had to approach me. They saw that I was doing maths stuff and asked if I was some kind of maths tutor. Initially I tried to just brush them off with a few short answers. But then they seem to want to hire me for some coding or something 'cus obviously mathematics and engineering and programming is the same exact thing. They asked about my major of study and pretended to own a company that does things in my field, which upon further questioning, apparently has something to do with animals(???). I still struggle to fathom how that is related to biomedical engineering but sure whatever. They kept trying to offer me some job about programming and kept asking me about my programming portfolio or some shit. They seemed very eager to get me on board for something and keep insisting that we meet up at a later date and that I should call in my friends to do the same. I eventually surrendered my phone number for "future correspondence" before blocking their asses immediately. Speaking of their asses, the presumed husband looked quite old, possibly in his early 60s. He had some apparent deteriorated cognitive capacity since he couldn't seem to hold information very well, while appearing to be very confident and curious at the same time. Precisely the type of people I hate to deal with most. The presumed wife looked 10-20 years younger, not too noteworthy. They are honestly quite uncanny, being in-between sharp businessmen and proper old hags (and whatever the male equivalent of hag is). Maybe describing them as having this slight professor-ish aura amongst a vast ocean of general old-ness with a hint of delusion might be the most accurate I can be.  
> What was this all about anyway? Very suspicious.

### 17-10-2022
#### Programming midterm
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> This entire course is the bane of my existence. I absolutely despise *C* to the sincerest degree possible, as I do for other low-level programming languages. The languages by themselves is fine I suppose, since they do serve some kind of purpose as a side job to annoying all programmers everywhere. But in this context, in an academic context, this is intolerable. Imagine teaching basic maths to someone with no idea what maths even is by making them do calculus. 0.1 + 0.2 = 0.3? Never heard of it in my entire life! There is absolutely no reason to teach a programming language older than my dad to people of this era, especially not complete beginners. Its nuances with its types and strict syntax is the perfect match to not start learning programming with. I guess this is where all the negative connotations about programming stems from. As much shit I would like to give *Python* for its ugly syntax, its simplicity and ease of understanding is undeniable (sort of), at least as low-level-esque languages go. I would much rather schools teach *Python* as a starter rather than *C* as a starter if they must trouble complete beginners with needlessly confusing syntax and nuances for some psychotically sadistic reason. I guess there are worse ways to start, namely *Java*, but at least its complexity originates from its ambition to do classes and objects, while *C* struggles to do simple string manipulation unless you are willing to dive deep into pointers shit which, need I remind you, *complete beginners* absolutely are not. I genuinely do not understand why they couldn't teach modern widespread high-level languages like *JavaScript* (totally biased) instead, considering *JavaScript* is on literally every browser ever, it is responsible for running the majority of the internet, you can literally run it everywhere, it is literally designed to be hard to crash since you wouldn't want your internet browser to crash every 5 seconds now do we? Not to mention its flexible syntax and ease of understanding on top of native object and common function support. The list goes on. If schools want to play with types for shits and giggles to satisfy their sadistic nature, they have *TypeScript*, which is just a superset of *JavaScript*. Heck, both *JS* and *TS* even have strict mode if they want more sadism without needing to sacrifice precious abstraction and utility.  
> Admittedly, I have gone terribly off-track. But my point is, programming is not about syntax or types or whatnot, it never has been. It is about problem solving, simplification, and optimisation. Try perfecting a culinary recipe while wrestling with a wood and coal oven when a perfectly good gas stove is sitting right next to you. It is not only missing the point, but straight up insulting. A terrible waste of potential programmers when you start them off by pushing them off a cliff. And it basically sums up my experience of taking (or rather not attending) this course so far. The same goes for that of doing this paper. It is insulting to do, stupidly easy and yet stupidly challenging at the same time. I doubt one can find another subject that is as polar as this shit is. Just thinking about this atrocity makes my stomach churn and my soul leave. Utter injustice and blatant slaughter. May whomever sadistically constructed these barbaric curriculum suffer anguish as twisted as fathomable before dying a death as painful as imaginable, and I say this with every atom of my being.

#### Outline of Chinese Culture midterm
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> This course is really quite interesting. Despite what the course title suggests, it is really more about studying, questioning, and subverting traditional Chinese culture and ideas than simply appreciating it as we have done for years. It is a little bit radical in a sense. This might be the only course that I completely have no idea about when I took it. *UGEA (Chinese Cultural Heritage)* courses were the ones I dreaded most since this area concerns Chinese culture and history, all of which urges me to pull my hair out, but this is easily the most interesting course I have taken so far, barring *UGFN (In Dialogue with Nature)*.  
> The midterm exam consists of 20 T/F questions and 6 long questions. The lecturer was quite insistent that we give concise and precise answers instead of writing everything that comes to mind, for which I'm quite glad. Interestingly, we were allowed to bring in a double-sided A4 cheat sheet, which I honestly didn't really find too much utility in, but I guess I can see why this is a thing. I have genuinely no idea how I did, as do I for most expressive-type questions/papers. I guess I understood the ideas pretty well, although not so much for the material itself on a word-to-word basis. So I guess I can't imagine myself doing either too bad or terribly great.

#### Prince of Wales Hospital biomechanics lab
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> This is quite a weird experience for a lab. We were split into groups to visit the lab. Louis, Wales, Helen, and I went to the lab together.  
> But to talk about the lab, we have to first talk about some backstory. We could choose the timeslot ourselves, but as per usual, all of the timeslots sucked. Not only were they in ridiculous times, most of them also clash with our lesson schedule. So I proposed for us to choose the best compromise time slot where we would leave around an hour early the previous lesson, which happened to be a Chinese lesson, so that we could attend the lab in time.  
> When we leave the class early, I was intending to take a bus near one of the CUHK entrances; however, I decided that calling an Uber directly would be preferable considering it was raining at the time, and it would only cost us ~$2 more. Of course, as my luck would have it, we waited for ~15 minutes for a match but no driver took the job. That left us with no choice but to stick to the original plan of taking the bus. On the bus, I tried to offer an Uber job again, but this time the pick-up location was just outside the MTR station, and a driver took the job immediately. Anyway, we got to the hospital, but we have no idea where on earth the venue is. It took us ~10 minutes to actually find the lab and we barely got there in time.  
> The lab does mainly gait study. There were ~20 cameras mounted on the ceiling surrounding the test area. The analysis would be done using motion-tracking technology and pressure-sensitive floor tiles. Apparently, one of us were supposed to be the test subject. The study requires 16 shiny tracking balls stuck to the subject's body, and I was the only wearing shorts (as I always do), which would mean that my skin would be the most easily accessible, and I was named the test subject for the day. To be fair, I was quite a bit exposed, as the tracking balls require me to be.  
> Anyhow, the lab person start by explaining the basics of motion tracking and whatnot, and we spent quite a bit of time waving around this shiny wand for calibration. When it was time for the actual gait analysis, apparently my weight distribution is quite skewed and swayed quite a bit. I definitely had not noticed this normally. Perhaps I do suffer from this weirdness in general, but I blame the fact that I could not wear shoes the entire time so it wasn't like I was walking how I would anyway. I was then told to try to balance on one leg on the pressure-sensitive floor tiles for force analysis and apparently I also have quite a horrible balance. Then I was told to jump onto the tiles first with both legs, then with one. Now I might add that the floor tiles are made of metal so you could imagine that it hurt quite a bit when I jumped onto the tiles, especially with one leg.  
> I guess this whole lab was quite a weird experience, as might be the case for anyone named the test subject of the day. But the entire concept of the lab seems to me the be quite weird. I just cannot fathom a whole office-lab hybrid space will all sorts of gadgets and equipment solely for the purpose of gait analysis. I don't think this is something that is of particularly high demand either. I suppose this is why the equipment are all so old and frail. We spent a total of 90 minutes there which I feel 90 too many already. Seems to me to be a giant waste of resources and human intellect, but what do I know?

> Well this was not a course that I would foresee myself taking. I guess I have always have a basic idea of what the study of economics concerns, mainly from what CNok used to talk about. For me, economics has always been the sort of memorising subjects, be it basic equations or definitions. CNok said that the subject of economics is mainly about identifying edge cases, and I can't say this idea hasn't helped me along the way. I guess the first step to getting to know the subject material is to know the assessments. I am well aware that this is horribly misaligned with the actual purpose of education and learning in general, but for me this kind of shape my expectation and mindset for what I should actually be paying attention to.

I can't say I can see how it relates too much to society and culture as other courses in this area do, but I do suppose I can't complain too much. What's interesting is that, this course is actually doubled-coded with *ECON*, aka for actual economic major students. It wasn't really too difficult, as one might be able to catch from the implication, despite me not having attended any lectures at all and only having studied the material for ~3 hours. This crunch study mode where I would wake up at ~03:00 the morning/night before the exam and go through the material before going back to bed for another consolidation nap really do seem to work for some godforsaken reason. I did the exact same thing for the [Chinese Culture midterm](#outline-of-chinese-culture-midterm) and a couple others before.  
> Anyhow, I was quite worried when I took this course since it was a 3-credit course while we are only required to take 2-credit course for *UGE (University General Education)* courses, especially considering I was not familiar with economics at all. We have to take at least one 3-credit course among the 4 areas, and I was trying to save it for the area I am most confident in, namely *UGEB (Nature, Science and Technology)*. I was genuinely contemplating late-dropping this course if I would be to fail or perform terribly in the midterm, since policies are built to be abused and toyed with in order to extort grades with. This option is still on the table though, since apparently economics is quite adamant about precision and keywords, both of which I am terrible with. Let's see how this goes.

### 10-11-2022
#### Mortal currency
<!-- 💭 Philosophy -->
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
> There's something I feel like people don't talk enough about. There is always this talk about how time is limited for us mortals, and how it is the one most important currency that we will ever have the luxury, or displeasure, of owning and spending. But for me, that place should really be given to energy. I think have briefly talked about this before, though I can't find the entry for the life of me. But the gist is, I get tired terribly easily. I might as well be a frail old sack of meat and bones. Whenever I get out of the house, I get extremely tired. Not at the moment really, but more so after the event. It's like some sort of debt that I have to repay at the end of every event and social interaction I partake in. I guess it's similar to what I talked about in [social forfeit](#social-forfeit). For me, the time cost of participating in anything includes: the mental and physical preparation prior to leaving my house, the trip travelling to the venue, the event itself, the trip travelling back home, the un-preparation after returning, the mental and physical collapse from the exhaust that I will have for the next few days, and the nagging reliving of and betterment proposal from the memories of the event. This is basically the sole reason why I would very much like to avoid social interactions or anything near that realm. Simply put, the true time cost for me for participating in any event at all is way way higher than one might assume. I literally cannot get back onto my feet and return to my prior productivity levels until I have gone through my exhaust cycle. Maybe there is already some existing economic concepts that can perfectly describe what I'm trying to convey, but the opportunity cost for me attending anything is simply way too high. I guess you could say that it is my desire to not waste my mortal time not attaining my maximum productivity that is my main reason for trying to minimise things to have to do. I am aware that some people (maybe most) can recharge instead of draining themselves by going out. I have heard enough analogies about this types of introvert vs extrovert thing, but I don't believe the exhaustion is either mental or physical, but rather it stems from the soul of my being. There is simply a nagging feeling that I should be doing something productive with my time, precisely because my time is so limited. I can basically never sit still if I know deep-down that what I am currently doing is not what my soul is yearning to do. I am terrible with words but please do try to grasp at what I'm trying to say.  
> That desire is not merely about preferring work or school or whatnot over social stuff either. It is something about perfection. It is also this desire to do what I think I should be doing that is keeping me from doing precisely that. I believe what I deem to be most deserving of my time, and hence where I should spend most of my limited mortal time on, is to reach for perfection. It's not that I dread social stuff and enjoy doing solitary stuff, but rather I dread not being able to do something to a perfect extent, and avoiding spending precious time on things I don't believe I am good at is simply a better economic choice for me. Looping back to the soul thing and the reliving I've mentioned, I, or rather, my sub-consciousness, simply cannot cease to ponder how I could have acted better in any given past situation. The more impactful the situation, naturally the more I ponder. But pondering itself takes up so much mental capacity and energy at a time that it is simply better to not have put myself in such circumstances in the first place. I tend to put off my obligations until I have reasonable confidence that I would be able to complete them to the best of my abilities; half-assing things is simply not acceptable. But as you might have guessed, this also can lead to endless heaps of work sitting there simply not being done. I have still yet to figure out a tolerable compromise. I do realise I am not making too much cohesive sense, but I guess this is some kind of soul-searching exercise, and there really is not such thing as an organised soul. On that note, "soul" is a horrible word for what I'm trying to express, but it will have to do for the time being.  
> The thing that tipped me to this mortal currency, is that I have recently noticed more and more that my preferred mode of scheduling is based on rationing energy instead of time. I believe this has always been the way that I have operated, just that I have only started to notice recently, for whatever reason. I find myself not really following the circadian rhythm, as anyone who knows me can testify. I believe this originates from my childhood insomnia (or is it the other way round?), but I do like to believe that my productivity is mostly unaffected by the time of day. The thing that I mentioned not enough people talk about, is that not all time is equal. One's productivity strictly wanes as time passes, however, crucially, it is not only dependent on the passage of time, rather on a multitude of other factors, for example the aforementioned social events. Therefore I propose that a fixed sleeping cycle, or circadian rhythm is very much outdated. It simply fails to consider energy/productivity as a valuable resource. On the contrary, my sleep-whenever-I-want pattern might work tons better seeing that I recharge whenever I feel necessary and work whenever my excessive energy urges me to, rather than to have some inanimate indifferent time-telling device dictate that for you. Spacing out work according to energy is really quite the hack, for me at least, especially during times of need, like exams and whatnot. Although I believe I have been operated in this mode since forever, I have only really recognised it recently. I might try to devise a better way than a daily calendar schedule to plan my energy expenditure, although I highly doubt there is any since there is hardly any metric one can rely on. Well this entry is really the classic rambling-on-and-on-until-I-have-no-idea-where-I-have-veered-off-into type of deal. My train of thought just ended so I guess this entry should too lest I write more empty nonsense.
