### 21-11-2022
#### Deterioration
<!-- 💭 Philosophy -->
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
<!-- 🌞 Well-being -->
> I'm not sure if I have talked about this phenomenon before, but I've been feeling my mental capacity and clarity fade for a while now. I'm not sure about the cause, but the thing is I can feel it. I believe it started around a year ago, probably longer, but it's becoming more and more apparent by the day. I would describe it as a general fog in my brain. I seem to not be able to grasp and retain information well. Everything seem to be in more of a haze, and myself in the middle of it.  
> I seem to no longer be able to rewind what I have just heard; words would just slur past me without meaning. I found myself slurring on words more and more (This phenomenon in particular seems to have manifested ~5 years ago). Words generally have less meaning to me. Interestingly, perhaps fortunately, written ones do seem to still hold their meaning and power just yet, but spoken ones are getting harder to decipher. I used to be able to read very fast when I was younger, but this skill started deteriorating ~6 years ago I'd say. This is probably the very first symptom that I started noticing something might be wrong with myself. Along with the difficulties in deciphering spoken words, comes difficulties in parsing conversations and stories. I might attribute this to the general feeling of losing my grasp to the world that I mentioned above.  
> Another thing is, my memory seems to get foggier. I've always had moments of *deja vu* since I was young, everyone has, I think. I'm not sure about everyone else, but for my I've always thought of them as though I have seen flashes of the exact scene in my dreams before, like I was presented an image very briefly. I was very much convinced at the time. If I have to give an estimate, I'd say I was <10 at the time (I've briefly talked about it [before](#reality-and-dreams)). This *deja vu* thing started to be rarer and rarer as I age, or perhaps they just becoming less and less prominent and memorable that I didn't even log their existence into my memory. But recently, I've noticed a sudden surge of such events, but not in the way that *deja vu* normally presents itself. To my understanding, the reason *deja vu* exists at all is because the optic nerve and its signal gets routed through parts of the subconscious brain before reaching the visual cortex and getting processed into a conscious experience; and sometimes that subconscious brain reads the signal and commits it into short-term memory way before the conscious brain gets hold of it such that when it does compare it to past memories and events, the conscious brain finds a startling exact match in the aforementioned short-term memory. With all that said, *deja vu* tends to be a phenomenon that occurs instants after you witness the image-in-question, and you tend to be able to notice, acknowledge, and snap out of it relatively quickly. But the thing I find myself experiencing, is some sort of memory-related delayed *deja vu*. I would recall a recent memory, and then realise that I have done or seen that before, as in before the memory was actually made. I found that when this memory recall happens doesn't really matter, but there has to be a memory recall, passive or active, and the memory has to be somewhat recent. This might sound rather ridiculous, but this phenomenon is so convincing, or rather, intrusive, that I actually find myself getting quite confused about whether it had actually happened before. It's to the point where I sometimes start questioning my own reality for a brief moment. The fake fabricated scene isn't exactly the same as the actual thing, like for *deja vu*, but it's actual different with only the same vibe of the event; for example, a party with the same vibe and people but in *some* place and time. I italicised "some" there because there is never a concrete place and time attached to these fake scenes. Nevertheless, they work wonders in muddling my brain. To know the trick and to still be fooled by it; I dread the day I have to pull out proof or this journal just to verify my own reality.  
> I'm aware that I spent a large part of the entry so far just talking about this *vu* phenomenon, but it is genuinely just a small part of my perceived mental deterioration, just that it is the easiest to illustrate and put into words. However, it is those that I cannot really put into words that I find the most troubling. My mental capacity and efficiency is going down, as I have mentioned. It's not like I can't process those information, just that they take exponentially longer and exponentially more effort; actually, scrap that - it is getting quite hard to process spoken stories and words at all. I noticed myself not being able to hang on to current events, often just chugging along with the conversation trying to gather as much as I can manage. Just to clarify, casual conversations tend to be all fine and dandy, perhaps because they are quite empty in nature, but once characters, events, timelines are involved, I struggle to keep up. A recent example of this would be the [next zhong ordeal](#next-zhong-conflict). I had to listen to quite a few sides and quite a few versions of the same stories and accusations. Imagine when you're already struggling to keep up, but also have to critically analyse and challenge them while having to constantly question yourself and your memories to make a decision that resonates beyond yourself. It is truly a miserable experience.  
> Speaking of memories, I can't not also talk about my forgetfulness, or rather my dwindling working memory. An idea can just pop up in my head, I would make a mental note to do it very shortly (like literally in a minute or so), and I would just forget about it entirely. It's like making a bookmark to a page, coming back to find the bookmark still there exactly where you put it, but the marked page itself is wiped blank. It genuinely leaves you with the worst kind of anxiety and frustration. It doesn't matter what the task is either, it could be as small as what app I intended to click on when I grabbed my phone, or what I was trying to write and convey in the next sentence or paragraph. Heck, I even faced quite some difficulties while writing journal entries, every single one of them. In fact, this happens so often in the recent years that I have developed a technique just to counter it. I would have to retrace my memory path from the very moment the idea or intent was conceived, all the way up to the action-in-question. Often times it would work, but I find the effectiveness greatly depends on the nature of action-in-question. Going back to the example I gave above about what app I intended to click on, I would have to retrace the steps of my muscle memory, since I find that most often than not, I would've committed actions to my muscle memory when I had the intent before I forgot what they were. However, the technique seems to prove effective only for actions that *can* be committed to muscle memory. Everything else, like linguistic nuances, writing ideas, anything non-tangible in general just tend to get lost in the endless void of my mind, unable to retrieve no matter how hard one tries. Maybe I could draw a few comparisons to the idea of **memory islands**, where all neurons bridging between an area to the rest of the brain dies, thereby literally creating an island of memory unable to be accessed by the rest of one's being. Quite a terrifying concept, if I do say so myself. Your very essence crumbling, being trapped in the one place you can never escape from: yourself.  
> The fact that my very own mental capacity is falling terrifies me. The worst kind of existence is unaware. I dread to have to begin to imagine what it would be like if you can no longer realise your own existence. It's on a next level of existential dread, above losing your own identity, above losing your own personality; losing your awareness might be the deepest levels of dread one can ever experience. Existence and awareness is a cosmic curse, both one would do fine without ever possessing, but once one does, it shudders ever fibre of one's being to imagine losing them; however, awareness triumphs all, in the way that once you lose it, the only identity you will have left is that you have none, that you are unaware. Simply nothing else would matter at all. It's like a theatre playing your life, but no one is there to watch it unfold. The reason I suddenly went into this deep dark dive, is because I would name it akin to having *Alzheimer's disease*, or other much worse neuron degenerative conditions. To be able to question your own consciousness and awareness is the best proof of your consciousness and awareness. But what if you are in degenerative stages so advanced, you are no longer able to even raise that question? This might be unjustified concern, but I actually fear that I might be suffering from something like this. A disease that attacks you instead of your mortal vessel. A truly horrendous and sadistic cosmic joke.  
> I have been wondering something every time I write an entry. What if it is my last? What would be my last memoir be? A trivial way to interpret this question might be to picture a scenario where I die. If it was expected, surely I would've summoned the last energy of my being to write one last entry. Closure perhaps, but most likely a list of regrets and dread, knowing myself. If it was unexpected, this entire journal project would just be a generic documentary, a sentence without a full-stop. However, consider the grimmest scenario: a gradual fade. To have each entry document your deterioration, there is no greater horror to be read in this world.  
> > ***Post-script***:  
> > Artist *[William Utermohlen](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/William_Utermohlen)* drew portraits of himself after being diagnosed with *Alzheimer's disease*; the deterioration is evident. Album *[Everywhere at the End of Time](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Everywhere_at_the_End_of_Time)* also attempted to depict this but in music (I have not listened to it yet, but I intend to in the near future; [here](#[TK]) would be the report/comments for when I do).

### 24-11-2022
#### Mental sunk cost
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
<!-- 💻 Personal projects -->
> I guess I have noticed this a lot but kinda never managed to put it into words until now. I keep falling victim to the sunk cost fallacy I think, not a financial one, but a mental one. I have always had projects that I'd like to do but not managed to for one reason or another. They would just sit in the back of my mind bothering me. This has always been the case, but it wasn't until S1 that I started making a list of stuff I wanted to do. I've briefly talked about it [before](#2022-new-year), but I've always wanted to make games. I even managed to get Toby, Marwin, and Bennie on board with the idea and got some help from them. Needlessly to say, I did not manage. Partly it was because I had not very much time to work with, but mainly it was because my setup at the time was just completely horrendous and incapable. I tend to work in waves of motivation, but I'd say the main bulk of the motivation went to combating the incapable technology instead of actually working on the game. To be fair, I did spend a whole summer learning shit, but most of the knowledge was about how little my computer could do. It's genuinely quite sad that for a lot of the projects I have in mind, I was always hampered by subpar tools and shit. But the thing is, I never give up, I never have.  
> To date, I have ~40 ideas jotted down in my list, games or not, and that's not even counting the ones that I did not jot down for whatever reason. Some of them I managed to find the time and motivation to finish, or at least make some considerable progress, most notably [my personal site](https://ccheukka.github.io). I guess since all of my ideas are so disjointed and erratic, I keep having to learn completely new stuff every time I want to pursue something. That's I good thing, all things considered. I find that this fact rarely impeded me, nor drained my motivation to any discernable degree. Perhaps this is where all the intrinsic drive of learning new stuff comes from. But this means that time is the most significant limiting factor for me, and I have to basically ration and squeeze out every last drop that I can get. Now that I think about it, this is most definitely where my anti-circadian work cycle comes from. In windows of motivation and idea, sleep really is the devil. We have but limited time and yet we must set aside a whole third of our lives tending to such a primitive tax. I believe this is why I have only ever managed to actually finish something during summers, where I actually have some measurable quantity of time and complete control over it. But that doesn't mean my brain would stop churning out ideas anytime else. And from time to time, I also couldn't help myself but to work on something even if I'm already extremely busy otherwise. This has resulted in countless unfinished projects waiting to be picked up again. This is where the mental sunk cost comes in. I kept on pushing myself to continue working on them despite clearing not having the time or energy to do so. I would keep coming back to old projects every now and again, but the thing is, they are not the type of things that you can just set aside and come back at any time and work on them. You have to first get yourself refamiliarised with everything just to start making progress again. This puts a harsh soft deadline on everything. I have this constant time pressure that I should get on with it as fast as possible but that would really defeat the purpose of passion projects. It genuinely feels like such a waste to have ideas come and go with no one to execute on them. I just can't help but to spend time working on them, and when I'm not working on them, I can't stop thinking about them. I'd go as far as to say a non-negligible portion of my stress comes from this sunk cost fallacy type of deal. Every small break from school or life would seem to be just the last bit of time that I'd need to finish just one thing, some thing, anything; and yet, that is rarely the case.  
> The oldest idea in my list would be the game from S1, but the one that I've arguably make the most progress on has to be this very journal and my site. [My YouTube channel](https://www.youtube.com/@CCheukKa) probably comes as a close second. I guess the site kind of stuck the perfect balance of requiring just the right amount of effort such that it is engaging enough but also not takes ages just to get refamiliarised. My YouTube channel used to fill this role. It has always been intended to be a background project that just so happens to also be profitable sometimes. Its very nature would mean that I can work on it on-and-off without worry. I started it ~4 years ago. As mentioned above, practically every one of my projects demands me to learn something new, and YouTube seems to be when I was starting to do editing and shit. But as all things go, especially less functionalistic stuff like art, standards keep getting higher and higher. I am already a perfectionist as is, and a raising bar for quality control doesn't help at all. I ended up spending more and more time each video that I starting not being able to start and finish a video within short periods of break, and this resulted in hiatuses and unfinished projects, as they tend to.  
> Perhaps it is my perfectionism, perhaps it is my lack of determination, perhaps it is my lack of time and energy; whatever it may be, it seems that I'll have to start to learn to let go of some ideas lest I get nothing done. And truthfully, I have been archiving some old ideas that I have since deemed unworthy to pursue. Although not being able to put out any finished product, is the enjoyment had during its pursue enough to worth keep working on? To be fair, part of the reason for continuing working on this journal is that initial committent to write an entry every day. While I do admit that I am horribly far from it, at least it is still somewhat consistent. My main fear of pursuing passion projects too far is that it may completely distort the projects themselves and the reason behind why I started them in the first place. This journal, for example, was intended to act more of a vessel of thought and spontaneous philosophy than a record of my daily life. Arguably, it has veered from the initial reason somewhat. Projects could be a good snapshot of one's mentality and aspirations at the time, but those that are starting to span close to a decade? Probably not so much. It's like retroactively deciding who you were some years ago. Honestly, something similar is happening here too. On days I find not enough time to write, I'd just put down and entry title and leave the actual writing for another day. Even if the actual writing might only be some days after the event itself, a lot can already change. And it is precisely this internal struggle of whether to keep pursuing and risk distortion or to just stop and leave be that keeps bothered my mind. Knowing me, I will never stop thinking about stuff until I get them done to the point where it can pass my personal quality control with an ever-rising bar.

### 26-11-2022
#### Normal sleep (I think)
<!-- 🌞 Well-being -->
> Today is the first day I woke up to a normal sleep chart. There is actually a rhythm to my stages of sleep and a normal period length of ~90 minutes. From the graph, I can actually see and tell when I finished all my deep sleep. Surprisingly, I actually never went back to deep sleep after I was done, instead brief periods of being awake took its place. I actually woke up in the awake stage too, although it didn't seem to help with the tiredness as much as I thought it would. I had a good 7-hour-and-40-minute sleep too, despite it being completely off a normal circadian rhythm.

### 29-11-2022
#### Nervousness and artificial confidence
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
> Today we had to make a speech for our *University Chinese 2* class. I have never been good at public speaking, or rather, speaking in general. I used to get inexplicably nervous. Like, really nervous to an unreasonable extent. Funnily enough, this seems to come and go for some reason. In my primary school years, we had to make at least one presentation a year for our *Project Learning* class, and I remember I was doing quite fine back then. We kept having to do at least one presentation a year in secondary school, and I was doing quite fine in S1. I do get a bit nervous, but it was nothing too noteworthy. But when I got to S2 (or was it S3? idk), I got uncontrollably nervous during one of a group presentation and I kept stumbling on my words while shaking uncontrollably. I was even already holding cue cards at the time. I honestly remember that scene quite vividly. I kept reading what's on the cue card but the words coming out of my mouth didn't make any sense at all. The pronunciation was all wrong, the annunciation was horrible. Knowing me, I was probably talking quite quietly too. And when it was time to flip over to the next cue card, I was shaking so much I struggled a whole lot doing that and I even straight-up dropped the stack of cards onto the floor, which caused a scene that I so desperately not needed to have existed. I am really not sure, not right then, and not right now, why I had been so nervous at the time. It wasn't like it was anything different from a normal presentation, and it wasn't like the stakes were particularly high anyway.  
> But for some reason, that seemed to be the only time where I really did get extremely nervous for no goddamn reason. Past that, I felt like I am getting less nervous during public speaking, group or not. Somewhere along the way, I remember trying to increase my own confidence by faking it. It was kinda like self-hypnosis or something, and it kinda worked I guess. I went on to get less nervous every time I had to speak, even when unscripted. And up until now, I think that artificial confidence had worked wonders really. My heart do still pound hard, and I do still get shaky, but I have noticed today that I actually somehow got calmer as my speech went on. My heart rate legitimately went from "I can feel a heart attack coming" to barely above the resting rate. It was like there was this weird calmness to it. This is the first time I have been like this, as far as I can remember. I'm really not sure why there has been this whole trend of nervousness min-max. Perhaps I dread the anticipation more than the thing itself? I guess I have always liked the idea of giving a speech but hated having to actually do it.  
> I'm really not sure how to put this into words, as you might be able to tell from the lack of flow and organisation above, but I do think this artificial confidence thing extends beyond public speaking and whatnot. I guess there has always been the saying of "fake it until you make it" kinda thing. I really think I have been subconsciously adopting this philosophy and applying it everywhere, seeing that I think I have weirdly been more confident since university than secondary school even though I think the norm would be the opposite. Not sure what the intended content or point of this entry is, so let's just end it.

### 30-11-2022
#### Biomechanics quiz 3
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> As per usual, I didn't really start revising until quite late. Anyway, the syllabus material isn't really too friendly, with all its variables and symbols. The funny thing is, I have no idea why the lecture notes/ textbook felt the need to use a whole set of different greek letters to address the same quantity while most of them have the same/ similar equations. That was quite a confusing mess to have to wrap my head around. Another thing about these quizzes are that we are not allowed to bring in cheat sheets or anything (for a physics quiz!). That is genuinely rather ridiculous in my book. It's not like bringing cheat sheets would allow some sort of exploit. Granted, they have provided some sort of brief formula list, but that is not nearly enough at all. I think I have mentioned it before, but the one thing I hate most is having to memorise shit. The subject itself really isn't that difficult, and I would like to think I did pretty well in the quiz. However, I have remembered one crucial equation incorrectly, and I think it had costed me an entire question. Utter ridiculousness. I guess this also shed light on how much I actually relied on good cheat sheets, but that's besides the point. So yeah, I don't really have high hopes on this one.

## December - 2022
### 07-12-2022
#### Complex Analysis and Differential Equations final
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> The [midterm](#complex-analysis-and-differential-equations-midterm) for this course is absolutely ridiculous with its recycling of old questions, and I'm not very pleased to say that the final is not much different. I don't believe any single one question was new, not even a single number changed I don't believe. Utter absurdity. It's like why even have a normal cheat sheet anymore if a copy of the past paper answer would work just fine, if not better? I seriously do not understand the rationale behind this for whoever set the papers.

### 09-12-2022
#### Programming final
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> Holy shit this exam was quite the insanity. First off, its length is quite ridiculous. Of all past papers, the longest ones are at most 14 pages long, but this exam is 22 pages long. 22 pages in only 2 hours! I barely managed to finish the paper at all; double-checking was completely out of the question. I have already voiced my hatred for *C* [before](#programming-midterm), and a programming exam on paper is among the most idiotic things on the face of this planet. Programming is about problem solving, not memorising syntax and shit. I guess this paper did lean more heavily on the problem solving side, and by that I mean the problems are rather brutal, magnitudes more than those in past papers. I guess this was not the main point of absurdity either. The real royal pain are the fill-in-the-blank questions. They asked us to fill in the blanks among statements and shit. It is basically a guessing game at best. Seriously, who thought these questions types were acceptable? It takes a long of time and effort trying to decipher what the setter's code was trying to achieve with all the most crucial parts being blanks. Can you imagine if maths exams did shit like this? And the thing is, half of the time, the code and methods given are of the weirdest approaches. Definitely not what the sane would do. For the love of god just let me use my own approaches. Granted, these questions only account for a relatively small part of the paper, but they are still very much time-consuming.  
> I would say I did quite well. I mean at least I finished, which, from what I've heard, is not what most can say. Although I was unable to double-check, and I definitely utterly needed to do so, considering the kinds of careless mistakes I apparently so enjoy making. And considering I still had 2 whole questions (the hardest ones, might I add) to go when there was only 30 minutes left, I really can't be so certain my code would work at all. Logic errors and shit plague me as is without me having to code with pen and paper, and one can only imagine what horrors lay await amongst the graphite. Either way, I am very glad I am completely done with *C* in the foreseeable future. I wish you burn in programming language hell and die a horribly painful death. Amen.

### 13-12-2022
#### Chinese 2 final
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> Welp. I woke up very late and had to take an *Uber*. I still ended up being late for ~15 minutes but I guess it was all find and dandy since you can't really get prepared for composition anyway, not me at least. I ended up somehow writing almost to the word limit and even with time to spare. To be fair, I'm still not sure what the entire subject of Chinese wants from me even after almost two decades of studying it. It seems every single time I change my writing style I would find varying degrees of success but never consistently. For example, there was one time in S5/S6 I thought my composition was absolutely off the prompt, like I legitimately almost gave up when nearing the end of the composition. I was very much pulling my hair out in the examination hall since we have be told day after day that the most important aspect of Chinese composition is to be mindful to follow the prompt closely and not to veer off into the distance. I thought I had completely failed to follow the prompt at all, and I had no hope at all for the exam. But it turns out that that composition was somehow my best composition I have ever written in my 6 years of secondary school. ??? This made no sense to me then, and it still doesn't now. I still think the marker just had a stroke at the time and I seriously felt quite a lot of guilt for getting a high score with such a terrible piece of composition. Maybe what I thought they were looking for was just the complete opposite of that. I have not a clue.  
> I have always been writing story type questions when I had the chance to. We were almost always given a choice of prompts so I basically never wrote argumentative type questions. It's not that I was particularly good at story type questions, just that I am exceptionally bad at argumentative types ones. Although I still do not understand the standard for argumentative compositions, seeing that compositions I found very good and engaging seems to always get the worst scores and vice versa, and this seems to hold true for both my own compositions and others'. Efren's compositions are of this sort, and his ones are the ones that really led me to questioning this whole scandal in the first place. An argumentative essay by definition should be to argue something by putting forwards logic and points as compelling as possible, and truthfully, I think essays written by the two of us tend to do that quite well. However, the system seems to favour essays that are full of quotes and examples with little original points and logic. That to us seems absolutely absurd. I thought the whole point of reading an essay was to enlighten myself with original and insightful points; if I had wanted to find a compilation of examples and quotes, I could've just went online and search for them! Quoting and raising examples does absolutely nothing to strengthen your point, and it definitely does not act to convince the readers. Not us at least. I would much rather have an intellectual conversation with the writer through the paper than reading a compilation of whatever quotes they managed to stuff into the paper. Alas, the entire system seems to agree otherwise, literally the entire opposite of what I would deem good. And almost always, the best scoring papers are the ones with mindless examples and little to no actual insightful content. It really is a sad degenerate display of what argumentation should be like. I'd say this is the most significant reason as to why I never write argumentative if I have to chance not to. You can have the best arguments, the most logical flows, and the most insightful points, but ultimately you will only be judged by the amount of shit you managed to violate the paper with. Fortunately, argumentative essays for the English subject makes more sense in every single way.  
> What I wrote today is quite revolting at best. I basically just put down three examples and one quote that I can think of, and they accounted for ~80% of the entire thing. There was practically no real point and flow. From my experience, the more disgust I felt after writing a Chinese composition, the better the score tended to be. Let's see if that would be true in this case.  

### 15-12-2022
#### Brother contracted COVID-19
<!-- 🌞 Well-being -->
> It seems that virtual everyone I knew, barring my parents, had contracted COVID-19 at some point. It's honestly easier to enumerate those who hadn't contracted it than otherwise. And just today, my brother had tested positive from a RAT test. It could really be a miracle that I hadn't contracted it yet, but then again I don't suppose I go out too often nor keen enough to even have the slightest chance of contracting such. Actually, I'm not really sure if my immune system is actually good or not. Throughout my entire life, [I have constantly been in and out of clinics](#pain-and-suffering). While this might already seem like a closed case, I believe that almost all of my visits are solely for my GI problems and respiratory allergies. I don't actually reckon I have been sick for issues outside of those two. So I guess this could mean that my immune system is quite lopsided(?), although my GI problems are not strictly immune-related.  
> Anyway, my house is starting to remind me of my hostel in the last weeks before we got kicked out, what with me having to put on a mask every time I stepped out of my room. Interesting correlation my brain had made there.  
> Anyhow, I won't be observing the regulations anytime soon, seeing that I'm still in the middle of my exam period. It's not, strictly speaking, legal, but I honestly couldn't care less at this point considering the not-so-good performances I had in the midterms, so I seriously doubt letting them extrapolate my grade from that would do me any good.  

### 16-12-2022
#### Biomechanics final
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> Well, this exam is quite a weird one. From all the quizzes before, we had expected that the final would be equally tricky and unintuitive. The questions posed in this course tends to be very obscured and obfuscated. The terminology and logic tends to be quite dodgy at times, not to mention that literally all of the course materials are error-ridden. It would be safe to assume that this exam would be equally so. However, as it turned out, this paper in particular just so happens to skip right over all the most trickiest parts of the course, and practically the all the problems are pieces of pastry. I mean I guess the paper *is* interesting, which is honestly more than what one can say for most other courses. The biggest offender of this paper though, was precisely the one concerning what I deemed to be the trickiest part of the course. Despite this, the question was set to be trivially easy. It is literally a giveaway question. The setter even had the audacity to give the same problem twice, only doubling one quantity for the second instance. Partly due to this slack of problem-setting, I was even able to finish and leave a whole hour early. I even doubled-checked and all. Well, this course was definitely a whole roller coaster ride. I'm not sure if the score curve would be all weird and wonky because of all the shenanigans they pulled, but I don't suppose I would do too terribly in any case.

### 18-12-2022
#### Some fever
<!-- 🌞 Well-being -->
> Apparently I spoke too soon [here](#brother-contracted-covid-19). As of the writing of this, it is 04:37 and I am apparently having a fever of 38.1°C. I did take a COVID RAT test this morning and immediately before the writing of this, and they both came out negative, so that rules that out. I'm not sure if this is an early symptom, but I do tend to have abnormally cold feet for some reason, to the point where I literally can fail to make it warm near my feet under the blankets after a whole couple hours of snuggling. This is not too big of a problem in and of itself, I can just get more blankets. But the thing is, my whole torso is literally burning while this whole ordeal is going on. This is why I woke up in the first place. I simply couldn't sleep, not the mention the back pains this horrible mattress is giving me. I went to take a shower, and it was then that I felt my heart pounding rapidly. My heart rate stayed at ~115bpm for a whole hour while my blood oxygen was apparently at only ~88%. All the signs of COVID yet all the tests came back negative.  
> I mentioned I have a horribly weak respiratory system, and in fact, my whole family has it, so it's kinda like some hereditary ailment. I'm not sure if it is related, but I do get sore throats very easily. It could take as little as breathing in dry air while I'm sleep for me to manifest a sore throat. It is honestly very annoying considering its frequency, especially in winter. It really doesn't help having weird symptoms while under high risk of actually contracting COVID.  
> If you know me, the one thing I hate most about ailments is that they impair my cognitive capacity, and the fever is definitely doing that. I am in a bad enough head space as is normally, and I definitely do not need some other excuse to hinder my brain. I'm genuinely not sure why I'm writing this entry, but I guess all the disorganised rambling is a good display of my failing brain. Sure let's go with that.  

### 19-12-2022
#### COVID positive
<!-- 💭 Philosophy -->
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
<!-- 🌞 Well-being -->
> Well fuck. I absolutely despise this. I have just been test positive using a RAT test. I mean I don't even go out and about in the streets at all anyway, and I still contracted this shit from my fucking brother. And it's not like we interact much or at all either. We literally spend all of our time in our rooms anyway, and I specifically timed my activities to be off-cycle. The perils of not being alone. 　
> I have an exam coming on 22/12, and I absolutely do not need this right now. That would be my last exam, an economics final. Coincidentally, I actually did pretty well in the [midterm](#perspectives-in-economics-midterm-results-released), apparently, so I genuinely don't think it would upset me too much if the midterm would inflate to 100% of the entire course grade, given that they won't offer a make-up exam, that is, but this is still a big unknown at the moment.  
> Anyway, the thing I am most concerned about, barring the fucking nagging sore throat, is the possibility or eventuality of the onset of "brain fog". Imagine the largest asset of your entire life, nay- your entire existence being compromised. I still stand by what I have said [before](#deterioration), having yourself stripped of yourself is the absolute greatest horror there is. Well it's probably not this serious, but any sort of deterioration is absolutely despicable. Life really is painful. Existence itself is such a delicate balance, and the slightest perturbations can cause you immense agony. I guess this is why suicidal thoughts are basically universal, canonical even. I dare to bet that every single sentient life form in the expanse of the universe with intelligence above a certain threshold would agree with this. To be fair, I still don't see the ups of existence versus non-existence. It's not about wanting to die or anyway, just not wanting to have ever existed in the first place. To be able to contemplate one's own existence is suffering. Add altered mental status into the picture, and I would say there is no need for hell to exist at all. It truly is the purest form of psychological horror, quite literally unfortunately.  
> That was an unexpected path that I went down, although it's no stranger to me. Anyway, I really am quite concerned about not being able to be in the peak of my mind when I need to in the future, or rather, my peak being significantly dwindled. But for me, the most terrifying part of this is that I won't even be able to tell at all. It's something akin to not being able to discern carbon monoxide poisoning since your cognition is so hindered you won't even know something is wrong in the first place. I am doomed to be merely the shadow of what I might be, if I would be anything at all. I'm not talking about the short-term either; but if the short-term impact is half as impactful as it is, there really is no telling how the butterfly effect would unfold.  
> Back to actually talking about COVID, I really haven't slept much at all in these past few days. I'd say ~6 hours combined. [Like I said](#brother-contracted-covid-19), I have a horrible case of sore throat, and it gets even worse when the air is dry or when I haven't been constantly chugging water every minute. And on top of that, my nose was so blocked I can barely breathe. I literally have to breathe so hard that it fatigued my diaphragm. Those really aren't conditions that would allow one to fall asleep. The inside of my throat feels like its peeling off, flaky even. I honestly think it might even be true. I still hate how my path of infection is this unjustified considering the potential lifelong lasting shit that this would leave me with. Good run I guess. Being cruelly brought into conscious existence and *then* being robbed of myself. What a cosmic joke this lot is.

### 24-12-2022
#### COVID recovery
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
<!-- 🌞 Well-being -->
> I think I'm officially COVID-free again. It would seem that the symptoms I mentioned [here](#some-fever) was the worst. Everything else was just going uphill, weirdly enough. Anyway, I do still have some very mild cold-like symptoms going on, but it's really nothing I'm not familiar with.  
> Regarding [the psychological horror aspect](#covid-positive) of it, it would seem that all my concerns were wholly unjustified. I have overthought it all, as I always do, although I would argue that it is still too early to say whether there is some sort of lingering bullshit for me to deal with down the line, but I'm really not too worried about anything else as long as it doesn't affect my brain. Or perhaps it already has, and I have already been dumbed down so much that I am no longer able to tell at all. Perhaps unrelated, but I do find my drive to do stuff quite a bit lowered, or even killed entirely in the past few days. I barely want to move at all, it would seem. I mean I wasn't able to sleep at all for the aforementioned reasons, so I guess I have been catching up on sleep recently, but I would really hope that I would have some sort of urge to do the stuff that I had been wanting to do every single time I got free time.  
> Back to the exam shit. Yes, I've missed an exam due to COVID, and for some stupid reason, CUHK requires students to submit a absence excuse application form *in person* within 5 days of the original examination date in order to not be awarded a fail in the course. First of all, this is an absolutely horrible idea to have students not be able to submit online, considering that they have presumably just fucking recovered from whatever ailment they have been suffering from. Secondly, there is absolutely no way that someone could recover from anything that would warrant a sick leave in just 5 days. Lastly, there was absolutely no special policy regarding COVID-19 at all. They literally just reused the same system and application form for regular illnesses, and frankly I'm not even sure forcing students to leave their quarantine location in 5 days is legal at all. Also, as you may have noticed, it is nearly Christmas at this point, and I'm not even sure the office opens during the holidays. My deadline is 27/12, mind you, so I;m absolutely having a jolly time trying to play this little game of theirs. How very delightful.

## January - 2023

#### Perspectives in Economics make-up final
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> As mentioned in [COVID recovery](#covid-recovery), it took so long for a make-up exam arrangement to be made. In fact, I waited a whole week only to get an email with a pdf telling me to wait longer. But alas, two days ago, I was informed that the exam would be today. Anyway, the exam paper was apparently different from what the original final exam paper, although I was kinda surprised they actually had put effort to do this, I guess it is to be expected. The paper was inexplicably hard. I'd say half the stuff is different from what the lecture notes had covered. Despite this, I don't believe I'm too worried since I guess everyone else was struggling too. However, it *is* a 3-credit course, and I really only took it because I didn't want to underload my this semester, so it'd be rather silly is it would turn out that I get a terrible grade in this. Oh well.

### 12-01-2023
#### Year 2 Semester 1 results released
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> This semester pretty much just flew by without me noticing too much, probably because so much stuff was happening around me, but I digress.
> | Course Title                                                                                      | Credit | Grade |
> | :------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | :----: | :---- |
> | [Complex Analysis and Differential Equations](#complex-analysis-and-differential-equations-final) |   3    | A     |
> | [Problem Solving by Programming](#programming-final)                                              |   3    | A     |
> | [Perspectives in Economics](#perspectives-in-economics-make-up-final)                             |   3    | A     |
> | [Orthopaedic Biomechanics and Musculoskeletal Injury](#biomechanics-final)                        |   3    | A-    |
> | [University Chinese 2](#chinese-2-final)                                                          |   3    | B+    |
> | Outline of Chinese Culture                                                                        |   2    | B+    |
> **Term GPA: 3.741 @17**  
> *Cumulative GPA: 3.716 @51*
>  
> As mentioned before, the papers of *Complex Analysis and Differential Equations* *([M](#complex-analysis-and-differential-equations-midterm), [F](#complex-analysis-and-differential-equations-final))* are basically all completely recycled, so I'm really not too surprised that I got an A. I still very much dislike this lazy system though, despite how one might attempt to justify it by arguing it raises the passing rate or whatever. The goal of education is to teach students, not to make them pass.  
> *Problem Solving by Programming* *([M](#programming-midterm), [F](#programming-final))* is another unsurprising one. However, I would say that this one felt a lot more iffy than most other courses. I really thought I had blown the final examination since I barely have enough time to complete the paper at all. Apparently, they had to lower the passing grade to 20% since so many people are failing the final paper. And on top of all, I absolutely despise *C*, but I'm sure this journal has seen enough rant on it already. I don't believe I have talked about this before, but there is this course project where we had to make a weird tic-tac-toe variant with an AI and write a [report](https://ccheukka.github.io/papers/pdfs/[ENGG-1110]%20[1]%20projectpart2_1155174356.pdf) on it. I spent weeks doing this, especially for the AI part. I got so mad at *C* I even switched to *JS/TS* to complete it halfway through so that I didn't have to deal with all the stupid ass quirks while I fleshed out the logic. And for all the effort I put into this project, at the end of the day, I only got 93%. Absolutely no idea where I lost the 7%. Ridiculous course. I would have absolutely lost it had I not got an A.  
> As for *Perspectives in Economics* *([M](#perspectives-in-economics-midterm), [F](#perspectives-in-economics-make-up-final))* though, well colour me surprised. I have not taken economics in secondary school. In fact, I believe it to be quite a stupid field of study in the first place. I never really have taken too much interest in it at all. Granted, CNok did used to tell me all about economic concepts all the time, and we did have quite a few in-depth discussions about this, but I have in-depth discussions about all random topics with everyone all the time. If not for the fact that Martin persuaded me intensely to take this course with him, I would never have taken this in a million years, especially considering this is a 3-credit course, and those are generally not exactly suitable for interest exploration purposes lest you want to be award a bad grade. I honestly would have dropped the course after the midterm, and to be fair, that was the original plan; but I just so happened to manage to get a decent enough grade in the [midterm](#perspectives-in-economics-midterm-results-released), so here we now are. I also only ever attended a single lesson, so I'm not really sure how I got an A at all, but I definitely would've killed Martin for it if I hadn't.  
> All *Orthopaedic Biomechanics and Musculoskeletal Injury* *([Q1](#biomechanics-quiz-1), [Q2](#biomechanics-quiz-2), [Q3](#biomechanics-quiz-3) [F](#biomechanics-final))* really taught me was how reliant I actually am on cheat sheets. Like all good students do, I skip basically every single lesson possible and leave as little time for revision as possible, especially for maths courses where making the cheat sheet basically is the entirety of my revision. This courses didn't allow cheat sheets for its quizzes for some stupid reason, and that was the sole reason why I got horrible grades for all of them except the second one where my DSE physics knowledge carried me through it. Absolutely hated the quizzes though because I'm pretty sure they are the sole reason I only got an A- for this course.  
> Apparently I was wrong [here](#chinese-2-final), Chinese just hates me. It doesn't really matter what I do, I just never seem to be able to get it right. Everyone that I know of basically got the same grades for the group presentation and speech, so the final argumentative essay composition really was the sole deciding factor here. God I should just stop and never look back at Chinese as a subject ever again.  
> *Outline of Chinese Culture* *([M](#outline-of-chinese-culture-midterm))* is a completely ass course. I mean the course material and the lecturer is not bad, in fact, one of the best among those I have ever experienced. The course is surprisingly thought-provoking and provocative, even to a larger extent than *In Dialogue with Nature* if I dare say so. But the assessments are so hard and of a standard so high I never really had any chance of coming close to satisfying it. I suppose I knew it from the very beginning when I took the course. Again, I really only took this course since Louis, Helen, and Tom are all taking it. But it's not like there are too many good courses in the *UGEA (Chinese Cultural Heritage)* area anyway. Oh well, I guess it could be worse, since this is only a 2-credit course.  
> In general though, I guess I'm quite satisfied with my grade this semester, although I definitely feel myself losing grip of the judgement of whether I would be good at a course. This definitely made the grades of some courses felt less earned, but I did manage to raise my cGPA, so I suppose I can't really complain too much.


### 15-01-2023
#### IELTS exam
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> This exam costs a whopping $2300. Way more than I would have imagined had I not applied for it. It's like the cost of 5 whole subjects in DSE, but I digress. The whole reason I took this exam in the first place is because apparently you need a standardised English level test in order to be qualified for exchange, for some countries and universities anyway. The exchange application deadline is 26/01, and the IELTS results allegedly will take 3-5 days to be released, so this is pretty much the latest weekend I could take this exam in.  
> I barely got any sleep at all these few days, so as usual, I overslept until I had to take an Uber to even get there on time. In my defence, it was only 08:30, so ridiculously early. It took me quite a while to even find the entrance to the place after that. They told us to arrive 30 minutes early, and apparently all that time is for queueing up and mugshots. All the procedures took so much time and are needlessly manual, if I dare say so. There really wasn't any part of it that couldn't be completely automated.  
> Anyway, I applied for a computerised test, since apparently the alternative would take a whole week to have our results ready. And let's be real, I haven't even touched a real pen for so long I basically have forgotten how to write at all, regardless of speed. The computerised portion of the test is split into listening, reading, and writing. Apparently the entire IELTS test is easier than DSE, which I definitely didn't expect, seeing how the HKDSE is already constantly under fire for being too easy, but I definitely did feel the easier-ness. The listening was easy enough. You literally just type out what the recording said, kinda like a dictation with layers of obfuscation thrown in. I did miss one of the answers, but it was so early in the morning I was still half-asleep. For the reading test, I did find trouble for a couple questions, and it reminded me why I hated language tests in the first place. The ambiguity of the questions, along with having to guess what the setter wants from you, really takes away from the test. But then again, I have not been reading since, I'd say, ~6 years ago. The last part of the morning session was the writing test. Going into this entire IELTS thing, I am woefully underprepared. I was already dealing with so much this week that I didn't really have time at all, so I really was surprised by the kinds of questions there were. I thought the writing test would be a bit more conventional, like what one would expect from an international test. But apparently, they dumbed it down quite a bit, and it was more akin to LS than English composition. It gave us an hour to complete two questions. The first one was a graph description and comparison type of question. That was really not about English in any way. The second one was a "to what extent" question, again very much LS. I was quite caught off-guard by these that it took me a good while to dig back up my dusty LS concept terminologies. I mean, I'm not too good in LS in the first place. I barely got a 5 in DSE, and apparently that was a fluke because the remarking gave me 20 points less, which would place me comfortably in the low 4 region. This is already not a good start. Worse, I'm not really sure what they are expecting from me. Do they want English English, or LS English? What kind of exam is this anyway? The entire time I was writing this essay, I was influenced very heavily by this train of thought, and it definitely made be sway between writing an English essay and writing an LS essay. Incoherence and style inconsistency. In dumbing down the writing test, they had apparently successfully mad it more difficult. Why is IELTS easier than HKDSE English in the first place?  
> After a 2-hour break, I had the speaking test in the afternoon session. Again, due to my lack of preparation, I was caught completely off-guard by the structure of the test. The marker was some local guy, and from his souvenirs and stuff, was an HKU graduate. There is already something weird about having a local guy test your English abilities when I have clearly seen there was some British lady in the same test center. It's like some kind of improper hierarchy. Honestly, I would much rather have been tested by said lady. The worst offender is that, he couldn't even speak English clearly. His enunciation is rather subpar. I had quite a bit of trouble dissecting meaning from his words. The test is recorded, and by that I mean he literally had a microphone right in my face. The questions are sporadic at best, and completely irrelevant at worst. He started asking me about my name and occupation, and proceeded to my university. Then he asked what CUHK is special about, and what I think its worst qualities are. That on its own is already very hard to come up with on-the-fly. Anyway, he then started to ask about t-shirts. Yes, t-shirts. Do you remember me ranting about his poor enunciation? I literally could not tell between his "t-shirts" and "teachers". I spent quite a bit of time wondering what he meant by "Do you wear teachers often?" since the logical continuation to talking about one's school is apparently t-shirts instead of teachers. Expectedly, this gave me quite a startle. I wasn't sure why or even whether we switched topics, so I started to talk a bit about CUHK in my answer just in case. Apparently we did switch topics and he began drilling me on my opinions on t-shirts. "Have you ever bought t-shirts as a souvenir when you were on vacations?" Why yes of course I did in my completely true and totally not made-up-on-the-spot story. And of course, I am fully aware about the t-shirt culture in Hong Kong and how it differs from generation to generation as all good citizens do. To my credit, I did manage to make up a whole lot of historical factors that sounded true enough. Then apparently my t-shirt theory is not interesting enough as he then changed the topic to cooperation in children. Of course I can give you a suggestion to boost cooperation in children out of the blue (I mean I did just recycle the bridge building game we used in the [OCamp](#ocamp-day-2)), as I assume the role of paediatric psychologist to explain why children tend to have difficulties cooperating. And thank you for asking since I just so happen to randomly have a fully-formed opinion on why countries have difficulties cooperating and suggestions on how to improve the situation while referring to the benefits of medical communication to society.  
> By the way, I made none of these up. All of the questions are not exaggerated in any way. They are in all parts wacky and unorthodox. I am really unsure what they are trying to test for in this speaking test, but I really don't believe I did too well in this. I am well aware that my organisation skills are non-existent, and it's not a matter of Chinese vs English either. I organise my thoughts and ideas just as poorly in my native tongue. So needless to say, I absolutely struggled to put everything into words, especially under time pressure and the startle of randomly switching topics. Another thing is that, I think the entirety of my English communication is solely on the side of academic argumentation. I struggle a lot when talking about casual stuff but that struggle is nowhere to be seen when he was drilling me on some of the tougher questions with wider scopes. Food for thought. Yes, and one last rant: who in the actual fuck hired this enunciation-deficient ass person as a fucking marker????

### 20-01-2023
#### IELTS exam results released
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> *[Here](#ielts-exam) is the corresponding post-exam evaluation.*  
>   
> Tabulation time, as always.  
> | Section       |   Score   |
> | :------------ | :-------: |
> | Listening     |    9.0    |
> | Reading       |    8.5    |
> | Writing       |    7.5    |
> | Speaking      |    7.5    |
> | ***Overall*** | ***8.0*** |
>
> Well, I was genuinely quite worried about my performance seeing how underprepared I was. Virtually everything caught me off-guard. But apparently I did quite well, all things considered. The full score of each section is 9, so it's like a 88.9% overall. Well it's really 90.3%, but it got rounded down to the nearest 0.5. The speaking score is really unexpected, as I fully anticipated a complete failure seeing how much I was struggling in the organisation department. One thing I'll say is that, although I know IELTS is supposed to be easier than HKDSE, I wasn't quite expecting its standards to be this low.  
> Honestly, the thing I worry about most is whether I would have enough time to retake the exam for the exchange application if I was to fail it. As of now, I am a full point up the maximum minimum, so I can stop worrying about this and focus on choosing the exchange institute.  

## February - 2023

### 14-02-2023
#### Shitty physics electromagnetic lab
<!-- 🏫 School life -->
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> This has to be the worst lab I have ever had the displeasure of doing. We were supposed to investigate the Hall effect in this lab. Sure. They played a demo video on the projector as instructions, and that has to be among one of the worst demo videos I have watched. First of all, the video is at least 10 years old. You can tell 'cus you can literally see the interlaced bullshit. The camera is of course of a very low resolution and with a shitty autofocus. The video is shot handheld, no less. The narrator has a mainland accent so heavy I can barely discern what she was saying. Her talking so quietly in the video didn't help either. The instructions are so unclear, in fact, that we basically just guessed what she was trying to do half the time. Anyway, when the video was over, the guys then say apparently we were not allowed to watch the video again or else they would give us zero marks. Great. So much for an instruction video. Absolutely ridiculous.  
> Sitting on our desk is some contraption along with a measuring scope of sorts. The contraption is the exact same one as they had demonstrated in the video, so that already tells you something about its age. You can just feel the amount of care and fucks these people give from how many times they have changed their lab sessions in 10 years' time. The contraption itself features three buttons and a coil thing along with a magnetic probe. And let me tell you the design reminds me highly of those electronic children's toys designed to be produced cheaply yet techy enough to be able to call itself electronic learning as a sales gimmick. Who the fuck designs a whole ass contraption just for a single experiment and manufactures it anyway? And who in their right mind actually buys stuff like this in bulk, no less?? When I said this whole thing reminds me of those shitty children's e-toys I was not joking whatsoever.  
> Throughout the entire 2-hour lab session, and I do mean the entire lab session, we were supposed to keep pressing the buttons in all their permutations and combinations and measure the voltage, only to turn the dials slightly and do the whole thing over and over again. If you think it is tedious enough, you haven't heard anything. The equipment is so old the scope is barely even working. We had to reset it every 10 measurements or so lest it gets stuck in an infinite loop somehow. The measurements tick creeps so slowly it is infuriating to watch. And every time you think the measurement has been stabilised, it would change the second after you write it down. And that's not it either. We had to suffer through a whole 132 measurements. What a load of joy.  
> For the last part of the 132, we had to measure how the distance of the probe affects the measurements. So we had to do the entire measuring process again except now we also have to move the probe every 4 measurements. The probe was mounted on a rail with markings. There were a ruler on the rail and another one on the probe itself. And you know what the best part of this whole ordeal is? The markings of those two rulers didn't even match! 10mm on one is 9mm on the other. What on god's green earth is this accurate science bullshit if we're making up our own unit sizes anyway?!?  
> This is the dullest and most labour intensive lab session I have ever done. And let me tell you one thing, there is absolutely no reason they couldn't have cut the entire thing in half either. They could only have us do half the work and we would still have gotten the same graph at the end, but no, they have to squeeze funding out of the faculty by pretending their lab sessions are long even though not a single drop of said funding actually ends up in the lab equipments.  

### 23-02-2023

Makes you wonder why they make us take the courses in this order. But anyhow, this course is actually quite delightful to study for, since it mainly concerns biotechnology, or rather all the rationales and tangents of biotechnology without actually talking about biotechnology.

However, I have noticed that the correct answer is ever so slightly more lightly shaded for one of the questions, which I believe since they always just print the marking scheme directly where the correct answers are in red and use it as the question paper. While I only noticed this phenomenon for this one question, apparently Louis said that he was able to see all the answers in this manner. Absolutely ridiculous. I might add that I believe this had happened before in a *Human Anatomy and Physiology* CA last year, though only vaguely so seeing that I seem to not have committed it to this journal. But I would be quite pissed if this would turn out to be the thing that would cost me.

#### Advanced physics quiz 2
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> If you're wondering why there wasn't any entry regarding quiz 1 of this course, it's because I missed it entirely. Yes, you saw that right. This piece of disgusting nuisance confident enough to call himself the lecturer had decided that apparently telling students about when quizzes happen is completely unnecessary and irrelevant at all. This shitty course has two lectures per week. We got a brief notice about a quiz happening that week but for some godforsaken reason not which lecture of the week. Yes you read that right. So as good students do, I painfully convince myself to attend the first lecture of that week since it just so happens to be right after my attendance-taking English course. We even arrived the lecture theatre early, mind you. And when we were there, we of course immediately went to ask the sack of sad shit when actually the quiz is. And now guess what this piece of specimen replied. He literally said "you will know when you know" word-for-word. Now may I ask you, what kind of sane lecturer on this planet would give such an answer? And he kept trying to keep up with this mystique for some reason even upon further questioning. So eventually we gave up and left the lecture theatre and went along our merry day. And of course, our one friend who doesn't value his time enough decided to stay behind and informed us that there was indeed a quiz a while after we had all left. Absolutely delightful.  
> I wasn't sure of it then, but I am sure of it now. This deplorable excuse of a human deployed such strategies to try and boost his lectures' attendance. Something like that. He literally pulled the same shit again this week. We kept asking if there would be a quiz and he kept trying not to answer. So I sat my ass down and entertained his little game for a bit until he announce there wouldn't be a quiz this lecture and ~10 or so people immediately walked out, myself included. There is absolutely no act more egregious than to waste another person's time for whatever reason. And something tells me that he wouldn't stop trying to pull this shit off.  
> Anyhow, today is the second lecture of the week and I of course attended for the quiz. But apparently, his lowly strategy has evolved. He decided to save the quiz for until the very end of the 2-hour lecture for whatever reason. We sat there with much disgruntle but there was no longer any reason to leave just to come back later. Sunk cost, I suppose. Either way, the quizzes are just 3 MC questions. And guess what, he still managed to fuck something up as simple as this quiz gets. I suppose he figured spending time conjuring his little battle plans to get attendance is more important than formulating a passable quiz. There are 3 total questions and he somehow managed to fuck up the choices for one of them, the question for another, and the answer key for the last. I do believe that he has forgotten what quizzes actually meaning because they definitely do not mean a showcase of incompetence and errors. At the end, I got 67.8% but each quiz only account for 1.25% of the entire course so it's not like it matters too terribly much.

## March - 2023
### 01-03-2023
#### Circuits and signals midterm
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> Electric circuits are by far the topic I like least in physics. I'm honestly not sure what I don't like about it specifically, it's just that it never really spoke to me. And now you're telling me that we are somehow going to put complex numbers into circuits and stuff? It is starting to get all hand-wavey, and I can't say I would like my course material to be like that. And on top of that, we are apparently going to actually have to look into chips and stuff, which entails us having to dig into the datasheets trying to decipher what the manufacturer intended the chip to perform. And that is the first problem I'm having with this exam. We are supposed to have an understanding of what a certain chip's behaviour is like, but the chip itself is no goddamn complicated it really isn't feasible to look into its inner workings. And as such, we basically have to treat it as a black box or some program instead of an actual electrical circuit. Normally how I would like to get an understanding on something would be to try and derive said stuff and their surrounding equations myself. This strategy is actually quite good for not only understanding the topic and concepts, but also for during exams when I go completely blank on something and have to derive stuff from the very fundamentals, which happens quite a lot for some obscene reason. Either way, as you might imagine, this completely breaks down for topics too complicated to even get a grasp of in the first place, let alone trying to derive stuff out from it. It is honestly about memorising arbitrary equations that have magically appeared out of thin air at that point.  
> This happened to be the case in the exam. Although the exam didn't really ask too deep into the chip itself, one of the questions actually requires us to construct a simple circuitry with it. The circuitry in its entirety actually was in one of the appendix of the lecture notes, but of course I didn't study it since, like I said, it was in the appendix, so I had simply assumed that it was just some sort of application demonstration of the chip. I still managed to draw an approximation of the circuit though, but I'm not sure it was good enough.  
> I can't say I have high hopes for this exam since it was really my weakest topic in physics even in secondary school. Hm.

### 03-03-2023
#### Advanced physics midterm
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> This stupid exam spans from 19:00 to 21:30 for some reason. I wouldn't begin to start pondering why it starts at the time it does but I do have to say it is rather convenient since my *Synthetic Biology Workshop* lab session ends at 18:30. Saves me having to figure out where to waste the time I suppose, with time for a little snack before the actual exam.  
> That was where the good bits end though. Martin and I got there ~18:40 after our snack. They told us to arrive at 18:30 even though the exam only real starts at 19:00 and apparently all the 30-minute buffer time is for pointless shenanigans. First of all, they require us to skip seats to leave vacancies between our neighbour and us. Now this alone isn't really anything unheard of. But they said that we have to skip 2 seats for some godforsaken reason, and they even whipped up a seating plan on the projector screen right there for some reason. The thing is that, they made the plan such that some students are forced to sit at isle seats. If you haven't partaken in university level exams, especially ones that concern mathematics in one way or another, you would know that having only one lecture theatre style shitty table at our disposal is definitely not enough space for an exam, what with all the stationery you'll be needing, your calculator, your cheat sheet, the question booklet, and the answer booklet. It is very infeasible to attempt to complete such an exam using solely a single table, and very much against your own interests if you try to. Hence, I have grown to develop a whole system using a whole three tables for organisation and it is very much critical for me. Yes, I understand that using three tables is quite insane and probably be a nuisance to my neighbours, but that's why I tend to choose seats in unorthodox places such that there would be no neighbours in the first place. But I generally also get by with only two tables, and I find that having the one to my left is most critical.  
> Anyway, let's back into the actual event. I guess sure, they tried to maximise valid seats by formulating the plan in such a way, but it was absolutely unnecessary since there are still so many unoccupied rows of seats begging to be warmed by stress glutei. The lecture theatre has three sub-rows in the same row, much like how it is like in an aeroplane. But as needless as it is, they apparently also made seating plans for those chains of three seats despite it being physically impossible to sit in a way that it would violate the skip-two-seats protocol. And of course, you guessed it, they opted for us to sit in the worst possible location of each of the sub-rows, the isle seats. Now as logical human beings, we all assumed the seating plan was just merely a suggestion, to demonstrate the idea of skipping seats, especially concerning the sub-rows where I was. But apparently, as the story goes, they treated it as law and raised their squeaky voices in protest whenever we even moved at all as guards do with prisoners. The audacity to compromise my three-seat exam plan! And with the lack of a left-side table too! How preposterous. I of course kept trying to shift into the middle seat and they keep coming up to me to protest about it. Eventually I did sit in a sub-optimal seat only to shift back to a middle seat as soon as the exam started.  
> This might be sound to be merely an over dramatisation of the events and some evil read to a seemingly tame event. However, this is not the only thing they tried to do in an attempt to compromise students' interests. No single act can sway mundane tomfoolery in the veil of evil. It must require but heaps of equally if not more ridiculous and malicious acts to force sabotage be the only logical way anyone can interpret this be. The [shenanigans they pulled with the quizzes](#advanced-physics-quiz-2) are one of them, and this is another. These two are definitely the worst offenders. Along with the [shitty lab session](#shitty-physics-electromagnetic-lab)‚ and the requirement to submit everything in paper. What archaicity. Truly deplorable and unredeemable. His goal is but not teaching, instead schemes and attention hogging. Feeble attempts to anchor himself into students' minds as we struggle to free from his web of traps and inconveniences. Unfitting to be a lecturer, and unbecoming of the course in a proper university.  
> I realise I still have not yet talk a single word about the actual exam paper. The paper itself is rather quaint. Despite the course seemingly being quite complicated with a lot of nuances, the exam seems to only concern secondary school level knowledge and question styles. Definitely unexpected of a course such as this. I barely used the cheat sheet at all, not in the way that I managed to know all the equations by heart, but in the way that the entire paper was about the same two or three equations over and over again. And by over and over again, I do mean it. One of the questions asks you to calculate the same thing over and over again but with different numbers substituted into the equation. Basically trying to catch you slacking when you're five calculations down the line. And those are not trivial equations to be done with a calculator, might I add. The MC questions are set pretty much exactly like DSE questions, trying to trick you by confusing you, and with wordplay and such, but less so concerning actual knowledge and deeper understanding. Safe to say, I didn't enjoy the exam very much, in every manner possible.

### 13-03-2023
#### Statistics midterm
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
> Okay, I'll say it right away. I dislike statistics. I think it is a horrible construct with the most arbitrary principles you can find in the entirety of mathematics. It is rather impossible to build intuition about it since there is no intuition possible that can serve to navigate this mess of a field. It is quite a miserable study in my opinion, not in the way that it is not useful, but in the way that it is extremely useful yet everything hangs on a thin thread of logic and solidity. There are no fundamental constants to speak of, nor are there formulae that are in total consensus. Literally everything about it is arbitrary and every conclusion is based on conventions. I guess this might not be too big of a surprise considering that probability lies in the heart of statistics, so I guess it is, by nature, not rigid.  
> Anyhow, I should probably talk about the actual exam itself. But first off, before I could actually go and take the exam, I had to go get my cheat sheet printed. So logically, I went to the learning common in *Wu Ho Man Yuen Building* to get it done, considering the time pressure and seeing that it is en route. I thought But as luck would have it, the internet of the place is out, and I can't print my cheat sheet without the internet since everything I have is in the cloud. Great. So then the next logic option would be the *University Library* which would only require a slight detour everything considered. But of course, the entire place is absolutely packed with people for some reason. I spent so much time looking for a vacancy but apparently every single computer is in use. Eventually, I found this accessibility computer. After fumbling with it for a bit, I discovered that it of course was not connected to the printers there. *Great*. Eventually, I just gave up and went back to *BME Computer Lab* to get my shit printed. The thing is that, I always have gone there to get my stuff printed, but the one time that I decided not to, shit like this happens. The one time I thought to avoid detours is the one time the detour proved to be necessary. After running a whole marathon, I barely got there ~5 minutes after the exam had started. But here's the thing: I arrived CU 30 minutes before the exam and apparently this whole ordeal wasted ~35 minutes of my time. Just the best.  
> I realise I still haven't talked a single bit about the exam. It was fine. Everything about it was easy, and I do mean it. There is not too much in the way of being challenging or tricky. Nothing was out of the ordinary, barring the last "bonus questions" which required you to derive some proofs on your own. It should be alright despite my indifference/disgust towards the subject.
