#### Bike trail walk and some fancy steakhouse experience
<!-- 👣 Experiences -->
<!-- 🍽 Food -->
> I proposed some days ago that Wales, Louis, Helen, Tom, and I go cycling after the [statistics midterm](#statistics-midterm) to *Shatin* and dine at *Outback Steakhouse*. While I thought this plan was all finalised and whatnot, apparently not, since literally everyone backed out of it saying that they didn't have the mood to cycle after an exam. Some bullshit. After a whole lot of convincing, eventually we decided that we would dine there at 18:45 but not cycle. It was still 16:30 by the time the exam finished, so I have ~2 hours of time to burn somehow. I didn't want to go back to my hostel since there wasn't really anything to do there, and I decided that cycling myself to *Shatin* would be rather boring and leave too much time for nothing once I get there. So for some reason, I decided that walking along the bike trail all the way to *Shatin* was apparently the next best thing to cycling.  
> I guess walking is kinda nice, since it's not like I get to do that a lot on any odd day. Most of my walking is usually just to get to places as fast as possible, and seldom to do so *as slow as possible* as I was trying to do. I guess this kind of walking can only be a thing in *New Territories*, not near any roads, no less, since anywhere else in Hong Kong you're basically just breathing in fumes for no reason. I was listening to a horror story narration the whole time and I'm not one for scenic walks or descriptive writing so I'm not really sure what else I could add here. The whole journey was apparently ~7 km, and it took me ~80 minutes. I can't say I really felt the distance at all, for some reason, not at the time at least. Though I would like to add that there weren't as many twists and turns and bends as I would've like, perhaps to break up the monotony, since most of the walk was just a long stretch of road, although I guess that was to be expected for a bike trail.  
> When I reached *Shatin*, there was still a whole hour to burn, so I just sat at an *IKEA* on one of their display sofas for the whole time while listening to the story. Once I sat down though, I definitely started feeling the distance. I legitimately think there's something wrong with my walking since my knees and hips felt stressed. I feel like something about my knees' hyperextension makes me unfit for walking, although running would still be fine since I don't think hyperextension would really affect it 'cus it's not like you can hyperextend while running anyway. My hips, however, I have no idea about. I wasn't carrying anything heavy at all, and as I've said, the road was just a flat stretch of pavement, nothing of note. [Undiagnosed ailments](#undiagnosed-ailments) part 2.  
> Wales literally went right back home to sleep after the exam, so the rest of us met up at 18:45 and went to the steakhouse. I have indeed been living under a rock my whole life since I literally have not heard of *Outback Steakhouse* before Wales mentioned it some weeks ago. So I was really going into this blind. Apparently, what I thought was just some mildly fancy steak restaurant serving ~$100 steaks was on a level of fancy three floors above what I was thinking. The very cheapest steak on the menu was something like $400. The four of us stood outside the restaurant looking at the menu for quite a long while considering what to order before we actually had the courage to go inside. We took another whole while figuring out what to order. And the waiters just keep giving us complementary bread the whole time. I mean the bread is some black sugar bushman bread along with some nice cream cheese, so that's one reason for the price. We spent so long trying to decide on something that I felt the waiters were starting to think we were juts there for the bread. They are legitimately getting visibly annoyed and even started coming to our table and suggesting menu items. The entire place was rather empty by the time we got there, but when we finally had decided what to order, it was getting quite packed. Eventually, we decided on two 2-person combo meals since that was the most affordable reasonable option.  
> No idea why I thought I should deploy a whole ass table for this but here it is:  
>   
> | Item                                     | Quantity |
> | :--------------------------------------- | :------: |
> | Black sugar bushman bread + cream cheese |    ∞     |
> | Cream soup                               |    4     |
> | Salad with croutons                      |    2     |
> | Grilled USDA Prime NY Strip              |    1     |
> | Grilled Lobster Tail                     |    1     |
> | BBQ Half Pork Ribs                       |    1     |
> | Roasted Chicken                          |    ½     |
> | Grilled Scallops & Bacon Creamy Risotto  |    1     |
> | Toowoomba pasta (shrimp fettuccine)      |    1     |
>   
> I don't really know where to start, but everything is so good. The bread was fragrant. The soup was not as creamy as I have hoped, but tasty nonetheless. The salad was not too noteworthy. The steak was very thick but wasn't seasoned enough and was a bit overcooked and tough. The lobster tail was amazingly sweet although it was a bit small. The ribs were very tend, and the meat just fell off the bone. The chicken was quite a small one and wasn't as juicy as I would've like although not dry either. The risotto was a bit too clumpy and bland and stingy; the scallops wrapped in bacon was very good though. The pasta was spicier than we had anticipated though very creamy; the shrimps were not noteworthy.  
> We shared everything on the table, of course, as some sort of pseudo-taster menu thing. They only put 3 scallops on a 2-person set meal though, weirdly enough. Not sure how that was meant to work. Honestly, I initially thought 2 sets didn't have enough food for all of us, but apparently surprisingly quite a bit of the price can be explained by the quantity of food. We actually barely finished everything at all. Perhaps a 3-person combo meal could do next time, although I'm not sure there will be a next time anytime soon since everything in total costed **$1135 ($283.75 per person)**, and we definitely need time to financially recover from this. I initially really just thought this would be some ~$200 tops meal and started to panic when the cheapest steak on the menu was ~$400 before settling for this combo meal thing. Honestly, I think it couldn't have gone better. The price wasn't that unreasonable all things considered. It's just that they hid this combo meal on the menu and it took some digging to realise its value. 10/10 would dine again (if I have the money and managed to get enough people on board).

### 17-03-2023
#### Advanced physics midterm paper checking
<!-- 📚 Academics -->
> After [the results were released](#advanced-physics-midterm-results-released), the TA responsible or marking the papers actually offered two paper checking sessions. He actually set the session times to be rather awkwardly early to go to, probably to discourage people from actually going there, but I went there nonetheless following Martin, who went yesterday and apparently got awarded 2 marks after some arguing. He said that the TA actually didn't even understood the material properly and he had to explain an entire equation to him; and while he was there, another international student got their hands on 6 extra points somehow.  
> Either way, when I got there, Louis was apparently still there, and he had been there for a whole hour somehow. When I got the paper and checked, I briefly went through the first couple questions, but when I came to the last question, apparently I got got 6/15 from it. I was rather shocked since I that question can literally be on a DSE paper and no one would question it at all. So after a bunch of investigation, I figured out that actually the entire marking scheme for that question is wrong, and instead, my answer was indeed what the marking scheme should've been. Basically everything is the same except that the marking scheme had substituted the wrong number into a variable andd got the wrong answer. And as things go, of course the answer for part b is also dependent on the answer for part a, and so both of them were incorrect. So I talked to the TA and explained everything to him and he eventually gave me a full score for that question, 15/15.  
> So yes, my final score is now actually 9 points higher, at 91%. I'm honestly surprised that an alleged wrong substitution of a number could've costed me 9 points. And the substitution step is literally the last step of the solutions, so I am absolutely stumped as to how that would constitute 9 points while the entire proof before that would only account for 6. The TA told me that apparently virtually no one got the last question right, and for some reason he didn't think to check the marking scheme because of that. Sure.  
> While this is a whole scandal and a half, borderline a scam, I guess I can't be too hard on him considering that he actually went through the effort of setting up this paper checking session, which wasn't really a thing for any other course ever. I would like to criticise the wrong marking and whatnot, but I wouldn't even have known if an error existed for the courses that didn't have paper checking sessions. Perhaps I would try to arrange such sessions myself in the future for other courses, since apparently these kinds of things [have historically turned out pretty well for me](#english-grade-appeal-conclusion-probably) (barring the hassle). Who knows?

>  
> I honestly enjoyed this course a whole lot. I have been wanting to take it since last year but just never got the chance to do so. Well, to be fair, I wanted to take the quantum mechanics course most but this is my second choice. The lecturer gave us minigames to play in each lecture, counted towards the final grade of course (which meant I couldn't really skip all lectures, grump-). The topic of this course isn't really too complex and I could genuinely see it being useful IRL, especially the algorithm of fairly splitting bills and stuff.

### 25-07-2023
#### Thought consolidation
<!-- 🧠 Mentality -->
> Yes yes another hiatus, I know. I'm not gonna dwell on it since it seems that I have [talked enough about them already](#inevitable-reoccurring-hiatuses). But I just wanna note that it's kinda interesting how June is lacking for both this year and last year. I suppose it's because of the summer holiday being the only time I can really rest my brain an body or something.  
> Anyway, I was just starting to notice a way that I can try to untangle my brain to look for important ideas that were just floating about in my head. I constantly have a scattered mind. It's like stuff comes in and out of my consciousness, randomly appearing as they please, but never reachable when I query for them. I guess this is why I thought I had an [undiagnosed case of ADHD](#undiagnosed-ailments); I still think I do. I guess I have tried to cope with this in numerous ways, most notably starting this journal. While it definitely helped, I found it has already acted more as a way for me to organise and chain thoughts together, instead of formulating new stuff. I speculate it's because the act of typing is so fast and commissive that I don't really have time to dwell on things in the way that is important to my brain, but more so in the way that makes sense for the entry itself. I suppose language just isn't tailored to thoughts as much as it is for communication.  
> Anyhow, another method I have noticed throughout the years (well, more like in these ~2 years) is that my thoughts seem to be hyperconnected when I'm at the brink of falling asleep or waking up. It's just the place where you're at the brink between consciousness and unconsciousness. Your unconsciousness is the body of the iceberg where the majority/all of thought and information processing takes place, and your consciousness is just responsible for accessing them like books in the library, without much freedom or power of actually authoring them. I've read that the process of formulating a thought isn't really by intuition, but rather it's more like your brain trying to enumerate every single possible new neuron synaptic connection until it finds one that makes progress, and continue ad infinitum. When and how a thought forms is really more like a weighted possibility. I conjecture that at the edge of consciousness is where you can get a glimpse towards your inner self, and how single idea you have had attempts to bridge itself with everything else whether it makes sense to or not. I guess this is one of the reasons why dreams tend to not make any sense; they are a sandbox for untested neuronal connections to occur. However, as you might have imagined, harnessing this is incredibly difficult. I have experimented with this for a couple times, and I found that I can influence the train of thought and nudge it towards the direction of the breakthrough I'm looking for. But as I have talked, I don't believe your conscious mind has too much control what's happening beneath the surface, so I'm just a small part of the audience yelling requests at best. Another thing is that you are at the brink of falling asleep, so the window is rather small. I have tried to extend it somewhat, but the most consistent and easiest way I have found to extend this is to wait until you're waking up, most desirably, after oversleeping by a lot. First of all, you're not troubled by the tire of the day. Second, you have the chance to comb through an entire night's worth of new stuff, along with whatever happened in your dreams. There is some scientific basis behind this I think. From what I have been able to observe from my sleep pattern using my [smartwatch](#technology-obtained-smartwatch), the human body goes through cycles of sleep in one night, from light sleep, to REM, to deep sleep, then to a brief period of being awake before repeating. However, the interesting thing is that the deep sleep portion gets dropped after a couple cycles when your body decided that it has had enough of that. And then you're left with cycles of extended REM and light sleep, where your brain is quite active. And with the brief periods of awakeness, you can consciously glimpse into the web of ideas happening. If you have the time, you can extend this state of being pretty much for hours. I have found that this method generally is best suited for creative pursuits and less so for actual regrouping since there is absolutely no semblance of organisation down there.  
> Let's get to the crux of what I'm actually trying to talk about. It's the kind of thought exploration concurrent to mechanical tasks. For me, it has been [*TETR.IO*](https://tetr.io/) (tetris), [*Celeste*](https://www.celestegame.com/) (platformer), and [*Trackmania*](https://www.ubisoft.com/en-gb/game/trackmania/trackmania) (racing game). They're the sort of game where quite a bit of mechanical skill and focus is required, but not as much for cognition. Your brain has a clock speed just like computer CPUs, and the clock speed can go up if you need it for intensive tasks. I conjecture that it's because these games demand so much mechanical skill and focus that your clock speed is heightened, but your cognition is really required and so it just gets tons of free time with a spun-up clock rate. Basically overcharging your brain for an extended period of time. I suppose this is kinda also the reason why shower thoughts are a thing. Perhaps this is part of the reason why people go jogging too, but I seriously doubt this since your brain is a very oxygen-hungry machine and jogging just doesn't go hand-in-hand with cognition, but I digress. Yes it does take some time to get into the zone, but after that, I find that it allows me to formulate ideas and thoughts to an extent I've never experienced before. I suppose there really isn't a lot of time that I spend with my brain overclocked and not actively working on something else. The most important part of this process, I found, is that it allows me to identify what has been bothering me subconsciously for the past while. You know the feeling of something unprocessed at the back of your mind but you can never quite tell what it is to even start working on it? This helps dig it up quick. Basically anything backlogged due to the hustle of life, dilemmas and such, self-discovery. The way I'd put it is thought consolidation. I guess it helps make decisions and formulate opinions, ones that I think I have always had but just never been put under the spotlight for examination and exploration. Now that I think about it, I suppose this is what those faux arguments in your mind also do, although to a much less effective extent, I would say.  
> I suppose I'm writing this entry to remind myself that such methods exist and help a lot.  
> > Recently I've been introduced to this tool [*obsidian.md*](https://obsidian.md/). It's basically a research and idea connection tool. It does what your brain already do but without having to rely on unreliable flesh memory. It's a part of an idea called the *external brain*. Using it is like writing a wiki with all the backlinks and such. I guess another one of its selling features is the graph view, which is a graph illustrating the web of backlinks and such. I have only recently started using it for my [*iGEM* research](https://github.com/CCheukKa/iGEM-research), though I think I should and will start to slowly incorporate literally everything into the vault. It's like the more I put in there the better. I've been taking notes and stuff in markdown with VSCode already for since I have discovered VSCode, so it's not like it's a big jump from that, and all the pre-existing markdown files can just be directly ported. I guess I don't really like the interface that much and I really wish there could be some VSCode extension so that I can stay here but I guess it's fine. I might start looking into migrating this journal over since it's lagging like hell 'cus this whole file is 450000+ characters long as of the writing of this. Wow this whole paragraph has just been an advertisement for it. No idea why I wrote this. It's tangentially related to what I've been talking about I guess? I'll just put this in double quotes.
